The Mu'tazilite Dilemma on Divine Attributes
Presents the Mu'tazilite dilemma that attributes must be either originated or eternal, both problematic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite argument that if attributes are additional to God's essence, they must be either originated (implying change and pre-eternal imperfection) or eternal (implying multiple eternal beings, which is disbelief).

Core Idea
Attributes cannot be additional without falling into an impossible dilemma.

The Mu'tazilites sought to deny real attributes by presenting a logical dilemma. This lesson examines their two-horned argument, which forced a choice between originated attributes (leading to change in God) and eternal attributes (leading to polytheism).

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
The Mu'tazilites are arguing against the Ash'arite view that attributes are real and additional to God's essence. Their objection is a logical dilemma.
2
Read the objection passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Identify the two possibilities presented.
The text presents two horns: attributes are either originated (haditha) or eternal (qadima).
3
Examine the first horn
If attributes are originated, then God's essence would be a locus for originated things (hawadith), implying change. Also, in pre-eternity, God would lack these attributes.
This contradicts divine immutability and perfection.
4
Examine the second horn
If attributes are eternal, then there would be multiple eternal entities, leading to shirk (associating partners with God). The Mu'tazilites cite the Christian belief in two eternal persons as a precedent.
Consensus of Muslims considers multiplicity of eternals as disbelief.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The Mu'tazilites conclude that real additional attributes cannot exist. This sets the stage for the Ash'arite response.
The response is covered in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تقرير شبهة المعتزلة في نفي صفات المعاني، ورَدُّها حادثة؛ فيلزم قيام الحوادث بذاته، وخلوه تعالى في الأزل عن العلم والقدرة والحياة وغيرها من الكمالات، وإما أن تكون قديمة فيلزم تعدد القدماء، وهو كفر بإجماع المسلمين، وقد كفرت النصارى بزيادة قديمين فكيف بالأكثر؟ فأجاب عنها بقوله: ثم صفات الذات أي: ثم بعد تقرر الواجب لذاته تعالى، وتقرر قيام صفاته الثبوتية بذاته أخبرك بأنه يدفع عنك إسكال تعدد القدماء أن تقول: إن الصفات القائمة بذات الواجب المتقرر زيادتها عليه خارجا ليست بغير الذات الواجب الوجود تعالى أو ليست بعين الذات.
A report of the Mu'tazilite doubt in negating the attributes of meanings, and its refutation: [that the attributes are] originated; then the occurrence of originated things in His essence would be necessary, and His transcendence in pre-eternity from knowledge, power, life, and other perfections [would be negated]; and if they are eternal, then multiplicity of the eternals would be necessary, which is disbelief by consensus of the Muslims, and the Christians were declared disbelievers for adding two eternals, so how about more? So he answered it by his saying: 'Then attributes of the essence' i.e., then after the establishment of the Necessary by His essence, and the establishment of His positive attributes subsisting in His essence, I inform you that He repels from you the difficulty of multiplicity of the eternals, that you say: The attributes subsisting in the essence of the Necessary, established as additional to it externally, are not other than the essence of the Necessary of existence, nor are they identical to the essence.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage presents the Mu'tazilite objection against the attributes of meanings (such as knowledge, power, will) and the response from the poem. The objection argues that if attributes are additional to God's essence, they must be either originated (haditha) or eternal (qadima). If originated, then God's essence would be a locus for originated things, implying change, and He would lack perfections in pre-eternity. If eternal, then there would be multiple eternal entities, which is disbelief; Christians were condemned for asserting two eternal persons (Father and Son), so positing many eternals is worse. The response (from the poet's line 'thumma sifat al-dhat') asserts that the attributes are neither entirely other than the essence (laysat bi-ghayr al-dhat) nor identical to it (laysat bi-'ayn al-dhat). This means they are not separate entities, but nor are they mere aspects without distinction. This resolves the dilemma of multiplicity without falling into either extreme.

Key Terms
صفات المعاني
الحوادث
تعدد القدماء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Attributes can be additional to God's essence without any problem.
Correction: The Mu'tazilites argue that any addition leads to one of two impossibilities. The Ash'arite response is needed to resolve this.

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazilite objection, what are the two possible statuses of attributes if they are additional to God's essence?
A) Created and uncreated
B) Originated and eternal
C) Necessary and possible
D) One and many

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilites argue that real additional attributes lead to either change in God or polytheism, so they must be denied.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that the Mu'tazilites thought denying real attributes protects tawheed, do you sense a similar tendency in yourself to avoid affirming something about God out of fear of shirk? What attribute of God have you ever hesitated to affirm as real, and how will you now correct that?
?
The passage says that if attributes were originated, God would lack knowledge and power in pre-eternity. Have you ever thought of God as 'incomplete' before creation? How does this passage challenge you to affirm that God has always been perfect in every attribute?
?
Consider the Christian analogy: they added two eternals and were declared disbelievers. Are you absolutely certain that your belief in God's attributes does not inadvertently lead to multiplicity? What will you do to ensure your tawheed is pure according to the understanding of Ahl al-Sunnah?

The Ash'arite Response: Neither Other Nor Identical
Presents the poet's response that attributes are neither other nor identical to the essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'arite response to the Mu'tazilite dilemma: the attributes are neither other than the essence nor identical to it, resolving the charge of multiplicity without assimilation.

Core Idea
Attributes are neither entirely separate from God nor completely the same as His essence.

The poet responds to the Mu'tazilite dilemma by articulating a middle path. The attributes of the essence are not entirely other (ghayr) nor entirely identical ('ayn) to the essence. This preserves both unity and distinction.

Guided Path
1
Recall the dilemma
Remember the Mu'tazilite objection: attributes cannot be additional without being either originated or eternal, both impossible.
This response directly addresses the charge of multiplicity.
2
Read the response passage
Read the Arabic and translation of the poet's answer. Notice the phrase 'laysat bi-ghayr al-dhat wa-la bi-'ayn al-dhat'.
This is the key formula.
3
Understand the negations
The response denies two extremes: (1) attributes are not completely other than the essence (which would imply multiple separate entities), and (2) they are not identical to the essence (which would be the Mu'tazilite position or reduce them to mere aspects).
This is a via media.
4
Analyze the resolution
By saying the attributes are neither other nor identical, the Ash'arites maintain that attributes are real and distinct in meaning (ma'nan) but not separate existing entities. This avoids both shirk (multiple eternals) and tahrif (denial of attributes).
This is the orthodox Sunni position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تقرير شبهة المعتزلة في نفي صفات المعاني، ورَدُّها حادثة؛ فيلزم قيام الحوادث بذاته، وخلوه تعالى في الأزل عن العلم والقدرة والحياة وغيرها من الكمالات، وإما أن تكون قديمة فيلزم تعدد القدماء، وهو كفر بإجماع المسلمين، وقد كفرت النصارى بزيادة قديمين فكيف بالأكثر؟ فأجاب عنها بقوله: ثم صفات الذات أي: ثم بعد تقرر الواجب لذاته تعالى، وتقرر قيام صفاته الثبوتية بذاته أخبرك بأنه يدفع عنك إسكال تعدد القدماء أن تقول: إن الصفات القائمة بذات الواجب المتقرر زيادتها عليه خارجا ليست بغير الذات الواجب الوجود تعالى أو ليست بعين الذات.
A report of the Mu'tazilite doubt in negating the attributes of meanings, and its refutation: [that the attributes are] originated; then the occurrence of originated things in His essence would be necessary, and His transcendence in pre-eternity from knowledge, power, life, and other perfections [would be negated]; and if they are eternal, then multiplicity of the eternals would be necessary, which is disbelief by consensus of the Muslims, and the Christians were declared disbelievers for adding two eternals, so how about more? So he answered it by his saying: 'Then attributes of the essence' i.e., then after the establishment of the Necessary by His essence, and the establishment of His positive attributes subsisting in His essence, I inform you that He repels from you the difficulty of multiplicity of the eternals, that you say: The attributes subsisting in the essence of the Necessary, established as additional to it externally, are not other than the essence of the Necessary of existence, nor are they identical to the essence.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage presents the Mu'tazilite objection against the attributes of meanings (such as knowledge, power, will) and the response from the poem. The objection argues that if attributes are additional to God's essence, they must be either originated (haditha) or eternal (qadima). If originated, then God's essence would be a locus for originated things, implying change, and He would lack perfections in pre-eternity. If eternal, then there would be multiple eternal entities, which is disbelief; Christians were condemned for asserting two eternal persons (Father and Son), so positing many eternals is worse. The response (from the poet's line 'thumma sifat al-dhat') asserts that the attributes are neither entirely other than the essence (laysat bi-ghayr al-dhat) nor identical to it (laysat bi-'ayn al-dhat). This means they are not separate entities, but nor are they mere aspects without distinction. This resolves the dilemma of multiplicity without falling into either extreme.

Key Terms
صفات الذات
غير الذات
عين الذات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Ash'arite response says attributes are identical to the essence or that they are completely separate.
Correction: The response explicitly says they are neither other nor identical, a middle position.

Checkpoint
According to the poet's response, what is the relationship between the attributes and the essence?
A) They are other than the essence.
B) They are identical to the essence.
C) They are neither other nor identical.
D) They are both other and identical.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'arite response resolves the dilemma by affirming that attributes are real yet not separate entities, being neither other than God's essence nor identical to it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself imagining God's attributes as if they are separate 'parts' of Him, or do you reduce them to mere human concepts? How does this lesson challenge your mental picture of God?
?
The poet says 'He repels from you the difficulty.' Have you truly allowed God to remove the intellectual anxiety about His attributes, or do you still carry doubts? What would it look like to trust this formulation in your worship tonight?
?
Can you identify an area of your life where you either treat something as 'other than' God (separate from His control) or 'identical to' God (making it an idol)? How does the principle of 'neither other nor identical' reshape your mindset?

The Four Types of Divine Attributes
Classification of divine attributes into four types with enumerations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourfold classification of divine attributes in Ash'ari theology and the specific attributes listed under each type.

Core Idea
Divine attributes are neatly classified into essential, negative, conceptual, and relational types.

Theology requires a precise vocabulary for speaking about God's attributes. Sanusi presents a widely accepted classification of divine attributes into four types, each with a distinct relation to God's essence. This lesson outlines that taxonomy.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification passage
Read the Arabic passage that lists the four types of attributes. Focus on the names of the types and the attributes enumerated under each.
The passage begins with 'قد عرفت مما مضى' and ends with 'وإن كان في بعض ذلك خلاف'.
2
Identify the four types and their Arabic names
Note the four Arabic terms: صفة نفسية, صفات سلبية, صفات معان, صفات معنوية. Write them down with their English translations.
These terms are central to Ash'ari kalam.
3
Count the attributes in each type
Observe that nafsiyya has one attribute (existence), salbiyya has five, ma'ani has seven, and ma'nawiyya has seven.
Memorize the numbers: 1, 5, 7, 7.
4
Reflect on the preferred status
Sanusi states that this classification is the preferred one. Consider why this might be the standard view.
There is disagreement, but this is the widely accepted system.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قد عرفت مما مضى أن صفات الله تعالى على أربعة أنواع: الأول: صفة نفسية وهي: الوجود، والثاني: صفات سلبية وهي خمس: القدم، والبقاء، ومخالفته تعالى للحوادث، وقيامه تعالى بنفسه، والوحدانية، والثالث: صفات معان، وهي سبع: القدرة، والإرادة، والعلم، والحياة، والسمع، والبصر، والكلام، والرابع: صفات معنوية وهي سبع: كونه قادرا، ومريدا، وعالما، و حيا، وسميعا، وبصيرا، ومتكلما، وهذا ما رجحناه تبعا للمؤلف والشارح، وإن كان في بعض ذلك خلاف. أما الصفة النفسية عند من قال بها وهو الأشعري فهي عين الموصوف؛ فالوجود عين الموجود عنده، وهي عند غيره غير الذات؛ فالوجود عندهم غير الموجود. وأما الصفات السلبية الخمس فهي غير الذات من قبل أنها أمور عدمية وهذا واضح جدا. وأما صفات الأفعال مثل الإحياء والإماتة والرزق وأشباهها؛ فهي غير الذات أيضا، بمعنى أنها منفكة عنها من قبل أنها عند التحقيق تعلقات القدرة التنجيزية الحادثة.
You have known from what has preceded that the attributes of God, exalted is He, are of four types: The first: the attribute of the essence (nafsiyya), which is existence. The second: negative attributes (salbiyya), which are five: pre-eternity, everlastingness, His opposition to originated things, His self-subsistence, and unity. The third: attributes of meanings (ma'ani), which are seven: power, will, knowledge, life, hearing, sight, and speech. The fourth: attributes of the meaning-derived (ma'nawiyya), which are seven: His being powerful, willing, knowing, living, hearing, seeing, and speaking. This is what we have preferred, following the author and the commentator, although there is disagreement in some of that. As for the attribute of the essence (nafsiyya) according to the one who affirms it, namely al-Ash'ari, it is identical to the described; thus existence is identical to the existent with him, and with others it is other than the essence; thus existence with them is other than the existent. As for the five negative attributes, they are other than the essence because they are non-existential matters, and this is very clear. As for the attributes of actions, such as giving life, causing death, providing sustenance, and the like, they are also other than the essence, in the sense that they are separable from it, because in reality they are relations of the determinate power that occur.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage provides a classification of divine attributes. The author states that there are four types based on the preferred view following the original poet and the commentator. First is the attribute of the essence (nafsiyya), which is existence itself. Second are negative attributes (salbiyya), which negate imperfections from God; five are listed: pre-eternity, everlastingness, being unlike originated things, self-subsistence, and unity. Third are attributes of meanings (ma'ani), which are real, positive attributes subsisting in the essence: power, will, knowledge, life, hearing, sight, speech. Fourth are attributes of the meaning-derived (ma'nawiyya), which express the state of the essence as qualified by those meanings, e.g., being powerful. The passage then discusses each type's relation to the essence: for al-Ash'ari, the nafsiyya attribute (existence) is identical to the essence. For others, existence is other than the essence. Negative attributes are other than the essence because they are non-existential (they are mere negations). Attributes of actions (like giving life) are also other than the essence because they are separable, being relations of God's power that happen in time.

Key Terms
صفة نفسية
صفات سلبية
صفات معان
صفات معنوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many negative (salbiyya) attributes are listed in this classification?
A) Three
B) Four
C) Five
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
Sanusi divides divine attributes into four types: nafsiyya (essential, one), salbiyya (negative, five), ma'ani (meanings, seven), and ma'nawiyya (derived, seven).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Knowing that God's existence is His essential attribute, how does this truth reshape your reliance on your own existence throughout the day? Will you consciously remind yourself that He alone is the self-subsistent, while you are contingent?
?
The negative attributes protect your understanding of God from any imperfection. Which of the five negatives do you find hardest to truly internalize in your heart? What would change if you lived as if God has no beginning, no end, and is unlike anything you've ever known?
?
You have just classified God's attributes into types. But does your worship reflect the reality that God is powerful, willing, and knowing in every moment? Is there an area where you act as if He is not all-powerful or unaware? What concrete step will you take this week to align your life with His attributes?

Divine Attributes

The Relation of Attributes to the Essence
Analyzes the relation of nafsiyya, salbiyya, and attributes of action to the essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different ways attributes relate to God's essence: identity for nafsiyya, non-existential for salbiyya, and temporal separability for attributes of action.

Core Idea
Not all divine attributes are identical to the essence; some are negations, others are temporal relations.

After classifying the attributes, Sanusi clarifies how each type relates to the essence. This is a key point of theological nuance, especially regarding whether existence is identical to God or distinct. He also distinguishes attributes of action as separable temporal relations.

Guided Path
1
Read the explanation passage
Read the second part of the source, beginning with 'أما الصفة النفسية'. This section discusses the metaphysical relation of each attribute type to the essence.
Focus on the three categories: nafsiyya, salbiyya, and attributes of action.
2
Understand the Ash'ari position on nafsiyya
Note that for al-Ash'ari, the nafsiyya attribute (existence) is identical to the essence ('ayn al-mawsuf). For others, it is additional.
This is a key difference within the Ash'ari school.
3
Understand negative attributes as non-existential
The salbiyya attributes are 'non-existential matters' (umur 'adamiyya), meaning they are negations, not positive attributes. Therefore they are other than the essence.
This makes sense because negation does not add a real entity.
4
Understand attributes of actions as separable
Attributes like giving life are 'ta'allaqat' (relations) of God's power that occur in time. They are separable from the essence, unlike the eternal attributes.
This distinguishes them from the ma'ani attributes which are eternal.

?

The Threefold Relation of Essence and Attributes
Classification of relations between a thing and another.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three possible relations between a thing and another (identity, inseparable difference, separable difference) and how they apply to the debate on divine attributes.

Core Idea
Not every 'other' is separable; some differences are inseparable in reality.

Before we can decide whether God's attributes are identical to His essence or distinct, we need a clear framework for thinking about relations between two things. This lesson presents that framework: the threefold division of sameness and difference. Understanding this classification is essential for following the theological dispute that follows.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice how the author first establishes an undeniable distinction between essence and attribute, then presents the threefold classification.
The author uses the example of 'wheat is grain' to illustrate complete identity.
2
Identify the three divisions
Find the three categories: (1) the thing identical to the thing, (2) the thing other in reality but inseparable, (3) the thing other in reality and separable. Write them down in your own words.
3
Compare with the twofold division
Some scholars use only a twofold division (identical vs. other). Ask yourself why the threefold division is more precise and why it matters for the attributes debate.
The twofold division misses the category of inseparable otherness, which is crucial for the Sunni position.
4
Connect to the broader debate
Reflect on how this classification will be used: the Mu'tazilites assume that if attributes are 'other' they must be separable (leading to problems), but the Sunni response will argue that attributes are 'other in reality yet inseparable'.
This lesson sets the stage for the Mu'tazilite objection and the Sunni answer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبقي صفات المعاني السبع - وهي التي عبر المصنف عنها هنا بصفات الذات ـ وهي التي ثارت فيها عجاجة أهل الكلام واختلفوا فيها اختلافًا طويلا أهي عين الذات، أم هي غير الذات، أم هي لا عين الذات ولا غيرها. وقبل أن نخوض في هذا البحث نقرر لك أنه مما لا خلاف فيه أن حقيقة الذات غير حقيقة الصفة، وإلا يكن الأمر كذلك لزم اتحاد الصفة والموصوف، وهو أمر لا يعقل. كما نقرر لك أن الشيء إما أن يكون نفس الشيء بمعنى لا خلاف بينهما لا في المفهوم ولا في غيره، كما يقال: البر هو القمح، وإما أن يكون غيره، وهذا إما أن يكون بينهما تلازم بحيث لا ينفك أحدهما عن الآخر، وإما ألا يكون بينهما تلازم بحيث يمكن أن يتفارقا، فالأقسام ثلاثة: الشيء نفس الشيء، والشيء غير الشيء في الحقيقة لكنهما لا يتفارقان، والشيء غير الشيء في الحقيقة وهما يتفارقان. ومن الناس من جعل القسمة ثنائية، فقال: الشيء إما أن يكون هو الشيء وإما أن يكون غيره. إذا علمت هذا فاعلم أن المعتزلة - تبعا لقدوتهم الفلاسفة - ذهبوا إلى أن الله تعالى قادر بذاته وعالم بذاته ومريد بذاته، وهكذا ...، وبعبارة أخرى ذهبوا إلى أنه ليست هناك صفة تسمى العلم، ولا صفة تسمى القدرة، ولا صفة تسمى الإرادة. قالوا: لا سبيل إلى إثبات صفة، أي صفة لله تعالى؛ لأن الصفة غير الموصوف البتة، ولو أثبتنا له صفات غير ذاته لم يكن بد من أحد أمرين: فإما أن تكون هذه الصفات حادثة، وإما أن تكون قديمة. فإن كانت حادثة لزم قيام الحوادث بذاته، وخلوه في الأزل عن الكمالات. وإن كانت قديمة لزم تعدد القدماء.
And there remain the seven attributes of meanings - which the author here expressed as attributes of the essence - and it is about them that the dust of the people of kalam was stirred, and they differed greatly: are they identical to the essence, or other than the essence, or neither identical nor other? Before we delve into this research, we establish for you that it is undebated that the reality of the essence is different from the reality of the attribute, otherwise the union of attribute and described would be necessary, which is unintelligible. Also we establish for you that a thing is either the very thing, meaning no difference between them in concept or otherwise, as is said: wheat is grain; or it is other than it, and this either with such inseparability that neither is separate from the other, or without such inseparability so that they can separate. Thus the divisions are three: the thing identical to the thing, the thing other than the thing in reality but inseparable, and the thing other than the thing in reality and separable. Some people made the division twofold, saying a thing is either the thing or other than it. Now that you know this, know that the Mu'tazilites - following their exemplars, the philosophers - held that God, exalted is He, is powerful by His essence, knowing by His essence, willing by His essence, and so on. In other words, they held that there is no attribute called knowledge, nor attribute called power, nor attribute called will. They said: There is no way to affirm an attribute, any attribute of God, because the attribute is entirely other than the described, and if we affirm for Him attributes other than His essence, then one of two matters is unavoidable: either these attributes are originated, or they are eternal. If they are originated, then the occurrence of originated things in His essence would be necessary, and His lack of perfections in pre-eternity. And if they are eternal, then multiplicity of the eternals would be necessary.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage focuses on the seven attributes of meanings (ma'ani) and the controversy surrounding their relationship to the essence. The author first notes that there is an unavoidable distinction between the reality of the essence and the reality of the attribute; otherwise, attribute and described would be identical, which is unintelligible. Then a threefold classification of the relation between two things is given: (1) they can be identical in every respect (like 'wheat' and 'grain'), (2) they can be different in reality but inseparable (like a object and its necessary concomitant), or (3) they can be different and separable. Some scholars only use a twofold division: identical or other. The author then presents the Mu'tazilite position, which follows the philosophers. The Mu'tazilites deny that there are real attributes (e.g., knowledge, power) subsisting in God's essence. Instead, they say God is knowing by His essence, etc. Their argument is that if attributes were real and other than the essence, they would have to be either originated (making God a locus of change) or eternal (implying multiple eternal entities), both of which are unacceptable. Therefore, they conclude that attributes cannot be real. The author is setting up the Sunni response that the attributes are neither identical nor entirely other, but a third category: they are other in meaning but inseparable from the essence.

Key Terms
عين الذات
غير الذات
القسمة الثنائية
القسمة الثلاثية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If attributes are not identical to the essence, they must be completely separate entities that can exist independently.
Correction: The threefold division shows that otherness does not imply separability; attributes are other in concept but inseparable in existence.

Checkpoint
According to the threefold division, which category best describes the Sunni view of divine attributes relative to the essence?
A) Identical in every respect
B) Other in reality but inseparable
C) Other in reality and separable
D) Neither identical nor other

Key Takeaway
The threefold classification (identity, inseparable otherness, separable otherness) provides the logical framework for the Sunni position that attributes are distinct from the essence yet eternally inseparable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Before studying this lesson, did you ever reduce the relationship between Allah's essence and His attributes to either complete identity or complete separation? How might that oversimplification affect your understanding of tawhid?
?
The passage warns against a twofold division that ignores inseparable otherness. Are there areas in your own faith where you have accepted a simplistic either/or, avoiding the deeper middle ground that preserves both unity and distinction? Commit to investigating one such area this week.
?
If the reality of essence is truly distinct from the reality of attribute, how does that impact the way you relate to Allah through His attributes like mercy or justice? Are you honoring both His essence and His attributes in your worship, or reducing one to the other?

The Mu'tazilite Denial of Real Attributes
Presentation of the Mu'tazilite argument against real attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite argument against the existence of real divine attributes and the dilemma they pose.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazilites argue that real attributes lead to an impossible choice: either God changes or there are multiple eternal beings.

Now that we have a clear classification of relations, the author presents the Mu'tazilite position. They deny that attributes like knowledge, power, and will are real entities subsisting in God. Instead, they say God is knowing by His essence, etc. Their argument is based on a dilemma: if attributes were real and other than the essence, they must be either originated (which implies change in God) or eternal (which implies multiple eternal beings). Both are considered impossible. This lesson presents their reasoning, which sets up the Sunni response that follows.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note that the Mu'tazilites follow the philosophers in denying real attributes. They affirm that God is powerful, knowing, willing 'by His essence'.
The phrase 'by His essence' means that these are not additional entities.
2
Identify the dilemma
The Mu'tazilites present a dilemma: if attributes are real and other, they must be either originated or eternal. Find these two options in the text.
They reject both because each leads to a theological problem.
3
Analyze the two consequences
First consequence: if originated, then God would be subject to change and would lack perfections in pre-eternity. Second consequence: if eternal, then there would be multiple eternal entities, which contradicts the oneness of God.
These are classical objections against real attributes.
4
Understand the Mu'tazilite conclusion
Since both options are unacceptable, the Mu'tazilites conclude that there are no real attributes; rather, God's attributes are identical to His essence.
This is the position of the Mu'tazilites and the philosophers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبقي صفات المعاني السبع - وهي التي عبر المصنف عنها هنا بصفات الذات ـ وهي التي ثارت فيها عجاجة أهل الكلام واختلفوا فيها اختلافًا طويلا أهي عين الذات، أم هي غير الذات، أم هي لا عين الذات ولا غيرها. وقبل أن نخوض في هذا البحث نقرر لك أنه مما لا خلاف فيه أن حقيقة الذات غير حقيقة الصفة، وإلا يكن الأمر كذلك لزم اتحاد الصفة والموصوف، وهو أمر لا يعقل. كما نقرر لك أن الشيء إما أن يكون نفس الشيء بمعنى لا خلاف بينهما لا في المفهوم ولا في غيره، كما يقال: البر هو القمح، وإما أن يكون غيره، وهذا إما أن يكون بينهما تلازم بحيث لا ينفك أحدهما عن الآخر، وإما ألا يكون بينهما تلازم بحيث يمكن أن يتفارقا، فالأقسام ثلاثة: الشيء نفس الشيء، والشيء غير الشيء في الحقيقة لكنهما لا يتفارقان، والشيء غير الشيء في الحقيقة وهما يتفارقان. ومن الناس من جعل القسمة ثنائية، فقال: الشيء إما أن يكون هو الشيء وإما أن يكون غيره. إذا علمت هذا فاعلم أن المعتزلة - تبعا لقدوتهم الفلاسفة - ذهبوا إلى أن الله تعالى قادر بذاته وعالم بذاته ومريد بذاته، وهكذا ...، وبعبارة أخرى ذهبوا إلى أنه ليست هناك صفة تسمى العلم، ولا صفة تسمى القدرة، ولا صفة تسمى الإرادة. قالوا: لا سبيل إلى إثبات صفة، أي صفة لله تعالى؛ لأن الصفة غير الموصوف البتة، ولو أثبتنا له صفات غير ذاته لم يكن بد من أحد أمرين: فإما أن تكون هذه الصفات حادثة، وإما أن تكون قديمة. فإن كانت حادثة لزم قيام الحوادث بذاته، وخلوه في الأزل عن الكمالات. وإن كانت قديمة لزم تعدد القدماء.
And there remain the seven attributes of meanings - which the author here expressed as attributes of the essence - and it is about them that the dust of the people of kalam was stirred, and they differed greatly: are they identical to the essence, or other than the essence, or neither identical nor other? Before we delve into this research, we establish for you that it is undebated that the reality of the essence is different from the reality of the attribute, otherwise the union of attribute and described would be necessary, which is unintelligible. Also we establish for you that a thing is either the very thing, meaning no difference between them in concept or otherwise, as is said: wheat is grain; or it is other than it, and this either with such inseparability that neither is separate from the other, or without such inseparability so that they can separate. Thus the divisions are three: the thing identical to the thing, the thing other than the thing in reality but inseparable, and the thing other than the thing in reality and separable. Some people made the division twofold, saying a thing is either the thing or other than it. Now that you know this, know that the Mu'tazilites - following their exemplars, the philosophers - held that God, exalted is He, is powerful by His essence, knowing by His essence, willing by His essence, and so on. In other words, they held that there is no attribute called knowledge, nor attribute called power, nor attribute called will. They said: There is no way to affirm an attribute, any attribute of God, because the attribute is entirely other than the described, and if we affirm for Him attributes other than His essence, then one of two matters is unavoidable: either these attributes are originated, or they are eternal. If they are originated, then the occurrence of originated things in His essence would be necessary, and His lack of perfections in pre-eternity. And if they are eternal, then multiplicity of the eternals would be necessary.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage focuses on the seven attributes of meanings (ma'ani) and the controversy surrounding their relationship to the essence. The author first notes that there is an unavoidable distinction between the reality of the essence and the reality of the attribute; otherwise, attribute and described would be identical, which is unintelligible. Then a threefold classification of the relation between two things is given: (1) they can be identical in every respect (like 'wheat' and 'grain'), (2) they can be different in reality but inseparable (like a object and its necessary concomitant), or (3) they can be different and separable. Some scholars only use a twofold division: identical or other. The author then presents the Mu'tazilite position, which follows the philosophers. The Mu'tazilites deny that there are real attributes (e.g., knowledge, power) subsisting in God's essence. Instead, they say God is knowing by His essence, etc. Their argument is that if attributes were real and other than the essence, they would have to be either originated (making God a locus of change) or eternal (implying multiple eternal entities), both of which are unacceptable. Therefore, they conclude that attributes cannot be real. The author is setting up the Sunni response that the attributes are neither identical nor entirely other, but a third category: they are other in meaning but inseparable from the essence.

Key Terms
صفات المعاني
المعتزلة
حدوث الصفات
قدم الصفات
تعدد القدماء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazilites affirm attributes like knowledge and power as real entities separate from God.
Correction: They explicitly deny that there are attributes called knowledge, power, or will; they say God is knowing by His essence, not by a distinct attribute.

Checkpoint
What is the Mu'tazilite argument against real attributes?
A) They say attributes are identical to the essence because the Qur'an says so.
B) They claim that if attributes are other than the essence, either they are originated (leading to change in God) or eternal (leading to multiple eternals), both impossible.
C) They argue that attributes cannot be known by reason, so we must deny them.
D) They say that affirming attributes leads to anthropomorphism.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilites deny real attributes by presenting a dilemma: if attributes were distinct from the essence, they would be either created (implying change in God) or eternal (implying multiple eternal beings), both of which they consider impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of God's attributes like knowledge or power, do you ever feel a tension between His oneness and the multiplicity of descriptions? How does this lesson expose your own reliance on human logic over the revealed texts?
?
Have you ever been tempted to simplify God's nature to avoid intellectual discomfort, just as the Mu'tazilites did? In what area of your faith might you be doing this today?
?
The Mu'tazilites claimed to protect God's perfection by denying real attributes. Could it be that your own attempts to 'defend' God actually limit Him? Where do you need to submit to divine revelation instead of your own reasoning?

The Four Categories of Divine Attributes in Kalam
Enumerates the four categories of divine attributes and lists the seven within each.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four-category classification of divine attributes: self-existence, oneness, attributes of meaning, and meaningful attributes.

Core Idea
The four types of divine attributes structure all kalam theology.

The author begins by outlining the primary classification of divine attributes that is favored by most Ash‘ari scholars. This passage introduces the four categories that form the bedrock of theological discussion about God's nature. Understanding these categories is essential because they determine how we speak about God's qualities without anthropomorphism.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
Read the Arabic and find the numbers (first, second, third, fourth). Notice that the first two are 'self-existence' and 'oneness'.
These are foundational categories.
2
Understand attributes of meaning
The third category lists seven real attributes that subsist in the essence. Memorize the list: power, will, knowledge, life, hearing, sight, speech.
These are the ṣifāt ma‘ānī.
3
Understand meaningful attributes
The fourth category lists seven derived descriptions (being powerful, etc.). These are judgments about the essence based on the real attributes.
These are the ṣifāt ma‘nawiyya.
4
Note the author's preference
The author states that this classification is preferred despite some disagreement. Understand that other classifications exist.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم الإلهيات: تعالى بنفسه، والوحدانية، والثالث: صفات معانٍ، وهي سبع: القدرة، والإرادة، والعلم، والحياة، والسمع، والبصر، والكلام. والرابع: صفات معنوية وهي سبع: كونه قادراً، ومريداً، وعالماً، وحيّاً، وسميعاً، وبصيراً، ومتكلماً. وهذا ما رجحناه تبعاً للمؤلف والشارح، وإن كان في بعض ذلك خلاف. أما الصفة النفسية عند من قال بها وهو الأشعري فهي عين الموصوف؛ فالوجود عين الموجود عنده، وهي عند غيره غير الذات؛ فالوجود عندهم غير الموجود. وأما الصفات السلبية الخمس فهي غير الذات بأنها ليست قائمة بالذات، وذلك من بمعنى أنها أمور عدمية وهذا واضح جداً. وأما صفات الأفعال مثل الإحياء والإماتة والرزق وأشباهها؛ فهي غير الذات أيضاً، بمعنى القدرة التنجيزية الحادثة.
The Divine Section: He is self-existent, oneness, and third: attributes of meaning, which are seven: power, will, knowledge, life, hearing, sight, speech. And fourth: meaningful attributes, which are seven: His being powerful, willing, knowing, living, hearing, seeing, speaking. And this is what we have preferred following the author and the commentator, even though there is some disagreement about some of that. As for the psychological attribute according to the one who affirmed it, namely al-Ash‘arī, it is identical to the described; thus existence is identical to the existent according to him. And according to others it is other than the essence; thus existence is other than the existent. As for the five negative attributes, they are other than the essence in that they are not subsisting in the essence, and that is because they are privative matters, and this is very clear. As for attributes of actions such as giving life, causing death, providing sustenance and the like, they are also other than the essence, meaning the newly originated effective power.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage defines the four categories of divine attributes. First, attributes of meaning (ṣifāt ma‘ānī) are the seven real attributes that subsist in the essence: power, will, knowledge, life, hearing, sight, speech. Second, meaningful attributes (ṣifāt ma‘nawiyya) are the derived descriptions like ‘being powerful’ which are judgments about the essence. The author notes that this is the preferred classification. Then it discusses the psychological attribute (al-ṣifa al-nafsiyya): for al-Ash‘arī, it is identical to the essence (e.g., existence is identical to the existent), while others hold it is distinct. The five negative attributes (ṣifāt sulūbiyya) are described as privative and not subsisting in the essence. Finally, attributes of actions (ṣifāt af‘āl) like giving life are also distinct from the essence, as they are relational or newly originated effects.

Key Terms
صفات المعاني
صفات معنوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think attributes of meaning and meaningful attributes are identical.
Correction: Attributes of meaning are the real subsisting attributes; meaningful attributes are the derived descriptions of the essence.

Checkpoint
How many attributes of meaning (ṣifāt ma‘ānī) are listed in this passage?
A) Five
B) Seven
C) Twenty
D) Three

Key Takeaway
The core classification divides divine attributes into four: self-existence, oneness, attributes of meaning, and meaningful attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'Allah is All-Powerful,' do you truly believe that His power is a real attribute inhering in His essence, or do you just say it without understanding? How would your life change if you internalized that God's power is not just a concept but a real meaning in His being?
?
The passage distinguishes between the attribute of power (صفت القدرة) and being powerful (كونه قادرا). Is your worship based on acknowledging both the attribute and the state? What would it mean for you to truly live in awe of a God who is eternally powerful?
?
Reflect on the fact that these seven attributes of meaning are considered real by scholars. Do you treat God's knowledge, life, and speech as real, personal, and immediate to your daily experience? Or do you reduce them to abstract ideas? What is one practical step you can take today to cultivate awe and love for the Living, Knowing, Speaking God?

Additional Categories: Psychological, Negative, and Attributes of Action
Explains three additional categories of divine attributes: psychological, negative, and actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three additional categories of divine attributes: the psychological attribute, the five negative attributes, and the attributes of actions.

Core Idea
Beyond the four, Ash‘ari scholars also discuss psychological, negative, and action attributes.

After presenting the preferred four-category classification, the author addresses further categories that other scholars have used. These include the psychological attribute (which al-Ash‘ari identifies with the essence), the five negative attributes (which are privative), and the attributes of actions (which are relational). Understanding these helps resolve disagreements in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read about the psychological attribute
Identify the view of al-Ash‘ari (it is identical to the described) and the view of others (it is distinct).
The example of existence and the existent clarifies the difference.
2
Understand negative attributes
The five negative attributes are not subsisting in the essence; they are privative matters (e.g., lack of composition).
They are other than the essence in that they are only negations.
3
Understand attributes of actions
Attributes like giving life and causing death are not eternal; they are newly originated effective power.
They are relational and depend on created effects.

The Threefold Division of Identity and Otherness
Establishes a three-way classification of identity and difference to frame the attribute debate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the threefold classification of identity and otherness as the logical groundwork for the debate on divine attributes.

Core Idea
Identity and otherness are not binary; there is a middle category of inseparable otherness.

Before the major controversy over the seven attributes of meaning can be addressed, the author establishes an essential logical classification. He clarifies that one thing may be identical to another, distinct but inseparable, or distinct and separable. This threefold division provides the conceptual toolkit needed to evaluate the different theological positions on whether attributes are identical to the essence or not.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the agreed premise
Notice that the author first asserts an uncontroversial point: the reality of the essence is distinct from the reality of the attribute. This avoided a logical absurdity—the union of attribute and described.
This premise is accepted by all sides, including those who later claim identity.
2
Learn the three categories
Read the classification carefully. The author explains that a thing can be identical to another (e.g., wheat is wheat), or other in reality but inseparable, or other and separable. Identify the examples given.
3
Contrast with the binary view
Some theologians reduce this to a binary distinction (identical or other). Understand why the threefold division is more precise and how it sets up the Ash‘arī position on attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبقي صفات المعاني السبع - وهي التي عبر المصنف عنها هنا بصفات الذات - وهي التي ثارت فيها عجاجة أهل الكلام واختلفوا فيها اختلافاً طويلاً أهي عين الذات، أم هي غير الذات، أم هي لا عين الذات ولا غيرها. وقبل أن نخوض في هذا البحث نقرر لك أن مما لا خلاف فيه أن حقيقة الذات غير حقيقة الصفة، وإلا يكن الأمر كذلك لزم اتحاد الصفة والموصوف، وهو أمر لا يعقل. كما نقرر لك أن الشيء إما أن يكون نفس الشيء بمعنى لا خلاف بينهما لا في المفهوم ولا في غيره، كما يقال: البر هو القمح، وإما أن يكون غيره. وهذا إما أن يكون بينهما تلازم بحيث لا ينفك أحدهما عن الآخر، وإما ألا يكون بينهما تلازم بحيث يمكن أن يتفارقا. فالأقسام ثلاثة: الشيء نفس الشيء، والشيء غير الشيء في الحقيقة لكنهما لا يتفارقان، والشيء غير الشيء في الحقيقة وهما يتفارقان. ومن الناس من جعل القسمة ثنائية، فقال: الشيء إما أن يكون هو الشيء وإما أن يكون غيره.
And there remain the seven attributes of meaning—which the author here called attributes of the essence—which stirred up the strife of the theologians and over which they differed at length: whether they are identical to the essence, or other than the essence, or neither identical nor other. Before we delve into this research, we affirm to you that there is no disagreement that the reality of the essence is other than the reality of the attribute—otherwise it would necessitate the union of attribute and described, which is inconceivable. And we also affirm to you that a thing is either the same as another thing, meaning there is no difference between them in concept or otherwise, as it is said: 'wheat is wheat', or it is other than it. And this otherness is either such that they are inseparable, so that one cannot be separated from the other, or they are separable. So the divisions are three: the thing is identical to the thing, the thing is other than the thing in reality but they are inseparable, and the thing is other than the thing in reality and they are separable. Some people made the division binary, saying a thing is either identical or other.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage is a preliminary to discussing the real controversy over the seven attributes of meaning. It first asserts the agreed fact that the essence and the attribute are really distinct in reality; otherwise they would be identical, which is absurd. Then it presents a threefold logical classification: (1) Identity: two things are the same in every respect (e.g., wheat is wheat). (2) Other but inseparable: two things are distinct in reality but always found together, like qualities with their substrate. (3) Other and separable: two things can exist apart. The passage notes that some reduce this to a binary distinction. This classification is crucial for understanding the Ash‘arī position that attributes are neither identical (like the Mu‘tazila claim) nor separate in every respect (which would imply multiple eternal entities).

Key Terms
عين الذات
غير الذات
تلازم
اتحاد الصفة والموصوف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'other' always implies separability, assuming that distinct things can always be separated.
Correction: The passage introduces a middle category of 'other but inseparable', showing that distinctness does not entail separability.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, how many divisions are there regarding identity and otherness?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) One

Key Takeaway
The debate on divine attributes rests on a precise logical framework: things can be identical, inseparable but distinct, or separable; the Ash‘arī position occupies the middle category.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Commit today to praise Allah by name and attribute as one inseparable reality.
?

?
The passage warns against the absurdity of union of attribute and described. Is there any area in your faith where you have unknowingly 'united' Allah with His creation—for example, by imagining His attributes as created? Resolve to clarify your understanding so your worship is built on tawḥīd.

Mu'tazila and Karāmiyya on Divine Attributes
Presents two sectarian arguments and their refutations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila argument against real attributes and the Karāmiyya alternative, and why both are considered problematic in Sunni theology.

Core Idea
Denying God's attributes or making them created both lead to impossible consequences.

This passage presents two opposing heretical views on God's attributes. The Mu'tazila deny real attributes, arguing they lead to either accidents in God or multiple eternal beings. The Karāmiyya affirm attributes but claim they are created. Both positions are refuted by the orthodox Sunni stance. Let's examine the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the translation. Notice the two groups mentioned.
The passage uses a dilemma structure for the Mu'tazila.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila dilemma
Find the two possibilities the Mu'tazila propose about attributes. Understand why both are impossible.
Key terms: قيام الحادث بالقديم and تعدد القدماء.
3
Understand the Karāmiyya position
See how they tried to avoid one problem but fell into the other. Recognize why their solution is also false.
They accepted attributes but said they are created.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا علمت هذا فاعلم أن المعتزلة - تبعاً لقدوتهم الفلاسفة - ذهبوا إلى أن الله تعالى قادر بذاته وعالم بذاته ومريد بذاته، وهكذا. وبعبارة أخرى ذهبوا إلى أنه ليست هناك صفة تسمى العلم، ولا صفة تسمى القدرة، ولا صفة تسمى الإرادة. قالوا: لا سبيل إلى إثبات صفة من صفات الله تعالى؛ لأن الصفة غير الموصوف البتة. ولو أثبتنا له صفات غير ذاته لم يكن بد من أحد أمرين: فإما أن تكون هذه الصفات حادثة، وإما أن تكون قديمة. فإن كانت حادثة - والفرض أنها قائمة بذاته تعالى - لزم قيام الحادث بالقديم، وهو محال. وإن كانت قديمة - والفرض أنها غير ذاته - لزم أن تكون قدماء متعددة بتعدد الصفات زيادة على الذات، والقول بتعدد القدماء هو الكفر بعينه. وقد نص الله تعالى على كفر من قال: إن الله ثالث ثلاثة، فكيف يكون حال من أثبت هذا العدد العديد من القدماء؟ وذهب الكرامية إلى إثبات الصفات، ولكنهم زعموا أنها حادثة، فروا من القول بتعدد القدماء، ولكنهم التزموا قيام الحادث بالقديم، وهو باطل؛ لما ثبت من قيامه بنفسه، ومخالفته للحوادث، ومن استحالة قيام الحادث بالقديم.
If you know this, then know that the Mu‘tazila, following their exemplars the philosophers, held that God is powerful by His essence, knowing by His essence, willing by His essence, and so on. In other words, they held that there is no attribute called knowledge, nor attribute called power, nor attribute called will. They said: there is no way to affirm any attribute of God; because attribute is absolutely other than the described. If we affirm for Him attributes other than His essence, then one of two things must be the case: either these attributes are originated, or they are eternal. If they are originated—and the assumption is that they subsist in His essence—then that would entail the subsistence of an originated thing in the eternal, which is impossible. And if they are eternal—and the assumption is that they are other than His essence—then that would entail multiple eternal beings according to the multiplicity of attributes in addition to the essence. And the statement of multiple eternal beings is pure unbelief. God indeed declared the unbelief of one who says God is the third of three; so what would be the case of one who affirms this numerous number of eternal beings? And the Karāmiyya held the affirmation of attributes, but they claimed that they are originated. They fled from the statement of multiple eternal beings, but they committed themselves to the subsistence of the originated in the eternal, which is false; because of what has been established of His self-subsistence, His being unlike originated things, and the impossibility of the subsistence of the originated in the eternal.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage presents the arguments of two sects. The Mu‘tazila deny real attributes because they lead to a dilemma: either the attributes are created (which would mean accidents subsist in God) or they are eternal (which would mean multiple eternal entities). Both are impossible, so they conclude God is powerful/knowing by His essence, not by attributes. They cite the Quranic condemnation of trinitarianism. The Karāmiyya accept attributes but claim they are created, trying to avoid multiple eternals. However, this leads to the same problem of accidents in God, which is false because God is self-subsistent and unlike originated things. So both positions are refuted.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
الكرامية
قيام الحادث بالقديم
تعدد القدماء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Mu'tazila deny that God knows or has power; they actually affirm He knows/powers by His essence, not by attributes.
Correction: The Mu'tazila do not deny God's knowing and power; they deny that there are distinct eternal attributes such as 'knowledge' and 'power'.

Checkpoint
What dilemma did the Mu'tazila argue follows from affirming attributes other than God's essence?
A) Attributes must be either self-subsistent or dependent
B) Attributes must be either created or eternal, both leading to absurdity
C) Attributes must be either identical to essence or nothing
D) Attributes must be either physical or spiritual

Key Takeaway
Both denying real attributes and affirming created attributes lead to theological impossibility; the orthodox view affirms eternal attributes without separation from God's essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you speak of God's knowledge or power, do you truly believe they are real and eternal, or do you sometimes think of them as mere descriptions without substance? How does your answer affect your trust in His promises and judgments?
?
This lesson shows that denying God's attributes leads to a view similar to atheistic philosophy. Have you ever been influenced by a secular mindset that reduces God to an abstract force? What would it cost you to repent from that and affirm His living attributes?
?
The Karāmiyya thought they could 'fix' the problem by making attributes created, but they fell into an even worse error. Are there areas in your faith where you try to 'solve' a theological difficulty by compromising—thinking that a small concession is harmless? What is the one thing you are most tempted to compromise today?

Al-Ash'ari's Middle Path on Attributes
Al-Ash'ari's middle position on attributes and the verbal nature of the dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ash'ari's nuanced position on divine attributes and why al-Samarqandi considered the dispute with the Mu'tazila to be verbal.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari navigates between identity and separateness to preserve both transcendence and attributes.

Al-Ash'ari faced a dilemma: if attributes are identical to the essence, they are not real; if they are entirely separate, multiple eternal beings result. This passage shows how he crafted a middle path, using the distinction between conceptual and real otherness. Al-Samarqandi later clarifies that once this distinction is understood, the dispute becomes largely verbal.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Ash'ari's position
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully, noting how al-Ash'ari affirms attributes without falling into extremes.
2
Identify the key distinction
Focus on the phrase 'غير بالمفهوم' (other in concept) and understand how it resolves the charge of multiple eternals.
3
Examine al-Samarqandi's comment
Read his remark that the dispute is verbal, and see how he reconciles the labels.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this is not a mere compromise but a logical necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما أبو الحسن فنظر إلى المسألة من جميع وجوهها؛ فأثبت صفات الله تعالى للدليل العقلي والسمعي الدال على ثبوتها، وأثبت أنها قديمة لاستحالة قيام الحوادث بذات الله تعالى، ثم قال: إنه لا يلزم على ما نقول تعدد القدماء كما زعم المعتزلة؛ لأن هذا إنما يلزم لو قلنا: إن كل صفة من هذه الصفات غير الذات من كل وجه. وبعبارة أخرى إنما يلزمنا القول بتعدد القدماء لو كانت كل صفة قائمة بنفسها. ونحن لا نقول: إن كل صفة من هذه الصفات غير الذات من كل وجه، ولا نقول: إن كل صفة منها قائمة بنفسها، وإن كنا نقول: إن كل صفة غير سائر الصفات. وإنما نقول: إن كل صفة من هذه الصفات التي نثبتها لله تعالى غير الذات من حيث المفهوم، وهذا مما لا جدال فيه. ولكن كل صفة من هذه الصفات لازمة للذات؛ فلا تنفك الصفة عنها كما لا تنفك الذات عن الصفة. فالصفة على هذا ليست عين الذات من كل وجه، وليست غير الذات من كل وجه. وهذا معنى قول المصنف: «ليست بعين أو بغير الذات» جعلها الأشعري ليست غير الذات؛ لئلا يلزم قيام الحادث بالقديم أو القول بتعدد القدماء، وليست عين الذات فراراً مما ذهب إليه الفلاسفة والمعتزلة من نفي الصفات. وقال الشمس السمرقندي: (وهذا خلاف لفظي؛ لأن القول بأنها ليست بغير الذات محمول على الغير الذي ينفث عن الذات وإن كانت غيراً في المفهوم، والقول بأنها غير محمول على الغير في المفهوم وإن كانت تنفث عن الذات) اهـ كلامه. وفي هذا القدر كفاية.
As for Abū al-Ḥasan [al-Ash‘arī], he looked at the matter from all its aspects. He affirmed the attributes of God based on rational and revealed evidence indicating their existence, and affirmed that they are eternal because of the impossibility of originated things subsisting in God’s essence. Then he said: the statement of multiple eternal beings does not follow from our position, as the Mu‘tazila claimed, because that would only follow if we said that each attribute is other than the essence in every respect. In other words, the statement of multiple eternal beings would only be forced upon us if each attribute were self-subsistent. We do not say that each attribute is other than the essence in every respect, nor do we say that each attribute is self-subsistent. Rather, we say that each attribute is other than the other attributes. We only say that each attribute that we affirm for God is other than the essence from the perspective of concept, and this is indisputable. But each attribute is inseparable from the essence; the attribute does not separate from it just as the essence does not separate from the attribute. Thus the attribute is neither identical to the essence in every respect nor other than the essence in every respect. This is the meaning of the author’s statement: 'not identical nor other than the essence.' Al-Ash‘arī made it not other than the essence to avoid the subsistence of the originated in the eternal or the statement of multiple eternal beings, and not identical to the essence to avoid what the philosophers and Mu‘tazila went to of denying attributes. Al-Shams al-Samarqandī said: 'This is a verbal dispute; because the statement that they are not other than the essence is to be understood as other in the sense of being separate from the essence, even though they are other in concept; and the statement that they are other is to be understood as other in concept even though they are not separate from the essence.' His statement ends. In this amount there is sufficiency.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage presents al-Ash‘arī’s balanced position. He affirms attributes as real and eternal, based on both reason and revelation. He then argues that the charge of multiple eternal beings only applies if attributes are entirely separate from the essence and self-subsistent, which he does not claim. Instead, attributes are conceptually distinct (ghayr bi al-mafhūm) but not separate in reality; they are inseparable from the essence. Thus they are neither identical (like the Mu‘tazila claim) nor entirely other (which would imply multiple gods). The passage ends with al-Samarqandī’s remark that the dispute is verbal: both sides agree that attributes are conceptually distinct but not separate; the labels 'identical' or 'other' are just different ways of describing the same reality.

Key Terms
أبو الحسن الأشعري
الغير بالمفهوم
الخلاف اللفظي
الشمس السمرقندي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari's position is an evasive compromise.
Correction: It is a precise logical distinction that avoids real contradictions.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ash‘arī, why does affirming attributes not lead to multiple eternal beings?
A) Because attributes are created
B) Because attributes are identical to the essence
C) Because attributes are not self-subsistent nor separate in every respect
D) Because attributes are only mental concepts

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's via media between identity and separateness defines the Ash'ari doctrine of attributes and reveals the dispute as largely verbal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of God's attributes like His knowledge or power, do you imagine them as separate 'things' added to His essence? How does al-Ash'ari's teaching that they are other only in concept but inseparable confront your inner picture of God?
?
Consider a time you argued passionately about a religious issue. Could it be that the dispute was, as al-Samarqandī says, verbal? How would you react if you learned you were fighting over words while the reality was agreed upon?
?
Al-Ash'ari walked a razor's edge between two errors. Where in your own life do you avoid the difficult middle path, preferring instead the comfort of one extreme or the other?

The Mu'tazilite Dilemma and the Karramiyya Attempt
The Mu'tazilite objection and the Karramiyya response, both rejected.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite objection against the attributes of meaning and why the Karramiyya solution fails.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazilites forced a choice: attributes are either identical to the essence or other, both leading to absurdity.

The Mu'tazilites argued that affirming eternal attributes necessarily leads to polytheism or the impossible. They presented a dilemma: if attributes are identical to the essence, they must be originated; if they are other, they multiply eternal beings. The Karramiyya tried to avoid the second horn by making attributes originated, but that entailed the subsistence of the contingent in the eternal. This lesson presents the objection and the failed attempt.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazilite objection
Read the first part of the passage where the Mu'tazilite argument is presented as a dilemma. Notice the two horns: identity vs. otherness.
The dilemma is designed to force the denial of attributes.
2
Understand the consequences
Identify why each horn is unacceptable: identity leads to origination of attributes (impossible for the eternal); otherness leads to multiple eternals (kufr).
The Mu'tazilites cite the verse about the Trinity to emphasize the gravity.
3
Examine the Karramiyya position
Read how the Karramiyya tried to avoid the second horn by making attributes originated. Note the problem: originated things cannot subsist in the eternal.
The refutation here uses the attributes of the essence itself (self-subsistence, dissimilarity to originated things).
4
Reflect on the failure
Consider why the Karramiyya solution is rejected. They avoided one error but fell into another.
This sets the stage for the Ash'ari response.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تقرير شبهة المعتزلة في نفي صفات المعاني، ورَدُّها ; لأنا لو قلنا: «هي هو» لأدَّى إلى أن تكون حادثة - والفرض أنها قائمة بذاته تعالى - لزم قيام الحادث بالقديم، وهو مُحالٌ ; وإِنْ كانت قديمة - والفرض أنها غيرُ ذاته - لزم أن تكون قدماء متعددة بتعدد الصفاتِ زيادة على الذَّاتِ ; والقول بتعدد القدماء هو الكفر بعينه، وقد نصَّ الله تعالى على كفر من قال: إنَّ الله ثالث ثلاثة ، فكيف يكون حالَ مَن أثبت هذا العدد العديد من القدماء ؟ وذهب الكرامية إلى: إثبات الصفات، ولكنّهم زعموا أنَّها حادثةٌ، فَرُّوا مِن القول بتعدد القدماء ، ولكنَّهم التزموا قيام الحادث بالقديم ، وهو باطل ; لما ثبت من قيامه بنفسه ، ومخالفته للحوادث ، ومن استحالة قيام الحادث بالقديم، فأما أبو الحسن فنظر إلى المسألة من جميع وجوهها ; فأثبت صفات الله تعالى للدليل العقلي والسمعي الدال على ثبوتها، وأثبتَ أَنَّها قديمة لاستحالة قيام الحوادث بذات الله تعالى، ثمَّ قال: إنه لا يلزم على ما نقول: تعدد القدماء كما زعم المعتزلة ; لأنَّ هذا إِنَّما يلزم لو قلنا: إِنَّ كلَّ صفة من هذه الصفات غير الذَّات مِن كلِّ وجه ، وبعبارة أخرى إنَّما يُلْزِمُنَا القولُ بتعدد القدماء لو كانت كل صفةٍ قائمة بنفسها ، ونحن لا نقول: إنَّ كلَّ صفةٍ مِن هذه الصفات غير الذات من كل وجه، ولا نقول: إِنَّ كلَّ صفةٍ منها قائمةٌ بنفسها ، وإنْ كنا نقول: إِنَّ كلَّ صفةٍ غير سائر الصفات، وإنما نقول: إن كلَّ صفة من هذه الصفات التي نُثْبِتُها لله تعالى غير الذات من حيث المفهوم، وهذا مِمَّا لا جدال فيه، ولكن كلّ صفة من هذه الصفات لازمةٌ للذات ; فلا تنفكُ الصفة عنها كما لا تنفكُ الذات عن الصفة، فالصفة على هذا ليست عينَ الذَّاتِ مِن كلِّ وجه، وليست غير الذات مِن كُلِّ وجه، وهذا معنى قول المصنف : «ليست بعين أو بغير الذات» جعل الأشعري ليست غير الذات ; لئلا يلزم قيام الحادث بالقديم، أو القولُ بتعددِ القدماء، وليست عين الذات فرارًا ممَّا ذهب إليه الفلاسفة والمعتزلة من نفي الصفات، وقال الشَّمس السَّمَرْقَنْدِيُّ: وهذا خلافٌ لفظي ; لأنَّ القول بأنَّها ليست بغير الذات، محمول على الغير الذي ينفكُّ عن الذات وإن كانت غيرا في المفهوم ، والقول بأنها غيرُ، محمول على الغير في المفهوم وإن كانت تنفكُّ عن الذات اهـ كلامه ، وفي هذا القدر كفاية. وتلخيص ما أشار إليه من الجواب : أنَّ المَحذُورَ إنَّما هو تعدد القدماء المتغايرة، ونحن نمنع تغاير الذات مع الصفات والصِّفاتِ بعضها مع بعض، فينتفي التَّعدُّد ; لأنَّه لا يكون إلا مع التغاير، فلا يلزمُ التَّعدُّد، ولا التَّكثُر ، ولا قدمُ الغير ، ولا تكثر القدماء، فعلِم أَنَّ مذهب أهلِ السُّنَّة أنَّ صفاتِ الذَّات زائدة عليها ، قائمة بها لازمةٌ لها لزوما لا يقبل الانفكاك.
A presentation of the Mu'tazilite objection concerning the negation of attributes of meaning (sifat al-ma'ani), and the response to it: for if we say 'they are He (huwa),' it would entail that they are originated — but the assumption is that they are subsisting in His essence, Exalted is He — then the subsistence of the originated in the eternal would be necessitated, which is impossible. And if they were eternal — and the assumption is that they are other than His essence — then there would be necessarily multiple eternals by the multiplicity of attributes additional to the essence; and the statement of multiple eternals is pure disbelief. Allah, Exalted, has stated the disbelief of whoever says that Allah is the third of three; so what would be the case of one who affirms this numerous number of eternals? The Karramiyya went to affirming the attributes, but they claimed that they are originated; they fled from the statement of multiple eternals, but they adhered to the subsistence of the originated in the eternal, which is false; because of what has been established of His self-subsistence, His dissimilarity to originated things, and the impossibility of the subsistence of the originated in the eternal. As for Abu al-Hasan, he considered the matter from all its aspects; so he affirmed the attributes of Allah, Exalted, by the rational and scriptural evidence indicating their establishment, and he affirmed that they are eternal because of the impossibility of originated things subsisting in the essence of Allah, Exalted. Then he said: It does not follow from what we say multiple eternals as the Mu'tazilites claimed; because this would only follow if we said that every one of these attributes is other than the essence in every respect. In other words, the statement of multiple eternals would only bind us if every attribute were self-subsisting. We do not say that every one of these attributes is other than the essence in every respect, nor do we say that every one of them is self-subsisting, although we do say that each attribute is other than the other attributes. We only say that every one of these attributes that we affirm for Allah, Exalted, is other than the essence in terms of conception (al-mafhum); this is indisputable. But every attribute of these attributes is necessarily concomitant with the essence; so the attribute does not separate from it just as the essence does not separate from the attribute. Thus the attribute on this basis is not identical to the essence in every respect, nor is it other than the essence in every respect. This is the meaning of the author's saying: 'They are neither identical to nor other than the essence.' Al-Ash'ari made them not other than the essence to avoid the subsistence of the originated in the eternal or the statement of multiple eternals, and not identical to the essence to flee from what the philosophers and Mu'tazilites went to of negating the attributes. Al-Shams al-Samarqandi said: 'This is a verbal dispute; because the statement that they are not other than the essence is interpreted as the otherness that separates from the essence, even if they are other in conception; and the statement that they are other interprets otherness in the conception, even if they do not separate from the essence.' His speech ends. In this amount, sufficiency. And a summary of what he indicated of the answer: the danger is only the multiplicity of distinct eternals, and we deny the distinctness (taghayyur) of the essence with the attributes and of the attributes with each other; so multiplicity is negated, because it only occurs with distinctness. Thus neither multiplicity nor plurality nor the eternity of another nor the multiplicity of eternals follows. So it is known that the school of Ahl al-Sunna is that the attributes of the essence are additional to it, subsisting in it, necessarily concomitant with it in a concomitance that does not accept separation.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage is a presentation and refutation of the Mu'tazilite objection against the attributes of meaning (sifat al-ma'ani). It also discusses the Karramiyya position and then fully expounds the Ash'ari solution. The author begins by reciting the Mu'tazilite argument: if the attributes are identical to the essence, they would be originated (since the essence is eternal, but identity would imply something originated?), or if they are other than the essence, they would be eternal and thus multiple eternals. The Mu'tazilites use this dilemma to deny attributes altogether. The Karramiyya attempt to avoid multiple eternals by affirming the attributes but claiming they are originated, but this leads to the impossible consequence of originated things subsisting in the eternal. The author then presents Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari's approach: he affirms the attributes as eternal based on rational and scriptural evidence, but denies the objection of multiple eternals by clarifying that the attributes are neither identical to the essence in every respect nor different in a way that implies separation. They are conceptually distinct but existentially inseparable. Al-Ash'ari's formulation avoids both extremes: making attributes identical (which leads to negation of attributes or origination) and making them fully distinct (which leads to multiple eternals). The passage concludes with a summary stating that the true danger is only multiplicity of distinct entities, and since the attributes are not distinct from the essence in a separating sense, no multiplicity follows. The school of Ahl al-Sunna holds that the attributes are additional to the essence, subsisting in it, and necessarily concomitant without possibility of separation.

Key Terms
صفات المعاني
تعدد القدماء
الكرامية
قيام الحادث بالقديم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Mu'tazilites only had one argument; actually they presented a dilemma with two horns.
Correction: The Mu'tazilite objection is a dilemma: if attributes are identical to the essence, they are originated; if they are other, they multiply eternals. Both are deemed impossible.

Checkpoint
What is the second horn of the Mu'tazilite dilemma against attributes?
A) If attributes are identical to the essence, they are originated.
B) If attributes are other than the essence, they are eternal and multiply eternals.
C) If attributes are denied, the essence is unknown.
D) If attributes are affirmed, they must be contingent.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilites used a dilemma to deny attributes, and the Karramiyya's attempted solution (origination) failed because it contradicted divine self-subsistence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Mu'tazilites thought they were protecting tawhid by denying attributes. Are there any beliefs you hold to protect Allah's oneness that actually limit His perfect attributes? Will you seek the correct middle path of the Salaf?
?
The Karramiyya invented a flawed solution to avoid shirk. When you face a theological difficulty, do you rush to a man-made compromise instead of accepting the revelation's apparent meaning with proper tawqif? What will you do to ensure your 'aqeedah is based on the Qur'an and Sunnah alone?
?
The passage calls multiple eternals 'pure disbelief'. Do you truly feel the weight of shirk in theological discussions, or do you treat it as an abstract debate? How will you make your tawhid more heartfelt and practical in your worship starting today?

The Ash'ari Solution: Neither Identical Nor Other
Al-Ash'ari's resolution: attributes are conceptually other but existentially inseparable.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari resolved the Mu'tazilite dilemma by affirming attributes as conceptually other but existentially inseparable.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's middle way: attributes are other in meaning but not separate entities.

Al-Ash'ari carefully examined the issue from all angles. He affirmed the attributes as eternal based on evidence, but he refused to say they are either identical to the essence in every respect or fully other in the sense of being separable. Instead, he introduced a nuanced distinction: the attributes are other than the essence in concept (mafhum) but necessarily concomitant with it, never separate. This avoids both the charge of origination and the charge of multiple eternals. This lesson explains his argument and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Ash'ari's approach
Read the second part of the passage starting from 'فأما أبو الحسن'. Notice how he first affirms the attributes as eternal, then addresses the objection.
He uses both rational and scriptural evidence.
2
Understand the key phrase
Focus on 'ليست بعين أو بغير الذات'. Grasp that the attributes are neither completely identical to the essence nor completely other in a separable way.
This is the core of the Ash'ari position.
3
See the distinction
Al-Ash'ari says the attributes are other than the essence in concept (ghayr bi al-mafhum) but not in a way that allows separation. They are inseparable concomitants (lazimah).
Conceptual otherness does not imply existential independence.
4
Review the summary
Read the concluding summary: the danger is only multiplicity of distinct entities. Since attributes are not distinct in the sense of being separable, no multiplicity follows.
This refutes the Mu'tazilite objection.
