٣٧ - وَغَيْرُ عِلْمٍ هذِهِ كَمَا ثَبَتْ ثُمَّ الحَيَاةُ مَا ثُمَّ الحَيَاةُ مَا بِشَيْ تَعَلَّقَتْ (وَغَيْرُ عِلْمٍ هَذِهِ الصِّفاتُ الأربعُ، وهي: الكلام، والسمع، والبصر، والإدراك، يعني أنَّها مغايرة للعلم في الحقيقة، وكذا بعضها مع بعض كما ثَبَتْ عند القوم بالأدلَّة السَّمعيَّة؛ لأنَّ هذه الصفات إنَّما ثبتت بالسمع، والمدلول لغةً لكلِّ واحدةٍ غيرُ المدلول للأخرى، فوجب حمل ما ورد على ظاهره، حتّى يثبتَ خِلَافهُ، واتّحادُ المُتَعلَّق لا يوجِبُ اتِّحاد الحقيقة، وسكت عَنْ وَحْدَةِ هذه الصفات كالحياة؛ للعلم بها مِن وُجوبها لأخواتها إذ لا فرق. وأما وجوبُ التَعلَّق؛ فهو مُستفاد من صيغة الأمر في قوله: ((أَنِطْ) كما اسْتُفِيدَ عدم تناهي مُتَعَلَّقاتِها مِن أداة العموم الداخلة على «موجود».
37. And distinct from knowledge are these, as established, then life, nothing then life nothing attached to anything. (And distinct from knowledge are these four attributes: speech, hearing, sight, and perception. That is, they are distinct from knowledge in reality, and likewise some of them from others, as established with the people by scriptural proofs. Because these attributes are only established by revelation, and the linguistic denotation of each is other than the linguistic denotation of the others. So it is obligatory to take what is reported on its apparent meaning until the contrary is proven. And the unity of the object of relation does not necessitate unity of reality. And he remained silent about the unity of these attributes like life because it is known from their necessity for their sisters, there being no difference. As for the necessity of relation, it is derived from the imperative form in His saying 'Anit' (make perceive), just as the non-finiteness of their objects of relation is derived from the universal particle applied to 'mawjud' (existent).)
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the verse line regarding the distinction of four attributes—speech, hearing, sight, and perception—from the attribute of knowledge and from each other. It begins by stating that these four attributes are distinct from knowledge in their reality (ḥaqīqa), meaning they have different essences or concepts. The distinction among themselves is also affirmed, based on scriptural evidence (al-adilla al-samʿiyya) because these attributes are known only through revelation, not reason. The commentator then explains that the linguistic meaning of each attribute is different from the others, so they must be taken as distinct unless proof of identity arises. He further notes that the objects of these attributes may coincide (e.g., the same thing is heard and seen) but that does not make the attributes identical. The author did not discuss the unity of these attributes (like the unity of life) because it is obvious that each is necessary for the others in some way. Finally, the necessity of relation (taʿalluq) for these attributes is derived from the imperative form in the verse 'Anit' (make perceive), and the non-finiteness of their objects is derived from the universal particle 'kull' in the earlier statement 'kull mawjud' (every existent).

The Attribute of Life Has No Relation
States that the attribute of life has no relation and is a condition for perception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the attribute of life is classified as non-relational and how it functions as a rational condition for perception without relating to any object.

Core Idea
Life has no object—it is a condition, not a relation.

This passage clarifies a subtle point about the divine attribute of life. Although life is necessary for perception, it does not itself relate to any object or known thing. Understanding why life is non-relational helps distinguish between attributes that have an object and those that are merely conditions.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation to grasp the literal meaning.
Notice the structure: first a direct statement, then an explanation, then a logical rule, and finally a list of similar attributes.
2
Understand the distinction between relational and non-relational attributes
The passage explicitly states that life is not among the relational attributes. Reflect on what makes an attribute relational (having an object) and why life lacks that.
Relational attributes were defined earlier in the text; life does not fit that definition.
3
Grasp the logical condition relationship
Life is a rational condition for perception: its absence necessitates absence of perception, but its presence does not necessitate perception. This is the key to understanding its non-relational nature.
A condition is not a relation—it enables but does not relate to its effect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيانُ أنّ صِفةَ الحياةِ لا تَعلُّقَ لها (ثُمَّ الحَيَاةُ) الأزليَّة (مَا بِشَيْ تَعَلَّقَتْ) أي: لا تتعلَّق بشيء، لا موجود ولا معلوم؛ فليستْ مِن الصِّفات المُتعلّقة المُتقدِّمُ ضابطها، وإِنَّما هي مِن الصفات غير المُتعلّقة؛ لأنَّها صفةٌ مُصححةٌ للإدراك، بمعنى أنَّها شرط عقلي له. يلزم من عدمها عدمه، ولا يلزم من وجودها عدمه ولا وجوده، ومِثلُ الحياة: الوجود، والقدم، والبقاء، عند من يعدُّها من الصفات الذاتية، والله أعلم.
Explanation that the attribute of life has no relation. (Then life) the eternal (nothing attached to anything) i.e., it does not relate to anything, neither existent nor known. So it is not among the relational attributes whose definition preceded. Rather, it is among the non-relational attributes because it is an attribute that qualifies (makes sound) perception, meaning that it is a rational condition for it. From its absence, its absence is necessary; and from its existence, neither its absence nor its existence is necessary. And similar to life are existence, pre-eternity, and everlastingness, according to those who count them among the essential attributes. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the phrase 'Then life nothing attached to anything.' It clarifies that the attribute of life (al-ḥayāh) is not a relational attribute (ṣifa mutaʿalliqa); it does not relate to any object, neither an existent nor something known. Earlier, a definition of relational attributes was given, and life does not fit that. Instead, life is a non-relational attribute (ṣifa ghayr mutaʿalliqa) because its function is to enable perception (idrāk) by being a rational condition (sharṭ ʿaqlī) for it. The logical relationship is that perception depends on life: if life is absent, perception is absent, but the presence of life does not necessitate the presence or absence of perception (since perception requires additional causes). The commentator then notes that other essential attributes like existence (wujūd), pre-eternity (qidam), and everlastingness (baqāʾ) are also non-relational according to those who list them among essential attributes. The passage ends with 'Allah knows best.'

القدم
البقاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Life must relate to perception because it enables it.
Correction: Life is a rational condition for perception, not a relation; it has no object.

Checkpoint
Why is the attribute of life considered non-relational according to the passage?
A) Because it does not have an object of relation
B) Because it is eternal
C) Because it is a condition for perception
D) Because it is essential

Key Takeaway
The attribute of life is non-relational: it has no object and serves only as a rational condition for perception.

If life from Allah is unconditioned—not a relation that depends on you—then your existence is purely from Him. What would it mean for you to live today as if your very being is a gift that requires no reciprocity? Could you live one hour without demanding anything from Allah?

Eternity of Allah's Names and Attributes
Affirms the eternity of Allah's names and essential attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni doctrine that Allah's names and essential attributes are eternal, not created.

Core Idea
Allah's names and attributes are eternal with Him.

This lesson affirms a central tenet of Ahl al-Sunnah: the eternity of Allah's names and essential attributes. The verse line states this clearly, and the commentary unpacks the grammar to reinforce the meaning. Understanding this helps distinguish Sunni creed from those who attribute temporality to Divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse line
Read the Arabic verse line and its translation carefully. Notice the key terms: 'His mighty names' and 'attributes of His essence'.
The verse is a concise doctrinal statement.
2
Identify the main claim
The claim is that both the names and the attributes of essence are 'qadīma' (eternal). This means they have no beginning and are not created.
3
Understand the grammatical analysis
The commentary explains that 'His names' is the subject, 'the mighty' is an adjective, and 'eternal' is the predicate. This structure emphasises the predicate's importance.
Grammatical analysis in kalam texts often highlights key doctrinal points.
4
Reflect on the significance
Why does this matter? If Allah's names were created, they would not be eternal and would imply change in Allah. Sunni creed avoids this by affirming their eternity.
This connects to the broader topic of divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۸ - وَعِنْدَنَا أَسْمَاؤُهُ العَظِيمَة كَذَا صِفَاتُ ذاتِهِ قَدِيمَهُ (وَعِنْدَنَا) أهلَ الحقِّ (أَسْمَاؤُهُ العَظِيمَة) أي: الجَليلة المُقدَّسة، (قديمة) خبر المبتدأ. قول المصنف (أسماؤه) مبتدأ و (العظيمه) صفةٌ له، وقوله فيما يلي (قديمة) خبر المبتدأ.

Commentary
This passage is a statement affirming the eternity of Allah's names and essential attributes from the perspective of Ahl al-Ḥaqq (the people of truth, i.e., Ahl al-Sunnah). It begins with the verse line: 'And with us His mighty names, likewise the attributes of His essence, are eternal.' The commentator explains that 'with us' refers to the people of truth, and 'His mighty names' means the magnificent and sacred names. He then provides grammatical analysis: 'His names' is the subject (mubtadaʾ), 'the mighty' is an adjective, and 'eternal' (qadīma) is the predicate (khabar). This reinforces the doctrine that both the names and the essential attributes (ṣifāt dhātihi) are eternal (qadīma), not created, in line with Sunni creed.

Why Life is Not an Attached Attribute
Explains why the attribute of life is not among the attached attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the attribute of life is not considered an attached attribute in Islamic theology and how it functions as a rational condition for perception.

Core Idea
Life is not attached to anything; it is a rational precondition for perception.

In this passage, the author explains a key distinction in divine attributes: some attributes 'attach' to their objects (like will and power), but life does not. Instead, life is a necessary condition for perception. This lesson unpacks that distinction and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the clear assertion that life 'has not attached to anything'.
The passage uses technical terms like 'attached attributes' and 'rational condition'.
2
Identify the key claim
The passage states that life is not among the attached attributes. Attached attributes have a defined rule (ضابط) which life does not follow.
3
Understand the rational condition
Life is described as a 'rational condition' (شرط عقلي) for perception. This means perception logically requires life, but life does not guarantee perception.
The logical relationship: absence of life necessitates absence of perception; presence of life does not necessitate either absence or presence of perception.
4
Note the examples given
The author mentions that existence, pre-eternity, and permanence are similar to life in this regard, according to some scholars who count them as essential attributes.
This shows the broader category of non-attached essential attributes.
5
Reinforce with the misconception
Consider the common misunderstanding: one might think life is attached like will or power. The passage clarifies that life is not attached; it is a precondition.
The checkpoint question will test this understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان أن صفة الحياة لا تعلق لها
بيانُ أنّ صِفةَ الحياةِ لا تَعلُّقَ لها ]
(ثُمَّ الحَيَاةُ) الأزليَّة (۱) (مَا بِشَيْ تَعَلَّقَتْ) أي: لا تتعلَّق بشيء، لا موجود ولا معلوم ; فليستْ مِن الصِّفات المُتعلّقة المُتقدِّمُ ضابطها(۲) ، وإِنَّما هي مِن ; فـ الغير المُتعلّقة ; لأنَّها صفةٌ مُصححةٌ للإدراك ، بمعنى أنَّها شرط عقلي له (۳) . له(۳) ، يلزم من عدمها عدمه، ولا يلزم من وجودها عدمه ولا وجوده (٤) ، ومِثلُ الحياة: الوجود، والقدم، والبقاء، عند من يعدُّها من الصفات الذاتية ، والله أعلم.
Statement that the attribute of life has no attachment: Statement that the attribute of life has no attachment. (Then life) the eternal (1) (has not attached to anything) meaning: it does not attach to anything, neither an existent nor a known; so it is not among the attached attributes whose rule has preceded (2). Rather, it is among the non-attached; because it is a attribute that corrects perception, in the sense that it is a rational condition for it (3). For it (3), its absence necessitates its absence, and its presence does not necessitate its absence nor its existence (4). And similar to life are: existence, pre-eternity, and permanence, according to those who count them among the essential attributes. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage defines the attribute of life (الحياة) and explains its nature in relation to attachment. It begins by stating that life does not attach to anything, whether existent or known. It then clarifies that life is not among the attached attributes (الصفات المتعلقة), which have a defined rule (ضابط). Instead, it is a non-attached attribute because it is a qualifying attribute for perception (مصححة للإدراك), meaning it is a rational condition (شرط عقلي) for perception: if life is absent, perception is absent; but from the presence of life, neither the absence nor the presence of perception necessarily follows. This logical relationship shows that life is a necessary precondition but not a direct cause. Finally, it notes that other attributes like existence (الوجود), pre-eternity (القدم), and permanence (البقاء) follow the same pattern for those who count them as essential attributes.

Correction: Life is not attached; it is a rational condition for perception, not an attachment to an external object.

Key Takeaway
Life is a non-attached, essential attribute that serves as a rational precondition for perception, distinct from attributes that directly attach to objects.

Pre-Eternity of Allah's Names and Attributes: The Rhetorical Proof
Grammatical analysis of the verse affirming pre-eternity using al-ih'tibak.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the rhetorical device of al-ih'tibak (interweaving) in the poem demonstrates the pre-eternity of both Allah's names and His essential attributes.

Core Idea
The grammar of the poem itself proves that Allah's names and attributes are equally pre-eternal.

In this lesson, we examine the opening verse of the poem and its grammatical analysis by the commentator. The poet states that Allah's names and essential attributes are pre-eternal, but the grammatical construction uses a subtle rhetorical device called al-ih'tibak. By unpacking the grammar, we see that both names and attributes are affirmed as pre-eternal through an elegant omission and interweaving. This linguistic precision reinforces the theological truth that Allah's names and attributes are not created.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and its translation
Start by reading the Arabic verse 'وَعِنْدَنَا أَسماؤُهُ العَظِيمَة كَذَا صِفَاتُ ذاتِهِ قَدِيمَهُ' and its literal translation.
2
Study the first grammatical analysis
The commentator gives two possible grammatical analyses. The first treats 'كذا' as a predicate and 'صفات' as a subject. Understand how this shows the attributes are likened to the names in pre-eternity.
3
Study the second analysis and al-ih'tibak
The second analysis reveals an omitted subject and predicate, using a figure of speech called al-ih'tibak. Notice how each sentence supplies the missing part of the other.
This is a key rhetorical device that emphasizes the simultaneous pre-eternity of names and attributes.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why the poet and commentator used such an intricate grammatical structure. It underscores the theological point that Allah's names and attributes are equally eternal and not created.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيانُ قِدم أسمائه تَعالى وصفاته الذَّاتية عند أهل السُّنَّة]
۳۸ - وَعِنْدَنَا أَسماؤُهُ العَظِيمَة كَذَا صِفَاتُ ذاتِهِ قَدِيمَهُ
(وَعِنْدَنَا) أهلَ الحقِّ (أَسْمَاؤُهُ العَظِيمَة ) (٥) أي: الجَليلة المُقدَّسة،
قوله: (كذا) جار ومجرور يتعلق بمحذوف خبر مقدم ، وقوله: (صفات) مبتدأ مؤخَّر ، وجملة هذا المبتدأ وخبره اعتراضية بين المبتدأ السَّابق وخبره ، والمراد تشبيه الصفات بالأسماء في القدم، وكلام الشارح له يشير إلى إعراب آخر غير الذي ذكرناه، وحاصله: أنَّ المبتدأ المتقدَّم وهو «أسماؤه» محذوف ، يدلُّ عليه خبر المبتدأ المتأخّر، وهو (صفات) وقوله: (قديمة) خبرٌ عن (صفات) وللمبتدأ المتأخّر صفة محذوفة تدلُّ عليها صفة المبتدأ المتقدم، وكأنَّه قال: وأسماؤه العظيمة قديمةٌ عندنا معشر أهل السُّنَّة ، كذا صفاته العظيمة قديمة، فقد حذف من كلِّ جملة مثل ما أثبته في الجملة الأخرى ، وهذا نوع من البديع يسمى الاحتباك .
ومعنى العظيمة الجليلة المقدَّسة، أي: المطهرة عن أنْ يُسمّى بها غيره، أو المطهرة عن أنْ تُفسَّرَ بما لا يليق، أو المطهرة عن أنْ تُذكَر على غير وجه التَّعظيم، وتعظيم أسمائه تعالى بأحد هذه المعاني مُجمَعٌ عليه ، والمراد : أنَّ كلَّ أسمائه تعالى وكل صفاته السَّبعة أو الثّمانية على الخلاف السابق - قديمةٌ ، فليست أسماؤه تعالى من وضع خَلْقه له، وليست صفاته حادثة له ؛ لأنَّها لو كانت حادثة له لزم قيام الحوادث بذاته تعالى ، ولزم أيضا أن يكون له عارياً عنها في الأزل ، ولزم أيضًا افتقارها إلى من يصفه أو يسميه بها، وهو ينافي وجوب الغنى المطلق، وهو انتفاء الحاجات مطلقا، وهذا الغنى المطلق ليس ثابتا إلَّا الله تعالى، بخلاف الغني المقيّد المُفسَّر بقلة الحاجات، فإنَّه ثابت للمخلوقات، وخرج بقول المصنف صفات ذاته صفات الأفعال، فإنّ فيها خلافًا ، فالأشاعرة على أنه ليس شيء من صفات بقديم ، والماتريدية على أن صفات الأفعال قديمة كصفات المعاني، وإنما كانت صفات الأفعال حادثة عند الأشاعرة ؛ لأنَّها عند التحقيق عندهم تعلقات القدرة التنجيزية الحادثة، وكانت قديمة عند الماتريديَّة ؛ لأنَّها عندهم عين صفة التكوين القديمة، وأما الصفات السَّلبيَّة كالقِدم فهي قديمة أو أزليَّة إن قلنا بالفرق بين القديم والأزلي كما سبق لنا تقريره ، وعلى هذا يحتاج قول الشارح: وخرج بإضافة الصفة إلى الذات السلبيَّة» إلى البيان، فإما أن يكون الشارح دَرَجَ على القول بالفرق بين القديم والأزلي ، فنفى قدم الصفات السلبية وهو يذهب إلى أزليَّتها ، وإما أن يكون ذكرها في هذا الموضع سَبْقَ كما قال العلامة الأمير.
Statement of the pre-eternity of His names - exalted is He - and His essential attributes according to the People of the Sunnah: 38 - And upon us His magnificent names, likewise the attributes of His essence, are pre-eternal. (And upon us) the People of Truth (His magnificent names) (5) meaning: the glorious, the sacred. His saying: (likewise) is a prepositional phrase attached to an omitted predicate that precedes, and His saying: (attributes) is a delayed subject, and the sentence of this subject and its predicate is parenthetical between the previous subject and its predicate, and the intent is to liken the attributes to the names in pre-eternity. And the words of the commentator about it point to another grammatical analysis different from what we have mentioned. Its summary: that the preceding subject which is 'His names' is omitted, indicated by the predicate of the delayed subject which is (attributes), and His saying: (pre-eternal) is a predicate of (attributes), and for the delayed subject there is an omitted attribute indicated by the attribute of the preceding subject, as if He said: And His magnificent names are pre-eternal with us, the community of the People of the Sunnah, likewise His magnificent attributes are pre-eternal. So from each sentence, what is affirmed in the other sentence has been omitted, and this is a type of badi' called al-ih'tibak (the interweaving). And the meaning of al-azimah (magnificent) is al-jalilah (glorious) al-muqaddasah (sacred), that is, purified from anyone else being named with them, or purified from being interpreted in a way that is not befitting, or purified from being mentioned in a manner not of veneration. And venerating His names - exalted is He - with any of these meanings is agreed upon. And the intent: that all His names - exalted is He - and all His attributes - the seven or eight according to the previous difference - are pre-eternal. So His names - exalted is He - are not from the invention of His creation for Him, and His attributes are not occurrences for Him; because if they were occurrences for Him, it would necessitate the occurrence of contingencies in His essence - exalted is He - and would also necessitate that He be devoid of them in pre-eternity, and would also necessitate their need for someone who describes Him or names Him with them, and that contradicts the obligation of absolute self-sufficiency (al-ghina al-mutlaq), which is the negation of all needs. And this absolute self-sufficiency is not established except for Allah - exalted is He - in contrast to restricted self-sufficiency, interpreted as few needs, for that is established for creatures. And by the author's statement 'the attributes of His essence', attributes of action (sifat al-af'al) are excluded, for there is disagreement concerning them. The Ash'aris hold that none of the attributes of action are pre-eternal, while the Maturidis hold that the attributes of action are pre-eternal like the attributes of meanings. And the attributes of action were regarded as contingent by the Ash'aris because, upon investigation according to them, they are the determinate attachments of the newly occurring power; and they were regarded as pre-eternal by the Maturidis because, according to them, they are the very attribute of origination (sifat al-takwin) which is pre-eternal. As for the negative attributes (al-sifat al-salbıyya) like pre-eternity, they are either pre-eternal (qadim) or eternal (azali) if we say there is a difference between the pre-eternal and the eternal as we have previously established. And upon this, the statement of the commentator: 'And by adding the attribute to the essence, the negative attributes are excluded' requires explanation. Either the commentator followed the view of the difference between the pre-eternal and the eternal, thus denying the pre-eternity of the negative attributes while holding them to be eternal; or he mentioned them in this place as a slip of the tongue, as said by the distinguished scholar al-Amir.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage proves the pre-eternity of Allah's names and essential attributes. It begins by citing the poetic verse and then provides a grammatical analysis, showing a form of rhetorical eloquence called al-ih'tibak (الاحتباك). The meaning of 'magnificent' is then explained as 'glorious' and 'sacred', signifying that these names are not to be used for other beings, interpreted improperly, or mentioned without veneration. The core theological argument follows: all names and attributes (seven or eight according to earlier discussion) are pre-eternal. The passage refutes the notion that attributes are created by listing three necessary implications if they were contingent: (1) contingencies would subsist in Allah's essence, (2) He would have been devoid of them in pre-eternity, and (3) they would depend on a creator or namer, contradicting absolute self-sufficiency (الغنى المطلق). The passage then distinguishes between attributes of essence (صفات الذات) and attributes of action (صفات الأفعال), noting the Ash'ari view (attributes of action are contingent) and the Maturidi view (they are pre-eternal as the attribute of origination). Finally, it addresses negative attributes (الصفات السلبية), clarifying that they are either pre-eternal or eternal depending on terminology, and resolves an apparent inconsistency in the commentator's statement.

Key Terms
أسماء الله
صفات الذات
قديم
احتباك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that only Allah's names are pre-eternal, while His attributes are created or contingent.
Correction: The grammatical analysis shows that both names and attributes are affirmed as pre-eternal through the figure of al-ih'tibak, emphasizing their equal eternity.

Checkpoint
What rhetorical device is used in the grammatical analysis to show the pre-eternity of both names and attributes?

B) Al-Ih'tibak
C) Taqdim wa Ta'khir
D) Ijmal wa Tafsil

Key Takeaway
The rhetorical device of al-ih'tibak demonstrates that Allah's names and essential attributes are equally pre-eternal, linguistically reinforcing the theological principle.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The grammatical device of al-ih'tibak shows that Allah's names and attributes are equally pre-eternal—neither is more fundamental. Is there any attribute of Allah that you subconsciously treat as less important or less eternal? What will you do to correct that imbalance in your heart?
?
The poet and commentator used intricate linguistic analysis to affirm a single theological truth. When was the last time you devoted such careful attention to understanding one of Allah's names or attributes? Will you commit to studying one name or attribute in depth this week?
?
Knowing that every name and attribute of Allah is equally pre-eternal and perfect, how does this change the way you call upon Him by His names? Which name have you neglected, and how will you begin to invoke it with full reverence?

Divine Attributes

The Proof from Absolute Self-Sufficiency for the Pre-Eternity of Attributes
Theological proof for pre-eternity using the concept of absolute self-sufficiency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical argument that if Allah's attributes were created, it would contradict His absolute self-sufficiency (al-ghina al-mutlaq), thereby proving their pre-eternity.

Core Idea
If Allah's attributes were created, He would depend on something else, negating His absolute self-sufficiency.

This lesson presents the core theological argument for the pre-eternity of Allah's attributes. The passage first explains the meaning of 'magnificent' names and then lays out three logical consequences if the attributes were created. The third consequence is particularly powerful: created attributes would need a creator or namer, which contradicts Allah's absolute self-sufficiency. This argument establishes that the attributes must be pre-eternal, just as He is.

Guided Path
1
Read the explanation of 'magnificent'
The passage explains that 'magnificent' means glorious and sacred, purified from being used for others, interpreted incorrectly, or mentioned without veneration.
This sets the context that Allah's names are unique and holy.
2
Identify the three implications of created attributes
Look for the three consequences that would follow if attributes were created: (1) contingencies would subsist in Allah, (2) He would be devoid of them in pre-eternity, (3) they would need someone to describe or name Him, contradicting self-sufficiency.
These are listed with 'لزم' (necessitate).
3
Understand absolute vs restricted self-sufficiency
The passage distinguishes between absolute self-sufficiency (negation of all needs) and restricted self-sufficiency (few needs). Absolute self-sufficiency belongs only to Allah, and any dependence would negate it.
This distinction is crucial for the argument.
4
Reflect on the proof
Consider how the argument moves from the possibility of created attributes to a contradiction, proving that attributes cannot be created and must be pre-eternal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيانُ قِدم أسمائه تَعالى وصفاته الذَّاتية عند أهل السُّنَّة]
۳۸ - وَعِنْدَنَا أَسماؤُهُ العَظِيمَة كَذَا صِفَاتُ ذاتِهِ قَدِيمَهُ
(وَعِنْدَنَا) أهلَ الحقِّ (أَسْمَاؤُهُ العَظِيمَة ) (٥) أي: الجَليلة المُقدَّسة،
قوله: (كذا) جار ومجرور يتعلق بمحذوف خبر مقدم ، وقوله: (صفات) مبتدأ مؤخَّر ، وجملة هذا المبتدأ وخبره اعتراضية بين المبتدأ السَّابق وخبره ، والمراد تشبيه الصفات بالأسماء في القدم، وكلام الشارح له يشير إلى إعراب آخر غير الذي ذكرناه، وحاصله: أنَّ المبتدأ المتقدَّم وهو «أسماؤه» محذوف ، يدلُّ عليه خبر المبتدأ المتأخّر، وهو (صفات) وقوله: (قديمة) خبرٌ عن (صفات) وللمبتدأ المتأخّر صفة محذوفة تدلُّ عليها صفة المبتدأ المتقدم، وكأنَّه قال: وأسماؤه العظيمة قديمةٌ عندنا معشر أهل السُّنَّة ، كذا صفاته العظيمة قديمة، فقد حذف من كلِّ جملة مثل ما أثبته في الجملة الأخرى ، وهذا نوع من البديع يسمى الاحتباك .
ومعنى العظيمة الجليلة المقدَّسة، أي: المطهرة عن أنْ يُسمّى بها غيره، أو المطهرة عن أنْ تُفسَّرَ بما لا يليق، أو المطهرة عن أنْ تُذكَر على غير وجه التَّعظيم، وتعظيم أسمائه تعالى بأحد هذه المعاني مُجمَعٌ عليه ، والمراد : أنَّ كلَّ أسمائه تعالى وكل صفاته السَّبعة أو الثّمانية على الخلاف السابق - قديمةٌ ، فليست أسماؤه تعالى من وضع خَلْقه له، وليست صفاته حادثة له ؛ لأنَّها لو كانت حادثة له لزم قيام الحوادث بذاته تعالى ، ولزم أيضا أن يكون له عارياً عنها في الأزل ، ولزم أيضًا افتقارها إلى من يصفه أو يسميه بها، وهو ينافي وجوب الغنى المطلق، وهو انتفاء الحاجات مطلقا، وهذا الغنى المطلق ليس ثابتا إلَّا الله تعالى، بخلاف الغني المقيّد المُفسَّر بقلة الحاجات، فإنَّه ثابت للمخلوقات، وخرج بقول المصنف صفات ذاته صفات الأفعال، فإنّ فيها خلافًا ، فالأشاعرة على أنه ليس شيء من صفات بقديم ، والماتريدية على أن صفات الأفعال قديمة كصفات المعاني، وإنما كانت صفات الأفعال حادثة عند الأشاعرة ؛ لأنَّها عند التحقيق عندهم تعلقات القدرة التنجيزية الحادثة، وكانت قديمة عند الماتريديَّة ؛ لأنَّها عندهم عين صفة التكوين القديمة، وأما الصفات السَّلبيَّة كالقِدم فهي قديمة أو أزليَّة إن قلنا بالفرق بين القديم والأزلي كما سبق لنا تقريره ، وعلى هذا يحتاج قول الشارح: وخرج بإضافة الصفة إلى الذات السلبيَّة» إلى البيان، فإما أن يكون الشارح دَرَجَ على القول بالفرق بين القديم والأزلي ، فنفى قدم الصفات السلبية وهو يذهب إلى أزليَّتها ، وإما أن يكون ذكرها في هذا الموضع سَبْقَ كما قال العلامة الأمير.
Statement of the pre-eternity of His names - exalted is He - and His essential attributes according to the People of the Sunnah: 38 - And upon us His magnificent names, likewise the attributes of His essence, are pre-eternal. (And upon us) the People of Truth (His magnificent names) (5) meaning: the glorious, the sacred. His saying: (likewise) is a prepositional phrase attached to an omitted predicate that precedes, and His saying: (attributes) is a delayed subject, and the sentence of this subject and its predicate is parenthetical between the previous subject and its predicate, and the intent is to liken the attributes to the names in pre-eternity. And the words of the commentator about it point to another grammatical analysis different from what we have mentioned. Its summary: that the preceding subject which is 'His names' is omitted, indicated by the predicate of the delayed subject which is (attributes), and His saying: (pre-eternal) is a predicate of (attributes), and for the delayed subject there is an omitted attribute indicated by the attribute of the preceding subject, as if He said: And His magnificent names are pre-eternal with us, the community of the People of the Sunnah, likewise His magnificent attributes are pre-eternal. So from each sentence, what is affirmed in the other sentence has been omitted, and this is a type of badi' called al-ih'tibak (the interweaving). And the meaning of al-azimah (magnificent) is al-jalilah (glorious) al-muqaddasah (sacred), that is, purified from anyone else being named with them, or purified from being interpreted in a way that is not befitting, or purified from being mentioned in a manner not of veneration. And venerating His names - exalted is He - with any of these meanings is agreed upon. And the intent: that all His names - exalted is He - and all His attributes - the seven or eight according to the previous difference - are pre-eternal. So His names - exalted is He - are not from the invention of His creation for Him, and His attributes are not occurrences for Him; because if they were occurrences for Him, it would necessitate the occurrence of contingencies in His essence - exalted is He - and would also necessitate that He be devoid of them in pre-eternity, and would also necessitate their need for someone who describes Him or names Him with them, and that contradicts the obligation of absolute self-sufficiency (al-ghina al-mutlaq), which is the negation of all needs. And this absolute self-sufficiency is not established except for Allah - exalted is He - in contrast to restricted self-sufficiency, interpreted as few needs, for that is established for creatures. And by the author's statement 'the attributes of His essence', attributes of action (sifat al-af'al) are excluded, for there is disagreement concerning them. The Ash'aris hold that none of the attributes of action are pre-eternal, while the Maturidis hold that the attributes of action are pre-eternal like the attributes of meanings. And the attributes of action were regarded as contingent by the Ash'aris because, upon investigation according to them, they are the determinate attachments of the newly occurring power; and they were regarded as pre-eternal by the Maturidis because, according to them, they are the very attribute of origination (sifat al-takwin) which is pre-eternal. As for the negative attributes (al-sifat al-salbıyya) like pre-eternity, they are either pre-eternal (qadim) or eternal (azali) if we say there is a difference between the pre-eternal and the eternal as we have previously established. And upon this, the statement of the commentator: 'And by adding the attribute to the essence, the negative attributes are excluded' requires explanation. Either the commentator followed the view of the difference between the pre-eternal and the eternal, thus denying the pre-eternity of the negative attributes while holding them to be eternal; or he mentioned them in this place as a slip of the tongue, as said by the distinguished scholar al-Amir.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage proves the pre-eternity of Allah's names and essential attributes. It begins by citing the poetic verse and then provides a grammatical analysis, showing a form of rhetorical eloquence called al-ih'tibak (الاحتباك). The meaning of 'magnificent' is then explained as 'glorious' and 'sacred', signifying that these names are not to be used for other beings, interpreted improperly, or mentioned without veneration. The core theological argument follows: all names and attributes (seven or eight according to earlier discussion) are pre-eternal. The passage refutes the notion that attributes are created by listing three necessary implications if they were contingent: (1) contingencies would subsist in Allah's essence, (2) He would have been devoid of them in pre-eternity, and (3) they would depend on a creator or namer, contradicting absolute self-sufficiency (الغنى المطلق). The passage then distinguishes between attributes of essence (صفات الذات) and attributes of action (صفات الأفعال), noting the Ash'ari view (attributes of action are contingent) and the Maturidi view (they are pre-eternal as the attribute of origination). Finally, it addresses negative attributes (الصفات السلبية), clarifying that they are either pre-eternal or eternal depending on terminology, and resolves an apparent inconsistency in the commentator's statement.

Key Terms
الغنى المطلق
صفات الذات
قديم
استغناء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if attributes are pre-eternal, then they are separate entities alongside Allah.
Correction: The passage does not claim that attributes are separate entities; rather, they are inherent to His essence and not created.

Checkpoint
What is the third implication that directly contradicts absolute self-sufficiency?
A) Contingencies would inhere in Allah's essence.
B) Allah would be devoid of attributes in pre-eternity.
C) The attributes would need someone to describe or name Allah with them.
D) The attributes would be multiple.

Key Takeaway
The logical impossibility of created attributes due to their contradiction of Allah's absolute self-sufficiency proves that they must be pre-eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that Allah's absolute self-sufficiency means He has no need whatsoever—not even for your description of Him—does your worship become about satisfying a need in yourself, or do you truly worship Him because He alone is worthy? How can you shift your intention today to reflect that reality?
?
The passage states that venerating Allah's names is a consensus. But does your veneration extend beyond your lips to your choices? Which name of Allah, if you truly revered it as eternal and uncreated, would change a decision you are facing right now?
?
If Allah's attributes were created, He would depend on something else. In your own life, where have you made your understanding of God dependent on your experiences or culture? What would it mean to submit to the pre-eternal attributes as described in this lesson, even if they challenge your assumptions?

Divine Attributes

Essential vs. Action Attributes and the Sectarian Differences
Distinction between essential and action attributes with sectarian differences and discussion of negative attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between attributes of essence (sifat al-dhat) and attributes of action (sifat al-af'al), and the Ash'ari vs Maturidi positions on their pre-eternity, as well as the status of negative attributes.

Core Idea
Only attributes of essence are pre-eternal by consensus; attributes of action are disputed between Ash'aris (contingent) and Maturidis (pre-eternal).

This lesson addresses the classification of divine attributes. The previous lessons established the pre-eternity of Allah's names and essential attributes. Now, the passage clarifies that attributes of action (e.g., creating, providing) are excluded from this pre-eternity according to the Ash'aris, but the Maturidis hold them pre-eternal as the attribute of origination. Additionally, negative attributes (e.g., pre-eternity itself) are described as either pre-eternal or eternal depending on terminology. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for navigating the scholarly differences within Sunni theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exclusion of action attributes
The passage states that by adding 'of His essence', action attributes (sifat al-af'al) are excluded. Learn what these are.
Examples: creation, provision, etc.
2
Understand the Ash'ari view
Ash'aris say none of the action attributes are pre-eternal because they are, upon analysis, determinate attachments of the newly occurring power (qudra).
They consider them contingent.
3
Understand the Maturidi view
Maturidis say action attributes are pre-eternal because they are the very attribute of origination (sifat al-takwin), which is pre-eternal.
This is a key point of difference.
4
Examine negative attributes
Negative attributes like 'pre-eternity' (qidam) are either called pre-eternal or eternal depending on terminology. The commentator's statement is reconciled.
The discussion involves the difference between qadim and azali.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The commentator might have made a slip of the tongue in his explanation. Have you ever been too quick to judge a scholar's mistake, forgetting that your own understanding might be limited? How can you cultivate humility when studying 'aqeedah?
?
If you were asked to explain the difference between qadīm and azalī to someone new to Islamic theology, would you be confident? This lesson highlights that terminology matters in protecting correct belief. What steps will you take to ensure you are precise in your own speech about Allah?

Pre-Eternity of Allah's Names and Attributes
Sanusi proves the pre-eternity of Allah's names and attributes with logical arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof for the pre-eternity of Allah's names and attributes and why they cannot be originated (ḥādithah).

Core Idea
Allah's names and attributes are pre-eternal — they are not created or acquired.

Sanusi turns to a critical theological claim: Allah's names and attributes are pre-eternal. Using logical reasoning, he shows that if they were originated, it would lead to impossible consequences. This lesson unpacks that argument and clarifies why absolute self-sufficiency demands pre-eternity.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without overanalyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the flow.
Pay attention to the opening definition of 'al-ʿaẓīmah' — it sets the tone.
2
Identify the three consequences
The passage lists three 'lāzims' (necessary consequences) that would follow if attributes were originated. Find each one and note how they each lead to an impossibility.
Each consequence is introduced by 'لزم'.
3
Connect to absolute self-sufficiency
Understand why the third consequence contradicts absolute self-sufficiency (al-ghinā al-muṭlaq). Reflect on why this contradiction proves pre-eternity.
Absolute self-sufficiency is unique to Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومعنى العظيمة الجليلة المقدسة، أي: المطهرة عن أنْ يُسمّى بها غيره، أو المطهرة عن أنْ تُفسَّرَ بما لا يليق، أو المطهرة عن أنْ تُذكَر على غير وجه التَّعظيم، وتعظيم أسمائه تعالى بأحد هذه المعاني مُجمَعٌ عليه. والمراد : أنَّ كلَّ أسمائه تعالى وكل صفاته السَّبعة أو الثّمانية على الخلاف السابق - قديمةٌ، فليست أسماؤه تعالى من وضع خَلْقه له، وليست صفاته حادثة له؛ لأنَّها لو كانت حادثة له لزم قيام الحوادث بذاته تعالى، ولزم أيضا أن يكون له عارياً عنها في الأزل، ولزم أيضًا افتقارها إلى من يصفه أو يسميه بها، وهو ينافي وجوب الغنى المطلق، وهو انتفاء الحاجات مطلقا، وهذا الغنى المطلق ليس ثابتا إلَّا الله تعالى، بخلاف الغني المقيّد المُفسَّر بقلة الحاجات، فإنَّه ثابت للمخلوقات.
And the meaning of 'the great' is the majestic, the sanctified, i.e., purified from being named with it other than Him, or purified from being interpreted in a way that is not fitting, or purified from being mentioned without reverence. And magnifying His names, may He be exalted, according to any of these meanings is agreed upon. And the intended meaning: that all His names, may He be exalted, and all His seven or eight attributes according to the previous disagreement — are pre-eternal. So His names, may He be exalted, are not from the invention of His creation for Him, and His attributes are not originated for Him; because if they were originated for Him, it would necessitate the occurrence of originated accidents in His essence, may He be exalted, and it would also necessitate that He be devoid of them in pre-eternity, and it would also necessitate their need for one who describes Him or names Him by them. And this contradicts the necessity of absolute self-sufficiency, which is the negation of needs absolutely. And this absolute self-sufficiency is not affirmed except for Allah, may He be exalted, unlike restricted self-sufficiency interpreted as fewness of needs, for it is affirmed for created beings.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the pre-eternity (qidam) of Allah's names and attributes. First, Sanusi explains the meaning of 'al-ʿaẓīmah' (the great) applied to the names: it means they are sanctified and purified from being used for other than Him, from being interpreted unfittingly, or from being mentioned without reverence. Then he states the central claim: all of Allah's names and all of His seven or eight attributes (the number is disputed) are pre-eternal (qadīmah). They are not inventions of human beings, and they are not originated (ḥādithah) in God. He then provides three logical consequences that would follow if they were originated: (1) it would necessitate the occurrence of temporal accidents (ḥawādith) in God's essence, which is impossible for the Necessary Being; (2) it would necessitate that God was devoid of them in pre-eternity, implying that He acquired them later; (3) it would necessitate that they depend on someone to describe or name Him, contradicting absolute self-sufficiency (al-ghinā al-muṭlaq). Only Allah possesses absolute self-sufficiency; created beings only have restricted self-sufficiency (fewness of needs). Thus, the names and attributes must be pre-eternal.

Key Terms
قدم
صفات الذات
أسماء الله
الغني المطلق
حادثة
الحوادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The pre-eternity of attributes means they are independent entities apart from God.
Correction: Pre-eternity here means they are not temporally originated in His essence; they are not separate but are intrinsic to His nature.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a necessary consequence if Allah's attributes were originated (ḥādithah)?
A) They would be temporal accidents occurring in His essence
B) They would be created by angels
C) They would be similar to human attributes
D) They would be self-sufficient

Key Takeaway
Allah's names and attributes are pre-eternal because their origination would necessitate impossibilities that contradict His absolute self-sufficiency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you call upon Allah by a name like Ar-Rahman, do you truly believe that this attribute has been with Him eternally, existing before creation? How does this belief affect your reliance on Him today?
?
The passage says that if attributes were originated, God would have been devoid of them in pre-eternity. Reflect on a time you felt incomplete without something—a role, a skill, a possession. How does God's absolute self-sufficiency challenge your tendency to define yourself by what you acquire?
?
If Allah's names and attributes are not inventions of creation, then your understanding of them comes from divine revelation. Where have you relied on your own reasoning or cultural assumptions about God rather than submitting to His own description of Himself?

The Ash'ari-Maturidi Dispute on Attributes of Actions
Sanusi describes the Ash'ari-Maturidi disagreement on attributes of actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the difference between Ash'ari and Maturidi views on the pre-eternity of attributes of actions, and why this distinction matters in Islamic theology.

Core Idea
Attributes of actions are either pre-eternal or originated, depending on your school.

Sanusi now draws an important distinction: not all divine attributes are the same. The attributes of actions (ṣifāt al-afʿāl) provoke a deep disagreement between the Ashʿarī and Māturīdī schools. This passage explains the two positions and their theological bases.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on attributes of actions
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Sanusi uses a very compressed style here.
2
Identify the Ash'ari position and its reasoning
The passage states that Ash'aris hold attributes of actions are not pre-eternal. Find the reason given: they are actualized relations of power which are originated.
3
Identify the Maturidi position and its reasoning
Maturidis hold they are pre-eternal. Find the reason: they are identical with the attribute of bringing into existence (takwīn) which is pre-eternal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخرج بقول المصنف صفات ذاته صفات الأفعال، فإنّ فيها خلافًا، فالأشاعرة على أنه ليس شيء من صفات بقديم، والماتريدية على أن صفات الأفعال قديمة كصفات المعاني، وإنما كانت صفات الأفعال حادثة عند الأشاعرة؛ لأنَّها عند التحقيق عندهم تعلقات القدرة التنجيزية الحادثة، وكانت قديمة عند الماتريديَّة؛ لأنَّها عندهم عين صفة التكوين القديمة، وأما الصفات السَّلبيَّة كالقِدم فهي قديمة أو أزليَّة إن قلنا بالفرق بين القديم والأزلي كما سبق لنا تقريره، وعلى هذا يحتاج قول الشارح: وخرج بإضافة الصفة إلى الذات السلبيَّة» إلى البيان، فإما أن يكون الشارح دَرَجَ على القول بالفرق بين القديم والأزلي، فنفى قدم الصفات السلبية وهو يذهب إلى أزليَّتها، وإما أن يكون ذكرها في هذا الموضع سَبْقَ كما قال العلامة الأمير.
And by the author's saying 'attributes of His essence' are excluded attributes of actions, for there is disagreement concerning them. The Ashʿaris hold that none of them are pre-eternal, and the Māturīdis hold that the attributes of actions are pre-eternal like the attributes of meanings. The attributes of actions are only originated according to the Ashʿaris because, upon investigation with them, they are the actualized relations of power (al-qudrah al-tanjīziyyah) which are originated. And they were pre-eternal according to the Māturīdis because they are, with them, the very attribute of bringing into existence (al-takwīn) which is pre-eternal. As for the negative attributes like pre-eternity (al-qidam), they are pre-eternal (qadīmah) or beginningless (azaliyyah) if we affirm a difference between the pre-eternal and the beginningless as we have previously established. On this, the commentator's saying: 'and are excluded by adding the attribute to the essence the negative [attributes]' needs explanation. Either the commentator followed the opinion differentiating between the pre-eternal and the beginningless, thus negated the pre-eternity of the negative attributes while affirming their beginninglessness, or he mentioned them in this place as a slip, as al-ʿAllāmah al-Amīr said.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is a classification and explanation of the exception regarding attributes of actions (ṣifāt al-afʿāl) and negative attributes (ṣifāt salbiyyah). Sanusi notes that the author's statement 'attributes of His essence' excludes attributes of actions, because there is disagreement among theologians. The Ashʿaris hold that none of the attributes of actions are pre-eternal (qadīmah); rather, they are originated because, in their analysis, these attributes are the actualized relations of power (taʿalluqāt al-qudrah al-tanjīziyyah) which arise when the action occurs. The Māturīdis, however, hold that attributes of actions are pre-eternal like the attributes of meanings, because they identify them with the single pre-eternal attribute of bringing into existence (ṣifat al-takwīn). As for the negative attributes (e.g., qidam—pre-eternity, baqāʾ—perpetuity), Sanusi explains that they are pre-eternal (qadīmah) or beginningless (azaliyyah) depending on whether one distinguishes between 'qadīm' and 'azalī'—a distinction already discussed. He then clarifies that the commentator's remark about excluding negative attributes requires explanation: either the commentator follows the distinction and denies their pre-eternity (qidam) while affirming their beginninglessness (azaliyyah), or he made a slip in mentioning them here.

Key Terms
صفات الأفعال
صفات المعاني
القدرة التنجيزية
التكوين
أشاعرة
ماتريدية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that attributes of actions being 'originated' for Ash'aris means they are temporal in God's essence, like human actions.
Correction: Actually, they are relational properties (taʿalluqāt) that arise when the action occurs, not temporal changes in God's essence.

Checkpoint
Why do the Ash'aris consider attributes of actions to be originated?
A) Because they are the same as the attribute of bringing into existence
B) Because they are negative attributes
C) Because they are actualized relations of power which are originated
D) Because they are not mentioned in the Quran

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari and Maturidi schools differ fundamentally on whether attributes of actions are pre-eternal or originated, based on their understanding of divine power and creative action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to choose between the Ash'ari view that God's attributes of actions are originated and relational, and the Maturidi view that they are pre-eternal and identified with a single creative attribute, which would bring you closer to a sense of God's constant involvement in your life? Why? What does your preference reveal about your relationship with God?
?
The Maturidis hold that God's attribute of bringing into existence (takwīn) is pre-eternal. If God's creative act has always been present in His essence, does that change how you perceive the universe as being sustained by God at every moment? How does this affect your reliance on God for your next breath?

Negative Attributes and the Qadim/Azali Distinction
Sanusi explains negative attributes and the qadim/azali distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the status of negative attributes like pre-eternity and the distinction between qadim and azali.

Core Idea
Negative attributes are pre-eternal or beginningless, depending on terminology.

After discussing attributes of actions, Sanusi turns to a special category: negative attributes (ṣifāt salbiyyah). These are attributes like qidam (pre-eternity) that negate their opposites. This passage explains their pre-eternity and introduces a subtle distinction between 'qadim' and 'azali' that affects theological terminology.

Essential Attributes and the Pre-Eternity of Allah's Names
Sanusi defines essential attributes and interprets their pre-eternity as divine institution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of essential attributes and the correct interpretation of their pre-eternity according to Ahl al-Sunnah, as well as the refutation of the Mu'tazilite view.

Core Idea
The pre-eternity of Allah's names means He set them for Himself before creation, not that the letters are eternal.

In this passage, Imam Sanusi clarifies a subtle point about the divine names and attributes. He explains that the essential attributes are those that indicate the essence, and the question of their pre-eternity (qidam) is not about the absence of a beginning in time but about divine institution before creation. This distinction refutes the Mu'tazila who claim the names are conventional human inventions. Let's follow the argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of essential attributes
Read the first part where Sanusi defines essential attributes as those that indicate the essence alone or with an attribute. Note the examples: 'Allah' and 'al-Qādir'.
2
Understand the two interpretations of qidam
The passage presents two interpretations: qidam as 'absence of priority' (temporal beginning) versus qidam as 'set before creation' (divine institution). Al-Mallawī's view is the latter.
This distinction is crucial against the Mu'tazila.
3
See the refutation and the process of divine institution
The passage concludes by stating that Allah set the names for Himself, then inspired angels, then inspired humans. This shows the divine origin of the names.
The word 'Muhyī' at the end may be a marginal note.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيانُ قِدم أسمائه تعالى وصفاته الذاتية عند أهل السُّنَّة والمراد بها ما دل على مُجرَّد ذاته، كالله، أو باعتبار الصفة، والقادِر، قديمةٌ باعتبار التّسمية بها، فهو الذي سمَّى بها ذاتَهُ أزلا، كَذَا وقد اختلف العلماء في تفسير معنى القدم في هذا الموضع، والذي انحط عليه كلام العلامة الملوي: أنَّ القدم هنا ليس بمعنى عدم الأوليَّة، بل بمعنى أنَّها موضوعة قبل الخلق خلافًا للمعتزلة، ومعنى ذلك أنَّ الله تعالى وضعها لنفسه قبل إيجاد الخلق، ثمّ ألهمها ملائكته، ثم ألهمها خَلْقَهُ، فاعرف ذلك. محي
An explanation of the pre-eternity of His names, may He be exalted, and His essential attributes according to the People of the Sunnah. And what is meant by them is what indicates His essence alone, like 'Allah', or in consideration of an attribute, like 'the Able'. They are pre-eternal (qadīmah) in consideration of the naming (al-tasmiyah) by them. For He it is Who named His essence by them in pre-eternity. Similarly, the scholars have differed in interpreting the meaning of pre-eternity (al-qidam) in this context. And that upon which the speech of al-ʿAllāmah al-Mallawī rests is that pre-eternity here is not in the sense of absence of priority, but rather in the sense that they were set (mawḍūʿah) before creation, contrary to the Muʿtazila. The meaning of that is that Allah, may He be exalted, set them for Himself before bringing creation into existence, then inspired His angels with them, then inspired His creatures with them. So know that. Muḥyī?
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage defines the essential attributes (al-ṣifāt al-dhātiyyah) and clarifies the meaning of their pre-eternity (qidam). Sanusi first states that the essential attributes are those that indicate either the essence alone (like the name 'Allah') or the essence in consideration of an attribute (like 'al-Qādir'—the Able). These are said to be pre-eternal (qadīmah) in consideration of the naming (al-tasmiyah) by them, meaning that God Himself named His essence by them in pre-eternity (azal). However, scholars disagreed on the interpretation of 'qidam' in this context. The preferred view according to al-ʿAllāmah al-Mallawī is that qidam here does not mean 'absence of priority' (i.e., not having a beginning in time) but rather that these names were set (mawḍūʿah) by God before creating the cosmos—contrary to the Muʿtazilites who claim the names are conventional human inventions. The process is that God first set the names for Himself, then inspired angels with them, then inspired human beings. This interpretation preserves the divine origin of the names without claiming that the physical letters are eternal.

Key Terms

تسمية
قدم
أزلي
وضع
معتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The pre-eternity (qidam) of Allah's names means the Arabic letters or sounds are eternal.
Correction: Qidam here means that Allah set the names for Himself before creation, not that the letters themselves are eternal. The names are divinely instituted, not created at a later time.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does 'qidam' (pre-eternity) of Allah's names mean in the preferred interpretation?
A) The names have no beginning in time
B) The names were invented by angels before humans
C) The names were set by God before creation
D) The names are eternal as attributes of essence

Key Takeaway
Allah's essential names and attributes are pre-eternal in the sense that He set them for Himself before creation, not in the sense of lacking a temporal beginning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If the Mu'tazila are wrong in reducing Allah's names to human convention, are there areas in your life where you treat the divine as something you can define or name on your own terms? Where do you need to submit to Allah's self-disclosure instead of your own assumptions?

The Eternality of Allah's Names: Definition and Interpretation
Sanusi defines the eternality of Allah's names and clarifies the intended meaning of 'qadim'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of the eternality (qidam) of Allah's names according to Ahl al-Sunnah and how it differs from the Mu'tazila view.

Core Idea
Allah's names are eternal because He named Himself with them before creation.

In this passage, Sanusi clarifies a subtle point about the eternality of Allah's names. The key is to understand what 'qadim' means in this context. It does not mean the words themselves are uncreated, but that they were placed by Allah before any creature existed. This lesson unpacks that distinction and its significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic source passage and its literal English translation. Focus on the flow of the argument without worrying about details.
The passage includes a main matn and a commentary gloss; treat them as a single unit for now.
2
Identify the definition of 'qadim'
Find the line where al-Mallawī's view is cited. Note that 'qadim' here means 'placed before creation' (mawḍūʿa qabla al-khalq), not 'lack of priority' (ʿadam al-awwaliyya). This is the core clarification.
This refutes the mistaken idea that the names are uncreated in essence.
3
Understand the two interpretations of names like 'Ālim'
The passage explains two views: (1) names indicate the essence by way of the attribute subsisting in it, (2) they indicate the attribute itself as subsisting in the essence. Both uphold that the names are pre-creation.
These interpretations are part of the broader discussion within Ahl al-Sunnah.
4
See the refutation of the Mu'tazila
Notice the explicit refutation: the Mu'tazila claim that names are human inventions. The passage asserts that Allah placed them for Himself before creation and then inspired them to angels and creation.
This highlights the orthodox stance that divine names are not conventional.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this distinction matters: it safeguards Allah's transcendence and the non-createdness of His attributes while avoiding the extreme of saying the Arabic words are co-eternal.
This balance is typical of Ash'ari theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيانُ قِدم أسمائه تعالى وصفاته الذاتية عند أهل السُّنَّة كالعالم والمراد بها ما دل على مُجرَّد ذاته ، كالله ، أو باعتبار الصفة ، والقادِر (١) ، قديمةٌ باعتبار التّسمية بها (٢) ، فهو الذي سمَّى بها ذاتَهُ أزلا ، كَذَا = وقد اختلف العلماء في تفسير معنى القدم في هذا الموضع ، والذي انحط عليه كلام العلامة الملوي: أنَّ القدم هنا ليس بمعنى عدم الأوليَّة ، بل بمعنى أنَّها موضوعة قبل الخلق خلافًا ذلك أنَّ ومعنى الله تعالى وضعها لنفسه قبل إيجاد الخلق ، ثمّ ألهمها ملائكته ، ثم للمعتزلة ، ألهمها خَلْقَهُ ، فاعرف ذلك. محي قوله: (أو باعتبار الصفة أي دلّ على الذات باعتبار الصفة فيه، وهذا جارٍ على طريقة بعضهم: أن المدلول بقولنا : عالم وقادر .. الذات باعتبار الصفة فيه ، أي : باعتبار قيام المعنى بها ؛ أي فالمدلول الذات فقط والصفة لوحظت قيدا وقال السبكي وغيره: المدلول من قولنا: قادر وعالم مثلا هو نفس الصفة التي هي القدرة ونفس الصفة التي هي . ، العلم من حيثُ قيامهما بالذات. وقدمُها باعتبار التعلق الصلوحي بها ، ويكون فيه الرد على المعتزلة في قولهم : هي من وضع الخلق له. فالحاصل أن قدم الأسماء على هذا ليس بمعنى انتفاء المسبوقية بالعدم، بل بمعنى أنها موضوعة قبل الخلق ، خلافا للمعتزلة، أي: إن الله وضعها بنفسه قبل إيجادنا . اهـ الشنواني .
An exposition of the eternality (qidam) of His names, may He be exalted, and His essential attributes according to the Ahl al-Sunnah, like al-ʿĀlim (the All-Knowing). And what is meant by them is what indicates His mere essence, like Allah, or by way of the attribute, and al-Qādir (the All-Powerful) (1), they are eternal (qadīma) by virtue of the naming (al-tasmiya) with them (2), for He is the One who named His essence with them eternally, likewise. And the scholars differed in interpreting the meaning of 'eternality (al-qidam)' in this context. What the statement of the scholar al-Mallawī settled upon is that 'eternality' here is not in the sense of lack of priority (ʿadam al-awwaliyya), but rather in the sense that they are placed before creation, contrary to that – and the meaning is that Allah, may He be exalted, placed them for Himself before bringing creation into existence, then He inspired them to His angels, then to the Muʿtazila, He inspired them to His creation, so know that. End. His statement: (or by way of the attribute) i.e., it indicates the essence by way of the attribute in it. This proceeds according to the way of some of them: that the indicated meaning by our saying 'ʿĀlim' and 'Qādir' is the essence by way of the attribute in it, i.e., by way of the subsistence of the meaning in it; i.e., the indicated meaning is the essence only and the attribute is considered a restriction. And al-Subkī and others said: the indicated meaning from our saying 'Qādir' and 'ʿĀlim' for example is the very attribute that is power and the very attribute that is knowledge, from the perspective of their subsistence in the essence. And their eternality is by virtue of the dispositional relation (al-taʿalluq al-ṣulūḥī) to them, and in it is a refutation of the Muʿtazila in their saying that they are from the placing of creation for Him. So the conclusion is that the eternality of the names according to this is not in the sense of the negation of being preceded by non-existence, but rather in the sense that they are placed before creation, contrary to the Muʿtazila, i.e., Allah placed them Himself before our creation. End of al-Shanwānī's commentary.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage defines the doctrine of the eternality (qidam) of Allah's names and essential attributes according to Ahl al-Sunnah. It begins by stating that names like al-ʿĀlim and al-Qādir indicate either the mere essence (like Allah) or the essence by way of an attribute. These names are described as eternal by virtue of the naming (tasmiya) with them, meaning that Allah named His essence with them from eternity. The passage then addresses a key clarification: scholars differed on the meaning of 'qadim' here. The view adopted from al-Mallawī is that it is not lack of priority (i.e., not the same as being uncreated in the sense of having no beginning), but rather that the names are placed (mawḍūʿa) before creation—that Allah placed them for Himself before creating, then inspired them to angels, and then to creation, contrary to the Muʿtazila who claim the names are invented by creatures. The footnote from al-Shanwānī expands on this: he explains that when we say 'ʿĀlim' or 'Qādir', there are two interpretations of what is indicated. Some say it indicates the essence qualified by the attribute; others (like al-Subkī) say it indicates the attribute itself as subsisting in the essence. The eternality of the names is by virtue of the dispositional relation—meaning that from eternity it was valid for Allah to be described by these attributes, so the names are considered pre-creation, not that the actual linguistic labels are uncreated. This refutes the Muʿtazilī position that the names are inventions of creation. The core idea is that 'qadim' here means pre-existence before creation, not absolute uncreatedness of the words themselves.

Key Terms
قدم (qidam)
أسماء (asmāʾ)
صفات ذاتية (ṣifāt dhātiyya)
التسمية (al-tasmiya)
القدم (al-qidam)
المعتزلة (al-Muʿtazila)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the names of Allah are uncreated like His essence, meaning the words themselves are eternal and not subject to creation.
Correction: They are eternal in the sense that Allah placed them before creation, not that they are uncreated in the absolute sense. The names are not co-eternal with Allah in essence, but are His acts of naming.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct interpretation of 'qadim' when applied to Allah's names?
A) They are uncreated like the essence of Allah.
B) They are not preceded by non-existence.
C) They were placed by Allah before creation.
D) They are eternal by virtue of the letters and sounds.

Key Takeaway
The eternality of Allah's names means He named Himself with them before creation, not that the words themselves are uncreated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you call upon Allah using His names, do you truly believe that He has always been known by that name, even before you existed? How does that affect the weight of your dua?
?
The Mu'tazila claimed that humans invented Allah's names. In your daily life, do you ever treat Allah's names as mere concepts or labels, rather than as eternal realities that He placed for Himself? What would change if you truly internalized their pre-creation origin?
?
If Allah inspired the knowledge of His names to angels and then to creation, what responsibility does that place on you to preserve and transmit these names correctly? Are you as careful with His names as you are with your own reputation?

The Objection That Names Are Created Words and the First Responses
Sanusi presents the objection and the first two answers with a critique.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the initial objection that names cannot be eternal because they are words, and the first two responses offered by Sunni theologians: the appeal to the eternal act of naming (tasmiya) and the eternal validity (ṣulāḥiyya) for being named.

Core Idea
Names are eternal in their divine designation, not in their verbal form.

This passage from Sanusi's commentary addresses a central objection raised by the Mu'tazila: if the names of Allah are Arabic words, and words are created, how can the names be eternal? Sanusi walks through several replies, beginning with the distinction between the name-as-word and the naming-act. In this lesson, we follow the first two answers and the critical response to the Mu'tazilite position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core objection
Read the opening lines of the passage. Notice the objection: names are words (alfāẓ), and all words are originated (ḥādith), so names cannot be eternal.
The objection is straightforward and based on a logical syllogism.
2
Examine the first answer: by virtue of naming
The text says names are eternal not in themselves but by virtue of the naming (tasmiya). Reflect on this distinction between the word and the act of naming.
This answer shifts the locus of eternality from the linguistic form to the divine act.
3
Consider the counter-objection about coinage
The opponent argues that naming itself is a coinage (waḍʿ) of a word for a meaning, and coinage is an originated human act, so naming is also originated.
This forces the defender to clarify what 'naming' means in the divine context.
4
Understand the second answer: eternal validity
The response is that 'the naming is eternal' means Allah was valid (ṣāliḥ) for being named from eternity. The naming itself is temporal, but the validity is eternal.
This answer attempts to preserve eternality without claiming the actual naming act is eternal.
5
Note the critique against the Mu'tazila
The passage states this answer is ineffective against the Mu'tazila because they deny even the eternal validity of names, since they hold names are purely human inventions.
This critique shows that not all answers are equally convincing against all opponents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲) قوله : (باعتبار التسمية بها والحاصل أن قوله : (باعتبار التسمية جواب عن إشكال حاصله أن الأسماء ألفاظ قطعا، وكل ما كان كذلك فهو حادث فينتج أن الأسماء حادث ، فكيف توصف الأسماء بالقدم ، وأجيب : بأنها قديمة لا باعتبار ذاتها ، بل باعتبار التسمية بها فالتسمية القديمة ، واعترض قدمها بأنها عبارة عن وضع اللفظ للمعنى ، ومن المعلوم أن الوضع حادث فتكون التسمية حادثة كالألفاظ ، وأجيب بأن معنى قولهم التسمية قديمة أي: باعتبار الصلاحية ، أي : إن الله صالح لها أزلا فالتسمية فيما لا يزال، والصلاحية قديمة، وفيه: أنَّ هذا لا يحسن في الرد على المعتزلة الذين يقولون إنها من وضع الخلق ، إذ لا ينافيه ، وقيل: المراد بالتسمية تعين الأسماء في الأزل فهي قديمة باعتبار تعينها وتقديرها، وأما هي في نفسها فحادثة ، فقولهم: «سمى نفسه أزلا أي عين الأسماء لذاته وقدرها في الأزل، واعترض بأن كل شيء مقدر في الأزل إذ المراد به القدم ، وقيل : المراد من قولهم: «الأسماء قديمة أي: مدلولها ،قديم كالعلم والقدرة والإرادة وقد يقال قدم هذه الأمور علم مما تقدم من قدم الذات والصفات وقيل : معنى قول التسمية قديمة أنها قديمة باعتبار الدال عليها وهو كلام الله ، وفيه: أنَّ قدم الكلام علم مما تقدم ولا يحسن ردا، مع أن الكلام دل=
(2) His statement: (by virtue of the naming (al-tasmiya) with them) and the summary is that his statement: (by virtue of the naming) is an answer to an objection whose conclusion is that names are definitely words (alfāẓ), and everything that is such is originated (ḥādith), so it follows that names are originated. So how can names be described as eternal (qadīm)? It was answered that they are eternal not by virtue of their essence, but rather by virtue of the naming with them, for the naming is eternal. And their eternality was objected to because it is an expression of the coinage (waḍʿ) of the word for the meaning, and it is known that coinage is originated, so the naming becomes originated like the words. And it was answered that the meaning of their saying 'the naming is eternal' is by virtue of the validity (al-ṣulāḥiyya), i.e., Allah is valid for it eternally, so the naming is in what is yet to come, and the validity is eternal. But in this it is said: This is not good as a refutation of the Muʿtazila who say they are from the coinage of creation, since it does not conflict with it. And it was said: What is meant by 'the naming' is the specification (taʿayyun) of the names in pre-eternity, so they are eternal by virtue of their specification and predetermination, but as for themselves, they are originated. So their saying 'He named Himself eternally' means He specified the names for His essence and predestined them in pre-eternity. And it was objected that everything is predestined in pre-eternity, for what is meant by it is the eternal. And it was said: The meaning of their saying 'the names are eternal' is that their referents (madlūluhā) are eternal, like knowledge, power, and will, and it may be said that the eternality of these things is known from what has preceded regarding the eternality of the essence and attributes. And it was said: The meaning of the statement 'the naming is eternal' is that it is eternal by virtue of that which indicates it, and that is the speech of Allah (kalām Allāh). But in this it is said: The eternality of speech is known from what has preceded, and it is not good as a refutation, and that speech indicates =
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is an extended objection-and-answer (shubha wa jawāb) unit regarding how names can be eternal when they are words, and words are created. The objection is straightforward: names are words (alfāẓ), and all words are originated (ḥādith); therefore names cannot be eternal. The first answer is that the eternality belongs not to the words themselves but to the 'naming' (tasmiya)—the act of naming is eternal, even if the words are temporal. But then a further objection arises: naming itself is a 'coining' (waḍʿ) of a word for a meaning, and coinage is an originated human act, so the naming would also be originated. In response, the commentator explains that 'naming is eternal' means that from eternity Allah was valid for it—He could be named—so the naming is considered pre-eternal by virtue of that validity (ṣulāḥiyya). However, this answer is criticized as ineffective against the Muʿtazila because they deny even the validity of names before creation. Alternative answers are then proposed: (a) 'naming' means the specific determination (taʿayyun) of the names in pre-eternity—Allah predetermined which names would apply to Him, and that determination is eternal; (b) 'names are eternal' refers to the referents (madlūl) like knowledge, power, and will, which are eternal as attributes; (c) 'naming is eternal' because it is indicated by Allah's speech (kalām), which is eternal. The last answer is also critiqued. The passage ends incomplete, but it shows the richness of debates around this issue. The core idea is that there are multiple ways to defend the eternality of names without asserting the words themselves are uncreated.

Key Terms
ألفاظ (alfāẓ)
وضع (waḍʿ)
حادث (ḥādith)
صلاحية (ṣulāḥiyya)
تسمية (tasmiya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the eternality of names requires belief that the Arabic words themselves are eternal.
Correction: The passage shows that Sunni theologians defend the eternality of names by appealing to the eternal act of naming or the eternal validity of being named, not the words themselves.

Checkpoint
What is the main objection presented in this passage?
A) Names cannot be eternal because they are derived from actions.
B) Names are words and words are originated, so they cannot be eternal.
C) Names refer to attributes but attributes are not eternal.
D) Names are invented by human beings after creation.

Key Takeaway
The first two defenses of the names' eternality appeal to the eternal act of naming and Allah's eternal capacity for being named, but both face difficulties against the Mu'tazilite denial of any pre-creational naming.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage shows that the Muʿtazila reduced the names of Allah to mere human conventions. In your own heart, do you treat the name 'Allah' as a divine reality that has always been worthy of you, or do you sometimes use it carelessly as just a word? What would change in your daily life if you truly believed that this name is eternal and carries weight from before time?
?
The concept of 'validity' (ṣulāḥiyya) is used to defend the names' eternity, but the critique says it doesn't refute the deniers. When you call upon Allah by His names, do you ever wonder if your use of them is simply a human habit, or do you actually feel connected to an eternal reality? If the names are eternal, then they demand a constant awareness in your life—are you giving them that?
?
Some scholars argued that the names are eternal because Allah is eternally valid for being named. But if that validity doesn't change your daily reverence for those names, what's the point of the doctrine? Examine your own practice: does the theological belief that Allah's names are eternal translate into a deeper awe and love when you recite 'Bismillah' before a meal or in prayer? If not, what are you missing?
