The Two Meanings of Kalam Allah and the Quran
Explains the dual usage of 'Kalam Allah' and 'Quran' and their respective rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the terms 'Kalam Allah' and 'Quran' each have two distinct meanings—one eternal and one created—and why this distinction matters for the doctrine of the speech of Allah.

Core Idea
The Quran is both an eternal attribute and a created text—knowing which reference is meant prevents theological error.

This lesson unpacks a key distinction in Sunni theology: the terms 'Kalam Allah' and 'al-Qur'an' are not univocal. They can refer either to the eternal attribute of speech subsisting in Allah’s essence or to the recited words we hear and write. Understanding this duality is essential for correctly affirming the uncreated nature of Allah’s speech while also acknowledging the created nature of the mushaf.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the flow: the author first states the topic, then explains the dual usage of each term, gives evidence, and concludes with the Mu'tazila position.
Pay attention to the phrase 'كل من «كلام الله» و«القرآن» يطلق بإطلاقين', which is key.
2
Identify the two meanings
List the two meanings for 'Kalam Allah' and the two for 'al-Qur'an'. See how the author distinguishes between the eternal attribute and the recited text.
Remember: the eternal attribute is not composed of sounds or letters.
3
Note the frequent usage
The author mentions which meaning is more commonly intended for each term. This explains why the poet clarified 'Quran' as 'His speech'.
This is important to avoid misunderstanding when reading classical texts.
4
Contrast with the Mu'tazila
The Mu'tazila deny the eternal attribute and consider all speech as created. See how this leads to a different understanding of the terms.
This contrast highlights the Sunni position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم الإلهيات
بيان أن كلام الله تعالى قديم عند أهل السنة خلافًا للمعتزلة
٤١ - ونزه القرآن أي كلامه عن الحدوث واحذر انتقامه
ثم شرع (1) في مسألة خلق القرآن، فقال: (ونزه القرآن) أي: يجب عليك (1) قد قدمنا في مبحث صفة الكلام أن مذهب أهل السنة والجماعة أن كلا من «كلام الله» و«القرآن» يطلق بإطلاقين؛ فأما «كلام الله» فيطلق ويراد به الصفة القديمة القائمة بذاته تعالى التي ليست بصوت ولا حرف، وهو بهذا المعنى قديم، ويطلق بإطلاق آخر ويراد به القرآن الكريم الذي نتلوه بألسنتنا، ويسمعه بعضنا من بعض ونكتبه بأيدينا في مصاحفنا، ووجه إطلاق كلام الله على القرآن المتلو: أنه دال على الصفة القديمة القائم بذاته تعالى، أو أنه سبحانه هو الخالق له على هذا النظم، بهذه الألفاظ، وهذا الترتيب المعجز، وليس لأحد فيه شيء ما، وقد أطلق الله تعالى على القرآن الكريم «كلام الله» بهذا المعنى في قوله سبحانه: {وَإِنْ أَحَدٌ مِنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ اسْتَجَارَكَ فَأَجِرْهُ حَتَّى يَسْمَعَ كَلَامَ اللهِ} [التوبة: 6] وأطلقت عائشة الصديقية «كلام الله» على المكتوب في المصاحب في قولها: «ما بين دفتي المصحف كلام الله» ونسب هذا إلى كثير من الصحابة، وأما «القرآن» فيطلق أيضا بهذين الإطلاقين؛ فتارة يطلق ويراد به الصفة القديمة القائمة بذاته تعالى، وتارة يطلق ويراد به ما نتلوه ونكتبه ويسمعه بعضنا من بعض، لما ذكرنا في إطلاق «كلام الله» فإن أطلق بالمعنى الأول - وهو الصفة القديمة - فهو قديم، وإن أطلق بالمعنى الثاني فهو مخلوق، ومع أن كلا من «القرآن» و«كلام الله» يطلق تارة على الصفة القديمة وتارة أخرى على المتلو الملفوظ به فإن الأكثر إطلاق لفظ «القرآن» على المتلو الملفوظ به، والأكثر إطلاق لفظ «كلام الله» على الصفة القديمة القائمة بذاته تعالى، ولهذا فسر الناظم القرآن بكلام الله في قوله: «ونزه القرآن أي: كلامه» حتى يكون أظهر في المراد، وقد ذكرنا - مع ذلك - أن أئمة هذه الأمة تحرجوا أن يصفوا القرآن بالحدوث مخافة أن يتبادر إلى أذهان العامة أن الصفة القائمة بذاته حادثة؛ لأن «القرآن» لفظ مشترك بين هذين المعنيين. وقدمنا أن المعتزلة ذهبوا إلى أن «القرآن» و«كلام الله» حادثان، وأنه لا معنى لهما إلا الكلام المرتب المستمل على الأصوات والحروف، ولهذا منعوا أن يتصف الله تعالى بالكلام.
Section of Ilahiyyat. Statement that the speech of Allah Most High is eternal according to the People of the Sunna, contrary to the Mu'tazila. 41 - And declare the Qur'an, i.e. His speech, free from being originated, and beware of His vengeance. Then he began (1) on the issue of the creation of the Qur'an, and said: (And declare the Qur'an free) i.e., it is incumbent upon you (1). We have already presented in the section on the attribute of speech that the doctrine of the People of the Sunna and the Community is that each of 'speech of Allah' and 'the Qur'an' are used with two usages. As for 'speech of Allah', it is used and by it is meant the eternal attribute subsisting in His essence Most High, which is not a sound nor a letter, and it in this sense is eternal (qadim). And it is used with another usage and by it is meant the noble Qur'an which we recite with our tongues, and some of us hear from others, and we write with our hands in our copies. The aspect of applying 'speech of Allah' to the recited Qur'an is that it indicates the eternal attribute subsisting in His essence Most High, or that He is the Creator of it in this composition, with these words, and this miraculous arrangement, and no one has any part in it. And Allah Most High has applied 'speech of Allah' to the noble Qur'an in this sense in His saying: {And if any of the polytheists seeks your protection, then grant him protection so that he may hear the speech of Allah} [At-Tawba 9:6]. And A'isha as-Siddiqa applied 'speech of Allah' to what is written in the copies in her saying: 'What is between the two covers of the copy of the Qur'an is the speech of Allah.' And this was attributed to many of the Companions. As for 'the Qur'an', it is also used with these two usages: sometimes it is used and by it is meant the eternal attribute subsisting in His essence Most High, and sometimes it is used and by it is meant what we recite, write, and some of us hear from others, because of what we mentioned in the usage of 'speech of Allah'. If it is used in the first sense - which is the eternal attribute - then it is eternal, and if it is used in the second sense then it is created. And although each of 'the Qur'an' and 'speech of Allah' is used sometimes for the eternal attribute and sometimes for the recited uttered thing, the more frequent usage of the term 'the Qur'an' is for the recited uttered thing, and the more frequent usage of the term 'speech of Allah' is for the eternal attribute subsisting in His essence Most High. Hence the poet interpreted the Qur'an as the speech of Allah in his saying: 'Declare the Qur'an free, i.e., His speech' so that it may be more apparent as to what is intended. And we have mentioned - along with that - that the imams of this nation were cautious about describing the Qur'an as originated (hadith) for fear that it might come to the minds of the common people that the attribute subsisting in His essence is originated, because 'the Qur'an' is a term shared between these two meanings. And we have presented that the Mu'tazila held that 'the Qur'an' and 'the speech of Allah' are both originated, and that there is no meaning for them except the ordered speech comprising sounds and letters, and for this reason they denied that Allah Most High is described with speech.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the dual usage of the terms 'Kalam Allah' (speech of Allah) and 'al-Qur'an' (the Quran). The author begins by stating the title: that the speech of Allah is eternal according to the People of the Sunna, contrary to the Mu'tazila. He then comments on the poet's line: 'Declare the Qur'an free from being originated and beware of His vengeance.' The explanation follows: first, it is established that in the doctrine of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, both 'Kalam Allah' and 'al-Qur'an' have two distinct meanings. First, they can refer to the eternal attribute (al-sifa al-qadima) that subsists in Allah's essence, which is not composed of sounds or letters—this is eternal (qadim). Second, they can refer to the recited Quran that we recite, hear, and write in copies—this is created (makhluq). The author then explains why the recited Quran is called 'Kalam Allah': either because it indicates the eternal attribute, or because Allah is its Creator in this miraculous composition and arrangement, with no human contribution. He cites Qur'an 9:6 where Allah calls it 'Kalam Allah' in the sense of the recited words, and reports that A'isha and many Companions used 'Kalam Allah' for the written text. He then reiterates that both terms share the two usages, but the more frequent usage is that 'al-Qur'an' often denotes the recited thing, while 'Kalam Allah' often denotes the eternal attribute. Thus the poet interpreted 'al-Qur'an' as 'His speech' to clarify the intended meaning (the eternal attribute). The author notes that the early imams hesitated to describe the Quran as 'hadith' (originated) because the term 'Qur'an' is ambiguous between the two meanings, and the unlearned might mistakenly think the eternal attribute is created. Finally, he contrasts the Mu'tazila position: they consider both 'al-Qur'an' and 'Kalam Allah' as originated, meaning only the composed speech of sounds and letters, and they deny that Allah is described with speech in the sense of an eternal attribute.

Correction: The passage clarifies that the eternal attribute is uncreated, but the recited text is created. The term 'Quran' is ambiguous, covering both meanings.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The terms 'Kalam Allah' and 'Quran' are each used in two ways: one referring to the eternal attribute (uncreated) and one to the recited text (created); Sunni creed distinguishes both, against the Mu'tazila who deny the eternal attribute.

The Eternity of Allah's Speech
Sanusi defines Allah's speech as eternal and refutes the Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni belief that Allah's speech is an eternal attribute of His essence, distinct from temporal recitation, and why this refutes the Mu'tazila position.

Core Idea
Allah's speech is eternal, not created—an attribute of His essence.

This lesson introduces a foundational point of Sunni creed: that Allah's speech (kalam) is eternal and uncreated. You will read a passage from al-Sanusi that states this belief, explaining why it is a necessary attribute of Allah and how it differs from the created words we recite. The passage also refutes the Mu'tazila who claimed His speech is created.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the literal translation. Notice the key terms: قديم (eternal) and حادث (temporal).
2
Identify the three claims
The passage makes three main points: (1) Allah's speech is eternal, (2) this refutes the Mu'tazila, and (3) the speech is an attribute of His essence, not created. Distinguish between internal (kalam nafsi) and external (recited) speech.
The footnote explains why the author used 'temporality' for 'creation'.
3
Reflect on theological significance
Consider why this belief matters for tawhid. If Allah's speech were created, it would imply change in His essence. The passage argues that created accidents cannot subsist in Allah.
This connects to the broader attribute of speech (sifat al-kalam).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كلام الله تعالى قَديمٌ عند أهل السُّنَّة خِلافًا للمعتزلة
أيُّها المكلَّف أنْ تُنزّه القرآنَ أَيْ: كَلَامَه النَّفسي الأزلي القائم بذاته تعالى (عَنِ الحُدُوثِ) أي : الوجودِ بعد العدم ؛ فليس مخلوقا، ولا قائما بمخلوق، بل هو صفة ذاتِه العليَّة ؛ لِمَا عُلِم مِن امتناع قيام الحوادث بذاته، ولضرورة النَّظم عبّر بالحدوث عن الخلق (۱) .
(۱) قوله : ( ولضرورة النظم احتاج لهذا ؛ لأنّ المشهور بين القوم التعبير بالخلق. الأمير.
Allah's speech is eternal according to Ahl al-Sunna, contrary to the Mu'tazila. O responsible person, you must declare the Quran transcendent, i.e., His eternal, uncreated speech subsisting in His essence, from temporality, i.e., existence after non-existence; for it is not created, nor subsisting in a created thing, but rather it is an attribute of His exalted essence. This is because it is known that created accidents cannot subsist in His essence, and due to the necessity of the arrangement, he expressed creation by temporality. (1) (1) He said: 'And due to the necessity of the arrangement, he needed this because the well-known expression among the people is creation.' - al-Amir.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage defines the core belief of Ahl al-Sunna regarding Allah's speech. It begins by stating that Allah's speech is eternal, in opposition to the Mu'tazila who claim it is created. The passage then addresses the responsible believer (mukallaf) to declare the Quran transcendent, meaning to deny that it is temporal. It distinguishes between the eternal, uncreated speech (kalam nafsi) that is an attribute of Allah's essence, and the temporal, created speech (kalam lafzi) which is the recited words. The reason for this is that created accidents cannot subsist in Allah's essence, so His speech must be eternal. The author notes that in this context, 'temporality' is used to mean 'creation' due to the conventional arrangement of terms. The footnote explains that the author used 'temporality' instead of 'creation' because the well-known expression among the people is 'creation'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the Quran (as recited) is entirely created or that denying temporality means denying the linguistic form of the Quran.
Correction: The passage clarifies that Allah's internal speech is eternal and uncreated, while the recited words are temporal and created. Denying temporality applies to the eternal attribute, not the physical recitation.

Checkpoint
What do Ahl al-Sunna believe about Allah's speech?
A) It is created.
B) It is eternal and an attribute of His essence.
C) It is not a real attribute.
D) It is both eternal and temporal.

Key Takeaway
Allah's speech is an eternal attribute of His essence, not a created thing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you truly believe you are engaging with an eternal attribute of Allah? How does that change the reverence and attention you give to each verse? Commit to pausing before each recitation to remind yourself of this truth.
?
Have you ever reduced the Quran to a mere book, treatable like any other text? Knowing that it is the expression of Allah's eternal speech, what will you change in how you handle, read, or listen to it starting today?
?
If someone were to tell you that your relationship with the Quran is superficial, would they be right? What one concrete action will you take this week to deepen your connection with the eternal speech of Allah?

The Danger of Saying 'The Quran is Created': Doctrinal Distinction
Warning and doctrinal distinction regarding the Quran's createdness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why saying 'the Quran is created' is dangerous and the key distinction between the eternal attribute and the recited words.

Core Idea
Ambiguous language about the Quran can imply that Allah's eternal speech is created.

This passage from al-Sanusi's Jawhara warns against a statement that may seem but carries a dangerous theological implication. The author carefully distinguishes between the Quran as the eternal attribute of Allah and the Quran as the recited words, explaining when it is permissible to say 'created' and when it is not.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the overall warning. Then read the translation. Notice the author's progression from warning to explanation.
The passage contains some unclear text due to OCR; focus on the clear parts.
2
Identify the two meanings of 'Quran'
The author defines two meanings: the eternal attribute of Allah, and the recited words. Understand each and how they differ.
The eternal attribute is uncreated; the recited words are created.
3
Understand the prohibition
Why is it prohibited to say 'the Quran is created' without qualification? Because it might be misunderstood to refer to the eternal attribute. The author mentions 'sadd al-dhara'i' (blocking the means).
This is a principle of preventing harm through ambiguous speech.

وَاحْذَرِ انْتِقَامَهُ) أي: انتقامَ الله منكَ وعقابَهُ لكَ إِنْ قلتَ بحدوثه .

الأئمة
كلامه أنه
وقالوا: إن معنى خلق الكلام في بعض الأجرام كالجبل أو الشجرة أو نحوهما. ومراد المصنف هنا أن يقول: إنّ القرآن بمعنى كلامه تعالى أي: بمعنى الصفة القديمة القائمة بذاته تعالى ، مما يجب على المكلف أن يعتقد قِدَمه ، وينزّهه عن الحدوث كما هو مذهب أهل السُّنَّة ، وأما القرآن بمعنى اللفظ الذي نقرؤه فهو مخلوق الذي نقرؤه فهو مخلوق، ومع كونه مخلوقا أن يقال: القرآن مخلوق ويراد اللفظ الذي نتلوه إلا في مقام التعليم ؛ لأنه ربما أوهم أنَّ القُرآن بمعنى كلامه تعالى، أي: صفتِه القديمة مخلوق ، ولهذا الإيهام امتنعتِ من القول بخلق القرآن ، وقد وقع في هذا الموضوع امتحان كبير لخلق كثير ، وأشهرُ مَن امتحِنَ بذلك الإمامُ النّاصر لسُنَّة رسول الله أحمد بن حنبل رضي الله تعالى عنه، فقد حُبِسَ وضُرِبَ على أنْ يقول: «القرآنُ مخلوقٌ» فأبَى ، ولم يقبل أن يقول هذه الكلمة - مع كونها صحيحة بأحد معنيين ـ مخافة أن تُحمل على المعنى غير الجائز، وممَّن ابتلي بهذه المحنة أبو يعقوب يوسف ابن يحي المصري، المعروف بالبويطي، صاحب الإمام الشافعي، فإنَّه حُملَ مِن مصر إلى بغداد وطلب إليه أن يقول: «القرآن مخلوق فلم يُجب إلى ما دُعِيَ إليه، وقال: القرآن هو كلام الله غير مخلوق، فحُبِس، ومات في السجن يوم الجمعةِ قبل الصلاة سنة إحدى وثلاثين ومائتين وخرج البخاري إمامُ أهل الحدِيثِ فارا من هذه الفتنة، وقال: اللهم اقبضني إليكَ غير مفتون، فمات بعد أربعة أيام، وسُجِنَ عيسى بن دينار عشرين سنةً، وسئل الشَّعبي عن هذا، فقال: التوراة والإنجيل والزبور والفرقان ، هذه الأربعة حادثة ، ورفع أصابع يده الأربعة مشيرًا ، فتركوه ، وهذا من المعاريض التي فيها مَنْدُوحَةٌ عن الكذب، وينسب مثل هذه الحكاية إلى الإمام الشافعي ، رضي الله تعالى عنه.
محي .
And beware of His vengeance) i.e., Allah's vengeance and punishment upon you if you say it is temporal. ... They said: The meaning of creating speech in some bodies like the mountain or the tree or the like. And the author's intent here is to say: The Quran in the sense of His speech, i.e., the eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, is what the responsible person must believe is eternal and declare it free from temporality, as is the madhhab of Ahl al-Sunna. As for the Quran in the sense of the word that we recite, it is created. And despite it being created, it is not said 'the Quran is created' intending the word we recite except in a teaching context, because it may give the impression that the Quran in the sense of His speech, i.e., His eternal attribute, is created. And due to this impression, they refrained from saying 'the creation of the Quran'. And a great trial occurred regarding this matter for many people. The most famous of those tried by this was the Imam, the supporter of the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, may Allah be pleased with him, for he was imprisoned and beaten to say 'the Quran is created', but he refused, and he did not accept to say this word – even though it is correct in one of two meanings – for fear that it would be taken in the impermissible sense. And among those afflicted by this trial was Abu Ya'qub Yusuf ibn Yahya al-Misri, known as al-Buwayti, the companion of Imam al-Shafi'i, for he was carried from Egypt to Baghdad and was asked to say 'the Quran is created', but he did not respond to what he was called to, and said: The Quran is the speech of Allah, uncreated. So he was imprisoned and died in prison on Friday before prayer in the year 231 AH. And al-Bukhari, the Imam of hadith, left fleeing from this tribulation, and said: O Allah, take me to You untested. So he died after four days. And 'Isa ibn Dinar was imprisoned for twenty years. And al-Sha'bi was asked about this, and he said: The Torah, the Gospel, the Psalms, and the Criterion, these four are temporal, and he raised his four fingers indicating, so they left him. And this is from the lawful evasions that provide an escape from lying. And a similar story is attributed to Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with him.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage begins a warning against saying the Quran is created, as it may lead to punishment. It then explains the technical meaning of creating speech in bodies, clarifying that the author's intent is to affirm the eternity of the divine attribute while acknowledging that the recited words are created. However, due to the potential misunderstanding, it is forbidden to say 'the Quran is created' without qualification, except in teaching contexts. The passage then narrates the historical trial (Mihna) where Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal and others were persecuted by Mu'tazila-leaning rulers who demanded they declare the Quran created. Ahmad refused despite imprisonment and beating. Other examples include al-Buwayti, who died in prison, and al-Bukhari who fled and died soon after. The story of al-Sha'bi shows a clever evasion using words to avoid the harmful statement. These examples emphasize the importance of guarding correct theological language.

Key Terms
انتقام
خلق
القول بخلق القرآن
سد الذرائع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the Ash'ari position denies any createdness of the Quran, even the recited words.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the recited words are created, but the general statement 'the Quran is created' is avoided because it could be misunderstood to refer to the eternal attribute.

Checkpoint
Why is it prohibited to say 'the Quran is created' without qualification, even though the recited words are created?
A) Because the recited words are not created.
B) Because it may give the impression that the eternal attribute is created.
C) Because the Quran is entirely uncreated.
D) Because it is prohibited by the caliphs.

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'the Quran is created' is avoided because it could falsely imply that Allah's eternal speech is created.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you speak about Allah's attributes, are you careful to avoid ambiguous language that could mislead others? How does this passage wake you up to the accountability of your words?
?
Do you fear Allah's vengeance when you speak carelessly about the Quran? What specific phrases must you now avoid?
?
How often do you consider the potential harm of your words in matters of aqeedah? Will you commit to learning the precise terms before speaking about divine attributes?

The Trial (Mihna) of Ahmad ibn Hanbal and Others
Historical accounts of the Mihna and the scholars' responses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical trial (Mihna) where scholars were forced to say 'the Quran is created' and the lessons learned from their steadfastness.

Core Idea
The fear of ambiguous words led to persecution; true scholars preferred suffering over doctrinal compromise.

Having established the doctrinal warning, the author now recounts the historical persecution known as the Mihna, where the Mu'tazila-leaning caliphs forced scholars to declare the Quran created. The most famous victim was Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal, whose steadfastness became a symbol of Sunni resistance. Other scholars like al-Buwayti and al-Bukhari also faced trials.

Guided Path
1
Read the historical accounts
Read the Arabic passage with its translation. Notice the different scholars mentioned and their responses to the demand to say 'the Quran is created'.
Pay attention to the variety of strategies: refusal, fleeing, taqiyya (lawful evasion).
2
Identify the principle of 'sadd al-dhara'i'
The author uses these stories to illustrate the danger of ambiguous language. Ahmad refused to say a phrase that could be misunderstood, even though in one sense it was true.
This is the same principle as in the previous lesson.
3
Reflect on the lessons
What do these stories teach about theological steadfastness? How should a believer balance truth and avoidance of harm?
Consider the different approaches: direct refusal, lawful evasion, or fleeing.

The Hermeneutic Principle for Quran Temporality Verses
Sanusi's instruction to interpret temporality verses as referring to the recited words.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the principle that any scriptural text that appears to indicate the Quran's temporality must be interpreted as referring to the recited words (al-lafẓ), not the eternal attribute of Allah.

Core Idea
All verses hinting the Quran is created point to the recited words, not Allah's eternal speech.

This passage establishes a crucial hermeneutic rule for protecting the doctrine of the Quran's eternity. When the Quran or hadith contain phrases that seem to say the Quran is created or temporal, the believer must understand these as referring to the physical words revealed to the Prophet, not to Allah's attribute of speech. Sanusi presents this principle and supports it with scriptural evidence, while cautioning against careless language.

Guided Path
1
Understand the problem: texts that seem to say Quran is created
Many Quranic verses and hadiths mention sending down, revealing, or 'new reminder'. These might be misread as implying the Quran is created. Sanusi provides the corrective.
This problem was used by Mu'tazila to support their doctrine.
2
Learn the rule: interpret such texts as referring to the recited words
Sanusi states that any text indicating temporality must be carried upon the recited word, not the internal speech.
The recited words are created, but the attribute is eternal.
3
See the refutation of Mu'tazila and their terminology
Sanusi refutes those who use such verses to claim the Quran is created, and notes that even those who say 'temporal' instead of 'created' are still wrong.
4
Examine the examples from Quran
Verses like 'We sent it down' and 'new reminder' are explained by scholars as referring to the created text in the Preserved Tablet, sent down piecemeal.
5
Grasp the final conclusion and practical ruling
It is impermissible to say 'the Quran is created' even if meaning the recited words, except in teaching contexts, to avoid misunderstanding.
This is a precautionary measure (sadd al-dhara'i').

(1) أراد بهذا الكلام الرَّدَ على ما تمسك به المعتزلة القائلون بأنَّ القرآن مخلوق أو حادث ، فإن جمهورهم كان يقول: القرآن مخلوق واشتهرت المحنة التي تحدثنا عنها بعض الحديث بمحنة «القول بخلق القرآن لكن محمدا البلخي ـ وهو من المعتزلة أيضا ـ كان يتحرج من كلمة الخلق، ويلتزم التعبير بحدوث القرآن، ويزعم أنَّ كلمة الخلق توهم الاختلاق، وهو الكذب ؛ لكون المادة واحدةً، فهو كمَن فَرَّ مِن المَطر فوقف تحت الميزاب ؛ لأنَّ الخلق والحدوث بمعنى واحدٍ ، تعالى الله عما يقول المبطلون علوا كبيرًا! والمراد أنَّ كل ما ورد في الكتاب الكريم والسُّنَّة النبويَّة مِن النُّصوص الدالة بظاهرها على كلام الله حادث ، أو على أنَّ القرآن حادث فإِنَّه يجب على المكلَّف أنْ يحمله على أنَّ المراد به اللفظ المُنزَّلُ على نبينا الله ، المُتَعبَّدُ بتلاوته المُتحدّى بأقصر سورة منه ، وذلك مثل قوله : إِنَّا أَنزَلْتَهُ فِي لَيْلَةِ الْقَدْرِ ﴾ [القدر: ١] وقوله: ﴿إِنَّا نَحْنُ نَزَّلْنَا الذِّكْرَ وَإِنَّا لَهُ لَحَفِظُونَ ) [الحجر: ٩ ] ، وقوله سبحانه: مَا يَأْتِيهِم مِّن ذِكْرِ مِن رَّبِّهِم مُّحْدَثٍ إِلَّا أَسْتَمَعُوهُ وَهُمْ يَلْعَبُونَ لَاهِيَةً قُلُوبُهُمْ ﴾ [الأنبياء: ۲ - ۳ ] ، والذي ذكره العلماء أنَّ الله تعالى خلق القرآن في اللوح المحفوظ ، ثمّ أنزله إلى سماء الدنيا في مكان منها يقال له بيت العِزَّة، وهذا هو المشار إليه بقوله سبحانه: ﴿إِنَّا أَنزَلْتَهُ فِي لَيْلَةِ الْقَدْرِ ﴾ [القدر: ۱] أي: الليلة المباركة العظيمة الشأن، ثم كـ كان يُوحَى إلى جبريل أن ينزل بما اقتضت إرادته سبحانه إنزاله على الرسول الأكرم صلى الله عليه وسلم ، فبلَّغَهُ جبريلُ رسول الله مُفرَّقا بحسب مقتضيات الأحوال والوقائع . والحاصل: أنه ينبغي للمكلف أن يحمل كل كلام ورد في القرآن أو السُّنَّة وهو دال بظاهره على حدوث القرآن أو حدوث كلام الله على اللفظ المتلو ، لا على الكلام النفسي لأنَّه صِفةٌ قديمة قائمة بذاته تعالى، وأنَّه لا يجوز أنْ يقال: القرآن مُحدَث» أو «القرآن مخلوق» أو كلام الله محدث» أو «كلام الله مخلوق ولو مع قصد المتلو، إلا في مقام التعليم، تأسياً بأئمة هذه الأمة، ومخافة أن يُفهم من إحدى هذه العبارات ما لا يجوز؛ فهو من باب سَدِّ الذرائع. محي.
٣١٦
Section on Divine Matters. 42 - So every text that indicates temporality, carry it upon the word that has indicated. Then he pointed to the interpretation of what gave the false impression of temporality by his saying: And when you realize what preceded, (so every text) (1) i.e., apparent (from the Book and Sunnah) (that indicates temporality) i.e., indicates that the Quran is temporal or that Allah's speech is temporal, (carry it upon the word that has indicated). (1) He intended by this speech to refute what the Mu'tazila who say that the Quran is created or temporal cling to. For the majority of them used to say the Quran is created, and the trial we spoke about some of it became famous as the trial of 'saying the creation of the Quran'. But Muhammad al-Balkhi – and he was also from the Mu'tazila – used to avoid the word creation and insist on using the expression of temporality of the Quran, claiming that the word creation suggests fabrication, which is lying, because the root is one. So he is like one who fled from the rain and stood under the waterspout, because creation and temporality are synonymous. Exalted is Allah above what the falsifiers say, greatly! And the meaning is that every text in the noble Book and Prophetic Sunnah that apparently indicates that Allah's speech is temporal or that the Quran is temporal, it is obligatory upon the responsible person to carry it upon the meaning of the word sent down upon our Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, the recitation of which is an act of worship and which challenges with the shortest surah of it. Such as His saying: 'Indeed, We sent it down in the Night of Decree' [al-Qadr: 1] and His saying: 'Indeed, We have sent down the Remembrance, and indeed, We will preserve it' [al-Hijr: 9] and His saying: 'There does not come to them any new reminder from their Lord except they listen to it while they are at play, with hearts occupied' [al-Anbiya: 2-3]. And what the scholars mentioned is that Allah created the Quran in the Preserved Tablet, then sent it down to the heaven of the world in a place called the House of Might, and this is what is indicated by His saying: 'Indeed, We sent it down in the Night of Decree' [al-Qadr: 1] i.e., the blessed night of great importance. Then He would reveal to Gabriel to bring down what His will required to be sent down upon the noble Messenger, peace be upon him, so Gabriel conveyed it to the Messenger of Allah piecemeal according to the requirements of circumstances and events. The conclusion: It is befitting for the responsible person to carry every statement in the Quran or Sunnah that apparently indicates the temporality of the Quran or temporality of Allah's speech upon the recited word, not upon the internal speech, because it is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence. And that it is not permissible to say 'the Quran is created' or 'the Quran is created' or 'Allah's speech is temporal' or 'Allah's speech is created', even if intending the recited word, except in a teaching context, following the Imams of this nation, and for fear that one of these expressions might be understood in an impermissible sense; for it falls under the principle of blocking the means to harm.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage provides the hermeneutical principle for interpreting scriptural verses that seem to indicate the Quran is created or temporal. It begins by stating that any text that apparently indicates temporality should be interpreted as referring to the recited words (al-lafz al-mutlu). The passage then refutes the Mu'tazila who used such verses to argue that the Quran is created. It mentions a sectarian nuance: some Mu'tazila like Muhammad al-Balkhi insisted on using the term 'temporal' instead of 'created', but the author notes that both terms are synonymous and thus the evasion is futile. Then the passage lists examples of verses that appear to indicate temporality, such as those about sending down the Quran. The scholars explain that Allah created the Quran in the Preserved Tablet, then sent it down to the lower heaven, and then Gabriel revealed it to the Prophet piecemeal. Thus, the createdness applies to the physical text, not the eternal attribute. The conclusion reiterates that all such verses must be carried on the recited words, and that it is forbidden to use ambiguous phrases like 'the Quran is created' or 'Allah's speech is created' except in teaching contexts, following the Imams and to block the means to misunderstanding.

Key Terms
نص (text)
حدوث (temporality)
لفظ (word)
كلام نفسي (internal speech)
تنزيل (sending down)
اللوح المحفوظ (Preserved Tablet)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran is created because verses say it was sent down or is a 'new reminder'.
Correction: Those verses refer to the recited words and their revelation, not to Allah's eternal attribute of speech.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what must one do when encountering a Quranic verse that seems to say the Quran is temporal?
A) Reject the verse.
B) Interpret it as referring to the eternal attribute.
C) Interpret it as referring to the recited words.
D) Accept it literally as indicating the Quran is created.

Key Takeaway
All verses that seem to indicate the Quran's temporality must be interpreted as referring to the created recited words, not Allah's eternal attribute of speech.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite a verse that speaks of the Quran being 'sent down,' does your heart immediately affirm that this refers only to the physical words, not to Allah's eternal speech? Or do you sometimes feel a subtle doubt about the Quran's eternity? What would it mean for your trust in Allah's speech if you confused the two?
?
The passage prohibits saying 'the Quran is created' even in private unless teaching with clarification. Are there theological statements you casually make that could lead others to misunderstand a core belief? How can you guard your tongue to avoid causing confusion about Allah's attributes?
?
Sanusi's principle protects the believer from falling into the error of the Mu'tazila. Reflect on a time when you encountered a verse that seemed to suggest the Quran is temporal. Did you interpret it correctly, or did you feel unsettled? How can you train yourself to apply this hermeneutic rule whenever you read such verses?

The Eternity of Allah's Speech and Interpreting Apparent Verses
Al-Sanusi affirms the eternity of Allah's speech and explains the hermeneutic rule for verses of temporality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni doctrine that Allah's speech is eternal and how to interpret Quranic verses that seem to indicate it is created.

Core Idea
Allah's speech is eternal; the created Quran is its uttered expression.

A fundamental principle of Sunni theology is that Allah's attribute of speech is eternal. However, the Quran we recite is composed of words and letters that are created. This lesson clarifies how to reconcile verses that speak of the Quran being 'sent down' with the belief in its eternity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on eternal speech
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Notice that the author begins by asserting the Sunni position in contrast to the Mu'tazila.
The Mu'tazila claimed the Quran is created in every sense.
2
Identify the interpretation rule
The author explains that any verse indicating temporality (like 'We sent it down') is to be understood as referring to the uttered expression (al-lafẓ), not the eternal attribute.
This preserves the eternity of Allah's attribute of speech.
3
Reflect on the significance
Think about why this distinction matters for Sunni theology. It allows Muslims to affirm both the eternal nature of Allah's speech and the historical reality of revelation.

فائدة: مذهب الإمام الأشعري والقاضي الباقلاني ومن تبعهما أن لا تفاضل بين سور القرآن الكريم وآياته ، والأحاديثُ المصرحة بذلك كـ: «يس قلب القرآن» إن صحت حملت على زيادة الأجر ، وهي لا تستلزم الأفضلية، أو على ما هو الأنفع والأليق بحسب أحوال العباد.
The speech of Allah the Exalted is eternal according to the People of the Sunnah, contrary to the Mu'tazila who say the Quran is created, such as: 'Indeed, We sent it down in the Night of Decree' (al-Qadr 1), 'Indeed, We sent down the Reminder' (al-Hijr 9). (Carry) O Sunni (upon the Quran in the sense of the) utterance sent down upon our Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) (which indeed indicates) that eternal attribute subsisting in Him, meaning that every apparent [text] from the Book and the Sunnah that came indicating the temporality of the speech of Allah the Exalted is interpreted by us as that which is described thereby is only the utterance indicating the internal speech (1), not the internal meaning, eternal, subsisting in His essence Exalted; because there is no dispute in the application of the two terms 'the Quran' and 'the speech of Allah' either by way of homonymy, and it is the preponderant (2), or metaphor and reality - to this created composition (3), as is customary among the common people, reciters, and fundamentalists; and to it refer the particular properties that are attributes of letters and accidents of words. And the speech of Allah the Exalted in this sense: reminder, created, Arabic, sent down upon the Prophet, recited, arranged, eloquent, powerful, miraculous, comprising sections and beginnings and other than that (1). Benefit: The school of Imam al-Ash'ari and Qadi al-Baqillani and those who follow them is that there is no superiority among the surahs of the Noble Quran and its verses, and the hadiths explicitly stating that, like 'Yasin is the heart of the Quran,' if authentic, are interpreted as indicating increase of reward, which does not entail superiority, or as what is more beneficial and suitable according to the states of the servants.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the Sunni position on the nature of the Quran. The author begins by affirming that Allah's speech is eternal, contrary to the Mu'tazila who claim the Quran is created. He then addresses verses that seem to indicate the Quran's creation, such as 'Indeed, We sent it down in the Night of Decree.' He explains that such verses are to be interpreted as referring to the uttered expression (al-lafẓ) that was sent down, not to the eternal attribute of speech. The utterance points to the eternal attribute. He emphasizes that every apparent text indicating temporality is applied to the expression that indicates the internal speech (al-kalām al-nafsī), not to the eternal meaning. He then discusses the application of the terms 'Quran' and 'speech of Allah,' stating that there is no disagreement about using them either by homonymy (ishtirāk) or by metaphor and reality. He notes that the preponderant view is homonymy. The commentary includes a footnote explaining that Imam Ahmad forbade saying 'my utterance of the Quran is created' due to possible misunderstanding, though it is correct in itself. The footnote also narrates the story of al-Karābīsī and Dāwūd al-Asbahānī. Another footnote explains the preponderance of homonymy, citing that calling a sura 'not the speech of Allah' constitutes disbelief. The third footnote discusses the ordering of metaphor and reality, concluding that the term 'Kalam Allah' (speech of Allah) is a reality for the internal meaning and a metaphor for the uttered, while 'Quran' is the opposite. The passage then lists the attributes of the created Quran (e.g., created, Arabic, sent down, recited) and includes a benefit about the Ash'ari position that there is no essential superiority among surahs, only in reward or benefit.

قديم
حدوث
اللفظ
المعنى النفسي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the Quran itself (the words and letters) is eternal, or that the verses indicating sent-down contradict the eternity of Allah's speech.
Correction: The correct Sunni view is that Allah's attribute of speech is eternal, while the uttered expression (the Quran we recite) is created. Verses about sending down refer to the utterance, not the attribute.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct interpretation of verses that seem to indicate the Quran was sent down?
A) They refer to the eternal attribute of speech directly.
B) They refer to the created uttered expression, not the eternal attribute.
C) They are metaphorical and have no real meaning.
D) They indicate that the Quran is created in every sense.

Key Takeaway
Allah's speech is eternal; the created Quran is its uttered expression.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you pause to consider that the very words you utter are a temporal creation pointing to an eternal reality? How does that distinction affect the reverence you bring to your recitation? This week, before you begin reciting, silently acknowledge that you are about to voice a created expression that indicates an uncreated attribute.
?
You have learned that verses like 'We sent it down' are interpreted as referring to the utterance, not the attribute. But knowing this intellectually does not guarantee it sinks into your heart. Have you ever felt a subconscious doubt about the Quran's eternity when reading such verses? What would it take for you to embrace this distinction not just as a theological formula but as a living conviction that shapes your relationship with the Quran?
?
The Mu'tazila stumbled because they took the apparent meaning of revelation verses at face value. Are there areas in your own faith where you are too literalist, missing the deeper eternal reality? Identify one belief or practice where you might be over-focusing on the created form and neglecting the eternal significance, and commit to reflecting on that this week.

Terms 'Quran' and 'Kalam Allah': Homonymy or Metaphor?
The commentator discusses the dual application of 'Quran' and 'Kalam Allah' and lists the attributes of the created Quran, followed by a benefit on surah superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sunni scholars apply the terms 'Quran' and 'Kalam Allah' to both the eternal attribute and the created composition, and the Ash'ari position on the superiority of surahs.

Core Idea
The Quran's words are created, but 'Kalam Allah' applies to the eternal attribute.

While the Quran we recite is a created composition of words and letters, Sunni theology distinguishes between the eternal attribute of speech and its uttered expression. This lesson explains how the same word 'Quran' can refer to both the eternal and the temporal, and concludes with the Ash'ari view that no sura is essentially superior to another.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on terminology
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Focus on the two ways the terms are used: homonymy (ishtirāk) or metaphor (majāz) and reality (ḥaqīqah).
Homonymy means the same word has two separate meanings.
2
Note the attributes of the created Quran
The passage lists eleven attributes of the Quran as created composition (e.g., created, Arabic, sent down). Identify them.
This list shows how the Quran shares properties with other created things.
3
Consider the benefit on surah superiority
The author states the Ash'ari position that no sura is essentially superior to another. Hadiths like 'Yasin is the heart of the Quran' are explained as indicating increased reward, not essential excellence.

(1) قوله : (المتصف بذلك إنما هو (اللفظ لكن منع الإمام أحمد أن يقال: لفظي بالقرآن حادث ، وإن كان صحيحاً في نفسه ؛ لكنه ربما أوهم، وقد يُلبّسُ به المبتدع، ذكر ابن حجر في «فتح الباري أول من قال لفظي بالقرآن مخلوق : الحسين بن علي الكرابيسي أحد أصحاب الإمام الشافعي، فلما بلغ ذلك الإمام أحمد بدعه وهجره، ثم قال بذلك داود الأصبهاني رأس الظاهرية وهو يومئذ بنيسابور ، فأنكر عليه إسحاق ، وبلغ ذلك أحمد فلما قدم بغداد لم يأذن له بالدخول عليه . نعم يجوز ذلك في مقام التعليم فقط . الأمير . (۲) قوله: (وهو الأرجح) بدليل كفر من قال: هذه السورة ليست كلام الله. على أنَّ الأصل في الإطلاق الحقيقة الأمير .
(۳) قوله: (أو المجاز والحقيقة على هذا المؤلف الحادث في العبارة حذف الواو وما عطفت عليه، والتقدير على هذا المؤلف الحادث والمعنى القديم وهو من باب اللف والنشر
:
المشوش ، فالحقيقة للمعنى القديم، والمجاز للفظ الحادث، لكن إطلاق القرآن على اللفظي أشهر من إطلاقه على النفسي ، وكلامه بالعكس . اهـ ملوي والظاهر : أنه مرتب ، والحاصل أن الذي ينبغي : أنّ المجاز راجع لعنوان كلام الله تعالى؛ فإنه قيل: إنه حقيقة في النفسي مجاز في اللفظي المؤلف، والحقيقة راجعة لعنوان القرآن فإنه قيل: حقيقة في المؤلف الحادث وفي القديم مجاز ، فكلا القولين يقابلان الاشتراك فيهما الذي ذكره أولا ، فتدبر المقال وافهمه على هذا المنوال ودع عنك ما قيل أو يقال ، ولا تنظر لمن قال . الأمير. وعند الشنواني ومحصل الأقوال في وضع القرآن وكلام الله لأي شيء وضع ثلاثة: فقيل:=
قسم الإلهيات
العامة والقُرَّاء والأصوليين، وإليه ترجع الخواص التي هي من صفات الحروف وعَوارِض الألفاظ، وكلام الله تعالى بهذا المعنى : ذِكْرُ ، ومُحْدَثُ، وَعَرَبيٌّ ، ومُنزَّلٌ على النبي ، ومتلو ، ومُرتَبٌ ، وفَصيح ، وبَليغ ، ومُعْجِزْ ، النَّبيِّ ومُسْتمِلٌ على مقاطع ومبادئ وغير ذلك (۱)
فائدة: مذهب الإمام الأشعري والقاضي الباقلاني ومن تبعهما أن لا تفاضل بين سور القرآن الكريم وآياته ، والأحاديثُ المصرحة بذلك كـ: «يس قلب القرآن» إن صحت حملت على زيادة الأجر ، وهي لا تستلزم الأفضلية، أو على ما هو الأنفع والأليق بحسب أحوال العباد.
The speech of Allah the Exalted is eternal according to the People of the Sunnah, contrary to the Mu'tazila who say the Quran is created, such as: 'Indeed, We sent it down in the Night of Decree' (al-Qadr 1), 'Indeed, We sent down the Reminder' (al-Hijr 9). (Carry) O Sunni (upon the Quran in the sense of the) utterance sent down upon our Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) (which indeed indicates) that eternal attribute subsisting in Him, meaning that every apparent [text] from the Book and the Sunnah that came indicating the temporality of the speech of Allah the Exalted is interpreted by us as that which is described thereby is only the utterance indicating the internal speech (1), not the internal meaning, eternal, subsisting in His essence Exalted; because there is no dispute in the application of the two terms 'the Quran' and 'the speech of Allah' either by way of homonymy, and it is the preponderant (2), or metaphor and reality - to this created composition (3), as is customary among the common people, reciters, and fundamentalists; and to it refer the particular properties that are attributes of letters and accidents of words. And the speech of Allah the Exalted in this sense: reminder, created, Arabic, sent down upon the Prophet, recited, arranged, eloquent, powerful, miraculous, comprising sections and beginnings and other than that (1). Benefit: The school of Imam al-Ash'ari and Qadi al-Baqillani and those who follow them is that there is no superiority among the surahs of the Noble Quran and its verses, and the hadiths explicitly stating that, like 'Yasin is the heart of the Quran,' if authentic, are interpreted as indicating increase of reward, which does not entail superiority, or as what is more beneficial and suitable according to the states of the servants.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the Sunni position on the nature of the Quran. The author begins by affirming that Allah's speech is eternal, contrary to the Mu'tazila who claim the Quran is created. He then addresses verses that seem to indicate the Quran's creation, such as 'Indeed, We sent it down in the Night of Decree.' He explains that such verses are to be interpreted as referring to the uttered expression (al-lafẓ) that was sent down, not to the eternal attribute of speech. The utterance points to the eternal attribute. He emphasizes that every apparent text indicating temporality is applied to the expression that indicates the internal speech (al-kalām al-nafsī), not to the eternal meaning. He then discusses the application of the terms 'Quran' and 'speech of Allah,' stating that there is no disagreement about using them either by homonymy (ishtirāk) or by metaphor and reality. He notes that the preponderant view is homonymy. The commentary includes a footnote explaining that Imam Ahmad forbade saying 'my utterance of the Quran is created' due to possible misunderstanding, though it is correct in itself. The footnote also narrates the story of al-Karābīsī and Dāwūd al-Asbahānī. Another footnote explains the preponderance of homonymy, citing that calling a sura 'not the speech of Allah' constitutes disbelief. The third footnote discusses the ordering of metaphor and reality, concluding that the term 'Kalam Allah' (speech of Allah) is a reality for the internal meaning and a metaphor for the uttered, while 'Quran' is the opposite. The passage then lists the attributes of the created Quran (e.g., created, Arabic, sent down, recited) and includes a benefit about the Ash'ari position that there is no essential superiority among surahs, only in reward or benefit.

كلام الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that some surahs (e.g., Yasin) are essentially superior to others in the Quran.
Correction: The Ash'ari school teaches that no sura is essentially superior; hadiths like 'Yasin is the heart of the Quran' refer to greater reward or benefit, not ontological superiority.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how are hadiths like 'Yasin is the heart of the Quran' interpreted in the Ash'ari school?
A) They are rejected as inauthentic.
B) They indicate that Yasin is essentially superior.
C) They indicate increased reward, not essential superiority.
D) They refer to the eternal attribute of speech.

Key Takeaway
The term 'Quran' can refer to both the eternal attribute and the created composition; and no sura is essentially superior to any other.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, are you conscious of the distinction between the eternal attribute of speech and the created composition you utter? How might this awareness deepen your reverence in recitation?
?
You may have a favorite surah you recite more often. Does the lesson's assertion that no surah is essentially superior challenge that practice? How will you internalize that all surahs are equal in merit, while still appreciating their unique rewards?
?
The term 'Quran' applies to both the eternal and temporal realities. Which meaning dominates your perception when you say, 'I am reading the Quran'? How can you hold both meanings in mind to enrich your experience of every ayah?

Attributes of Allah's Speech and Equality of Surahs
Attributes of divine speech and equality of surahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific attributes of Allah's speech as the revealed Quran and the Ash'ari position on the non-superiority of surahs.

Core Idea
Allah's speech as Quran is both timeless and created, and no surah is inherently superior.

This passage from Ithaaf al-Mureed elaborates on the nature of Allah's speech when it descends as a revealed text. It lists its properties and then clarifies a key Ash'ari teaching about the equality of all Quranic verses.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the list of attributes and the separate 'benefit' section.
2
Identify the list of attributes
The passage presents a series of attributes for Allah's speech in this sense. Find each one and note how they describe the revealed Quran.
The attributes include being created, Arabic, revealed, etc.
3
Understand the benefit on superiority
Read the second part carefully. It states the Ash'ari doctrine that no surah or verse is inherently superior. Note how the hadith about 'Ya-Seen is the heart of the Quran' is interpreted.
The hadith is explained as referring to increase in reward or suitability.
4
Reflect on the overall teaching
Ask yourself why these details matter. This passage helps distinguish between the eternal attribute of speech and its temporal manifestation, and safeguards against misunderstanding the equality of Quranic text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم الإلهيات العامة والقُرَّاء والأصوليين، وإليه ترجع الخواص التي هي من صفات الحروف وعَوارِض الألفاظ، وكلام الله تعالى بهذا المعنى : ذِكْرُ ، ومُحْدَثُ، وَعَرَبيٌّ ، ومُنزَّلٌ على النبي ، ومتلو ، ومُرتَبٌ ، وفَصيح ، وبَليغ ، ومُعْجِزْ ، النَّبيِّ ومُسْتمِلٌ على مقاطع ومبادئ وغير ذلك (۱) فائدة: مذهب الإمام الأشعري والقاضي الباقلاني ومن تبعهما أن لا تفاضل بين سور القرآن الكريم وآياته ، والأحاديثُ المصرحة بذلك كـ: «يس قلب القرآن» إن صحت حملت على زيادة الأجر، وهي لا تستلزم الأفضلية، أو على ما هو الأنفع والأليق بحسب أحوال العباد.
The division of Ilahiyyat: the general, the Qurra' and the Usuliyyun; and to it refer the properties that are from the attributes of letters and accidents of words. And the speech of Allah the Exalted in this sense is: remembrance, created, Arabic, revealed to the Prophet, recited, arranged, eloquent, miraculous, prophetic, and including sections and principles and other than that. (1) Benefit: The doctrine of Imam Ash'ari and Qadi Baqillani and those who follow them is that there is no superiority among the surahs of the Noble Quran and its verses; and the hadiths explicitly stating that, like: 'Ya-Seen is the heart of the Quran,' if authentic, are interpreted as indicating an increase in reward, which does not entail superiority, or as referring to what is more beneficial and suitable according to the states of the servants.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification. It begins by stating the division of Ilahiyyat (divine matters) and then discusses the attribute of speech (kalam). It states that the word kalam in this context includes specific properties related to the letters and the accidents of words. The speech of Allah in this sense is described as being 'remembrance, created, Arabic, revealed to the Prophet, recited, arranged, eloquent, miraculous, prophetic, and including sections and principles, etc.' This list indicates the characteristics of the revealed Quran. Then a benefit is added: the Ash'ari school holds that there is no inherent superiority among the surahs and verses of the Quran. Hadiths that seem to indicate superiority, like 'Ya-Seen is the heart of the Quran,' are understood as referring to an increase in reward for certain recitations, not that the verse itself is ontologically superior. This nuance guards against misunderstanding the nature of the Quran as the word of Allah.

Correction: The Ash'ari interpretation is that such hadiths indicate an increase in reward or benefit for the reciter, not an inherent ontological superiority of one verse over another.

Checkpoint

B) No surah is superior to another.
C) Surah Ya-Seen is the best.
D) The Quran is created.

Key Takeaway
The revealed Quran is Allah's speech in a literal sense but carries attributes of limitation (created, Arabic, etc.), and all its verses are equal in essential value.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you secretly treat certain surahs as 'more powerful' or 'more spiritual' than others, perhaps reciting Surah Ya-Seen for specific needs while ignoring others? How does the Ash'ari doctrine of equality challenge your practice—and what would change if you truly believed no surah is inherently superior?
?

But do you actually experience it as the speech of Allah, or do your habits reduce it to a routine of sounds and meanings? What would it mean for you to approach each verse with the same awe, knowing it carries the same divine origin as every other verse?
?
The passage lists attributes like 'remembrance,' 'Arabic,' 'revealed,' 'prophetic.' Which of these attributes do you neglect in your relationship with the Quran? For example, do you treat it as a reminder (remembrance) that should transform your heart, or just as a text to be recited? Choose one attribute you struggle with and commit to one concrete action to live it today.

The Meaning of Opposite (ḍidd) in Divine Attributes
Clarifies the meaning of 'opposite' and states the general rule of impossibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two meanings of 'opposite' (ḍidd) and why the linguistic meaning is used when referring to what is impossible for Allah.

Core Idea
The impossible for Allah is not just existential opposites but everything incompatible with His perfection.

This lesson begins by establishing the general rule: it is obligatory to believe that every opposite of the necessary attributes is impossible for Allah. The commentator then clarifies the crucial distinction between the customary and linguistic meanings of 'opposite', explaining that the linguistic sense includes non-existential opposites like annihilation.

Guided Path
1
Read the general rule
Read the opening sentence: 'And it is what is impossible in His right...' Understand that the opposites of all the preceding attributes are impossible for Allah.
The 'preceding attributes' refer to the necessary attributes like existence, pre-eternity, etc.
2
Identify the two meanings of 'opposite'
The commentator presents the customary meaning (an existential thing that cannot coexist with its opposite) and the linguistic meaning (any contradictory, whether existential or non-existential). Note why the linguistic meaning is chosen.
Because some impossible things, like annihilation, are non-existential.
3
Reflect on the application
Consider how this understanding of 'opposite' applies to the first impossibility mentioned: non-existence. Ask yourself why non-existence is considered an opposite of existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو ما يستحيل في حقه، فقال: ويجب شرعًا أن يعتقد أنه يستحيل عليه سبحانه ضد ذي الصفات من الصفات المتقدمة بأسرها، نفسية كانت أو سلبية، معاني كانت أو معنوية، في حقه أي في الحكم الواجب له تعالى؛ فلا يتصور في العقل ثبوت شيء من أضدادها له تعالى؛ إذ المستحيل: ما لا يتصور في العقل ثبوته. الضد له معنيان: أحدهما عرفي، والآخر لغوي. فأما معناه العرفي فهو: الأمر الوجودي الذي لا يجتمع مع ضده، وقد يرتفع هو وضده ولا تصح إرادة هذا المعنى في هذا الموضع؛ لأن من الأضداد المستحيلة في حقه تعالى ما ليس وجوديًّا كالفناء. وأما المعنى اللغوي: فالضد يطلق لغة على مطلق المنافي، سواء أكان وجوديًّا أم كان عدميًّا، وهذا المعنى هو الذي تصح إرادته هنا. فيستحيل عليه تعالى العدم، وهو ضد الوجود، ويستحيل عليه الحدوث وهو ضد القدم، ويستحيل عليه الفناء، أي: طرو العدم، وهو ضد البقاء، ويستحيل عليه المماثلة للحوادث، وهو ضد المخالفة للحوادث، والمماثلة المستحيلة تصور بأن يكون جرما سواء أكان مركبا ويسمى جسما أم كان غير مركب ويسمى جوهرا فردا، أو بأن يكون عرضا يقوم بالجرم، أو بأن يكون في جهة للجرم؛ فليس فوق العرش ولا تحته ولا عن يمينه ولا شماله عن ذلك، وقد عرفت مذهب الخلف والسلف في بيان معنى قوله تعالى: {الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى} [طه: ٥] أو بأن يكون في مكان ما أو يتقيد بالزمان، وقد ذكرنا تفصيل ذلك في الكلام على إثبات مخالفته تعالى للحوادث. ويستحيل عليه ألا يكون قائما بنفسه بأن يحتاج إلى محل يقوم به أو مخصص، وهو ضد قيامه بنفسه. ويستحيل عليه أن لا يكون واحدا، بأن يكون مركبا في ذاته، أو يكون له مماثل في ذاته، أو يكون له في صفاته تعدد من نوع واحد، كقدرتين وإرادتين، أو يكون لأحد صفة تشبه صفته، أو يكون معه في الوجود مؤثر في فعل من الأفعال، وهذا كله ضد الوحدانية. ويستحيل عليه أن يكون عاجزا عن ممكن ما، وهذا ضد القدرة. ويستحيل عليه أن يوجد أو يعدم شيئا من العالم مع كراهيته أو مع الذهول أو الغفلة، وهذا ضد الإرادة. ويستحيل عليه الجهل وما في معناه كالظن والشك والوهم والنوم، وهذا ضد العلم. ويستحيل عليه الموت، وهذا ضد الحياة. ويستحيل عليه البكم النفسي، وهو ضد الكلام. ويستحيل عليه العمى، وهو ضد البصر. ويستحيل عليه أيضا كونه عاجزا، وكونه مكرها، وكونه جاهلا... إلخ، وهي أضداد الصفات المعنوية.
And it is what is impossible in His right, so he said: And it is obligatory by law to believe that it is impossible for Him, exalted, the opposite of the attributes possessing the attributes from all the preceding attributes, whether psychic or negative, whether meanings or meaningful, in His right meaning in the judgment obligatory for Him, exalted; so it is not conceivable in the mind the establishment of anything from their opposites for Him, exalted; since the impossible is: what is not conceivable in the mind its establishment. The opposite has two meanings: one customary and the other linguistic. As for its customary meaning, it is: the existential thing that does not coexist with its opposite, and both it and its opposite may be absent, and it is not correct to intend this meaning in this place; because among the opposites impossible in His right, exalted, is what is not existential like annihilation. As for the linguistic meaning: the opposite is applied linguistically to any contradictory, whether it is existential or non-existential, and this meaning is what is correct to intend here. So it is impossible for Him, exalted, non-existence, which is the opposite of existence, and it is impossible for Him origination which is the opposite of pre-eternity, and it is impossible for Him annihilation, i.e., the occurrence of non-existence, which is the opposite of permanence, and it is impossible for Him similarity to originated things, which is the opposite of dissimilarity to originated things, and the impossible similarity is conceived as being a body, whether it is composite and called a body or non-composite and called an individual substance, or as being an accident subsisting in the body, or as being in a direction of the body; for He is not above the Throne nor below it nor to its right nor to its left beyond that, and you have known the school of the later and earlier scholars in explaining the meaning of His saying, the Most High: {The Most Merciful established Himself over the Throne} [Ta-Ha: 5] or as being in a place or being restricted by time, and we have mentioned the details of that in the discussion on proving His, exalted, dissimilarity to originated things. And it is impossible for Him not to be self-subsistent by needing a substrate to subsist in or a determiner, and it is the opposite of His self-subsistence. And it is impossible for Him not to be one, by being composite in His essence, or having a similar in His essence, or having multiplicity in His attributes of one type, like two powers and two wills, or someone having an attribute resembling His attribute, or there being with Him in existence an agent in any action, and all of this is the opposite of oneness. And it is impossible for Him to be incapable of any possible thing, and this is the opposite of power. And it is impossible for Him to bring into existence or annihilate anything from the world with dislike or with heedlessness or negligence, and this is the opposite of will. And it is impossible for Him ignorance and its like such as suspicion and doubt and illusion and sleep, and this is the opposite of knowledge. And it is impossible for Him death, and this is the opposite of life. And it is impossible for Him psychological muteness, and it is the opposite of speech. And it is impossible for Him blindness, and it is the opposite of sight. And it is impossible for Him also being incapable, and being coerced, and being ignorant... etc., and they are the opposites of the meaningful attributes.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of the attributes impossible for Allah (the Mustahilat), based on the commentary on al-Laqqani's poem. The commentator first states the general rule: it is obligatory by law to believe that every opposite of the attributes (the necessary attributes) is impossible for Allah. He distinguishes between the customary and linguistic meanings of 'opposite' (ḍidd), explaining that here the linguistic meaning is intended because some opposites are non-existential (like annihilation). He then provides a detailed list of impossibilities: non-existence (opposite of existence), origination (opposite of pre-eternity), annihilation (opposite of permanence), similarity to originated things (opposite of dissimilarity), being a body, accident, or occupying direction; not being self-subsistent (i.e., needing a substrate or determiner); not being one (composite, having a similar, multiplicity in attributes like two powers, having an attribute resembling His, or having another agent in existence); being incapable (opposite of power); acting with dislike or heedlessness (opposite of will); ignorance and its equivalents (opposite of knowledge); death (opposite of life); psychological muteness (opposite of speech); blindness (opposite of sight); and being incapable, coerced, or ignorant (opposites of the meaningful attributes). Each item is paired with its opposite necessary attribute, showing that the divine attributes of necessity (Wajibat) imply the negation of their opposites.

Key Terms

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: People might think that only existential attributes are impossible for Allah.
Correction: The commentator explains that the linguistic meaning of 'opposite' includes non-existential things like annihilation, so even non-existential impossibilities are covered.

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator reject the customary meaning of 'opposite' in this context?
A) Because it is linguistically incorrect.
B) Because it excludes non-existential opposites like annihilation.
C) Because it is too broad.
D) Because it contradicts the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The term 'opposite' (ḍidd) when applied to Allah must be understood in its linguistic sense to encompass both existential and non-existential impossibilities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that annihilation (fanā’) is impossible for Allah, or do you sometimes subconsciously imagine a time when Allah might cease to exist? If the latter, how will you uproot that thought from your heart today?
?
When you reflect on your own understanding of Allah’s attributes, are there any ‘opposites’ you implicitly attribute to Him—like weakness, ignorance, or change—that contradict His perfection? What specific step will you take to replace that with correct belief?
?
The passage says it is obligatory to believe that all opposites are impossible for Allah. Are there areas of your life where you act as if Allah’s power is limited, for example by worrying excessively as if something can happen outside His will? How can you realign your actions with this belief?

Enumeration of Attributes Impossible for Allah
Enumerates all attributes impossible for Allah, each paired with its opposite necessary attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the specific attributes that are impossible for Allah and understand how each relates to its opposite necessary attribute.

Core Idea
Allah is free from non-existence, origination, annihilation, similarity to creation, and every imperfection.

Building on the general principle, this lesson presents the detailed list of what is impossible for Allah. For each item, the commentator states the impossibility and pairs it with the corresponding necessary attribute. This enumeration helps solidify the doctrine of tanzih (divine transcendence).

Guided Path
1
Read the list of impossibilities
Read through the Arabic passage from 'فيستحيل عليه تعالى العدم' to the end. Each sentence states an impossible attribute and its opposite necessary attribute.
Notice the pattern: 'It is impossible for Him X, which is the opposite of Y.'
2
Categorize the impossibilities
Group them into: (1) ontological impossibilities (non-existence, origination, annihilation), (2) relational (similarity to creation, needing a substrate), (3) attribute opposites (ignorance, death, etc.).
3
Reflect on divine oneness
Note the detailed explanation under oneness (wāḥidiyya): it includes composition, having a similar, multiple attributes, and having partners in action.
This reinforces the concept of tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو ما يستحيل في حقه، فقال: ويجب شرعًا أن يعتقد أنه يستحيل عليه سبحانه ضد ذي الصفات من الصفات المتقدمة بأسرها، نفسية كانت أو سلبية، معاني كانت أو معنوية، في حقه أي في الحكم الواجب له تعالى؛ فلا يتصور في العقل ثبوت شيء من أضدادها له تعالى؛ إذ المستحيل: ما لا يتصور في العقل ثبوته. الضد له معنيان: أحدهما عرفي، والآخر لغوي. فأما معناه العرفي فهو: الأمر الوجودي الذي لا يجتمع مع ضده، وقد يرتفع هو وضده ولا تصح إرادة هذا المعنى في هذا الموضع؛ لأن من الأضداد المستحيلة في حقه تعالى ما ليس وجوديًّا كالفناء. وأما المعنى اللغوي: فالضد يطلق لغة على مطلق المنافي، سواء أكان وجوديًّا أم كان عدميًّا، وهذا المعنى هو الذي تصح إرادته هنا. فيستحيل عليه تعالى العدم، وهو ضد الوجود، ويستحيل عليه الحدوث وهو ضد القدم، ويستحيل عليه الفناء، أي: طرو العدم، وهو ضد البقاء، ويستحيل عليه المماثلة للحوادث، وهو ضد المخالفة للحوادث، والمماثلة المستحيلة تصور بأن يكون جرما سواء أكان مركبا ويسمى جسما أم كان غير مركب ويسمى جوهرا فردا، أو بأن يكون عرضا يقوم بالجرم، أو بأن يكون في جهة للجرم؛ فليس فوق العرش ولا تحته ولا عن يمينه ولا شماله عن ذلك، وقد عرفت مذهب الخلف والسلف في بيان معنى قوله تعالى: {الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى} [طه: ٥] أو بأن يكون في مكان ما أو يتقيد بالزمان، وقد ذكرنا تفصيل ذلك في الكلام على إثبات مخالفته تعالى للحوادث. ويستحيل عليه ألا يكون قائما بنفسه بأن يحتاج إلى محل يقوم به أو مخصص، وهو ضد قيامه بنفسه. ويستحيل عليه أن لا يكون واحدا، بأن يكون مركبا في ذاته، أو يكون له مماثل في ذاته، أو يكون له في صفاته تعدد من نوع واحد، كقدرتين وإرادتين، أو يكون لأحد صفة تشبه صفته، أو يكون معه في الوجود مؤثر في فعل من الأفعال، وهذا كله ضد الوحدانية. ويستحيل عليه أن يكون عاجزا عن ممكن ما، وهذا ضد القدرة. ويستحيل عليه أن يوجد أو يعدم شيئا من العالم مع كراهيته أو مع الذهول أو الغفلة، وهذا ضد الإرادة. ويستحيل عليه الجهل وما في معناه كالظن والشك والوهم والنوم، وهذا ضد العلم. ويستحيل عليه الموت، وهذا ضد الحياة. ويستحيل عليه البكم النفسي، وهو ضد الكلام. ويستحيل عليه العمى، وهو ضد البصر. ويستحيل عليه أيضا كونه عاجزا، وكونه مكرها، وكونه جاهلا... إلخ، وهي أضداد الصفات المعنوية.
And it is what is impossible in His right, so he said: And it is obligatory by law to believe that it is impossible for Him, exalted, the opposite of the attributes possessing the attributes from all the preceding attributes, whether psychic or negative, whether meanings or meaningful, in His right meaning in the judgment obligatory for Him, exalted; so it is not conceivable in the mind the establishment of anything from their opposites for Him, exalted; since the impossible is: what is not conceivable in the mind its establishment. The opposite has two meanings: one customary and the other linguistic. As for its customary meaning, it is: the existential thing that does not coexist with its opposite, and both it and its opposite may be absent, and it is not correct to intend this meaning in this place; because among the opposites impossible in His right, exalted, is what is not existential like annihilation. As for the linguistic meaning: the opposite is applied linguistically to any contradictory, whether it is existential or non-existential, and this meaning is what is correct to intend here. So it is impossible for Him, exalted, non-existence, which is the opposite of existence, and it is impossible for Him origination which is the opposite of pre-eternity, and it is impossible for Him annihilation, i.e., the occurrence of non-existence, which is the opposite of permanence, and it is impossible for Him similarity to originated things, which is the opposite of dissimilarity to originated things, and the impossible similarity is conceived as being a body, whether it is composite and called a body or non-composite and called an individual substance, or as being an accident subsisting in the body, or as being in a direction of the body; for He is not above the Throne nor below it nor to its right nor to its left beyond that, and you have known the school of the later and earlier scholars in explaining the meaning of His saying, the Most High: {The Most Merciful established Himself over the Throne} [Ta-Ha: 5] or as being in a place or being restricted by time, and we have mentioned the details of that in the discussion on proving His, exalted, dissimilarity to originated things. And it is impossible for Him not to be self-subsistent by needing a substrate to subsist in or a determiner, and it is the opposite of His self-subsistence. And it is impossible for Him not to be one, by being composite in His essence, or having a similar in His essence, or having multiplicity in His attributes of one type, like two powers and two wills, or someone having an attribute resembling His attribute, or there being with Him in existence an agent in any action, and all of this is the opposite of oneness. And it is impossible for Him to be incapable of any possible thing, and this is the opposite of power. And it is impossible for Him to bring into existence or annihilate anything from the world with dislike or with heedlessness or negligence, and this is the opposite of will. And it is impossible for Him ignorance and its like such as suspicion and doubt and illusion and sleep, and this is the opposite of knowledge. And it is impossible for Him death, and this is the opposite of life. And it is impossible for Him psychological muteness, and it is the opposite of speech. And it is impossible for Him blindness, and it is the opposite of sight. And it is impossible for Him also being incapable, and being coerced, and being ignorant... etc., and they are the opposites of the meaningful attributes.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of the attributes impossible for Allah (the Mustahilat), based on the commentary on al-Laqqani's poem. The commentator first states the general rule: it is obligatory by law to believe that every opposite of the attributes (the necessary attributes) is impossible for Allah. He distinguishes between the customary and linguistic meanings of 'opposite' (ḍidd), explaining that here the linguistic meaning is intended because some opposites are non-existential (like annihilation). He then provides a detailed list of impossibilities: non-existence (opposite of existence), origination (opposite of pre-eternity), annihilation (opposite of permanence), similarity to originated things (opposite of dissimilarity), being a body, accident, or occupying direction; not being self-subsistent (i.e., needing a substrate or determiner); not being one (composite, having a similar, multiplicity in attributes like two powers, having an attribute resembling His, or having another agent in existence); being incapable (opposite of power); acting with dislike or heedlessness (opposite of will); ignorance and its equivalents (opposite of knowledge); death (opposite of life); psychological muteness (opposite of speech); blindness (opposite of sight); and being incapable, coerced, or ignorant (opposites of the meaningful attributes). Each item is paired with its opposite necessary attribute, showing that the divine attributes of necessity (Wajibat) imply the negation of their opposites.
