God Creates All Actions and Grants Success
Introduces the doctrine that God creates all actions and clarifies its meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God is the sole Creator of all human actions and that success in reaching Him is a gift from His will alone.

Core Idea
God creates every action; success is by His will alone.

This lesson begins a new section on the creation of human actions. The author introduces the foundational belief that God is the Creator of both the servant and his deeds. He then addresses a potential confusion about the statement's apparent redundancy and clarifies its meaning through the word 'ma' indicating generality.

Guided Path
1
Read the matn and its explanation
Carefully read the Arabic line 'فَخَالِقُ لِعَبْدِهِ وَمَا عَمِلْ مُوَفِّقٌ لِمَنْ أَرَادَ أَنْ يَصِلْ' and the commentary that follows. Understand that this affirms God's creative power over all actions.
The commentary explains that this builds on the previous discussion of God's ability to bring into existence and annihilate.
2
Understand the objection and its answer
Some might say the statement 'the possible is possible' is redundant. Notice how the author uses the word 'ma' to show generality, meaning every possible thing is subject to God's power.
This refutes any claim that some possibilities are not under God's control.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this doctrine is important: it establishes that nothing in creation happens outside of God's will and power, including human actions.
This will be contrasted with the views of the Mu'tazila and Brahmins in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[مسألة خلق أفعالِ العِباد] ٤٥ . - فَخَالِقُ لِعَبْدِهِ وَمَا عَمِلْ مُوَفِّقٌ لِمَنْ أَرَادَ أَنْ يَصِلْ أشار إلى المسألة المُترجمة بخلق الأفعال ، مُفرّعًا على ما مرَّ مِن جهة إيجاده وإعدامه وإذا نظرتَ إلى هذا التقدير اندفع عندك ما يقال: إنه لا فائدة هذا ائدة في الإخبار ؛ لأنَّ المبتدأ والخبر شيء واحد، لأنَّ الجائز هو الممكن، والممكن هو الجائز، فكأنه قال: والجائز جائز في حقه تعالى أو قال والممكن ممكن في حقه تعالى. و«ما» في قوله: ((ما أمكنا» اسم موصول ، وهو دالّ على العموم، أي: أنه يجوز عليه تعالى إيجاد كل ممكن أو إعدامه ، وهذا الكلام يردُّ على طائفتين: الأولى: الذين يقولون بأنَّ بعض الأمور الممكنة واجبة عليه الله ، كالمعتزلة الذين ذهبوا إلى يجب عليه تعالى أن يفعل ما هو الصالح لعباده.. والطائفة الثانية: الذين ذهبوا إلى أن بعض الأمور المُمكنة مستحيلة عليه تعالى، كالبَرَاهِمَة الذين ذهبوا إلى أن بعثة الرسل مستحيلة، وسيأتي الكلام على كل واحدة من هاتين المسألتين تفصيلا . ، إن شاء الله تعالى. محي. أنه
[The Issue of the Creation of the Actions of Servants] 45. So He is the Creator of His servant and what he did, the Grantor of success to whomever He wills to reach. He pointed to the issue translated as the creation of actions, branching from what passed regarding the aspect of His bringing into existence and annihilating it. And if you look at this consideration, what is said is repelled: that there is no benefit in this statement, because the subject and predicate are one thing, since the possible is the possible, and the possible is the possible, so it is as if he said: 'The possible is possible for Him, exalted' or 'The possible is possible for Him, exalted'. And 'ma' in his saying 'what we can' is a relative pronoun, indicating generality, i.e., that bringing into existence every possible thing or annihilating it is permissible for Him, exalted. And this statement refutes two groups: the first: those who say that some possible matters are obligatory for God, like the Mu'tazila who held that it is obligatory for Him, exalted, to do what is beneficial for His servants. And the second group: those who say that some possible matters are impossible for Him, exalted, like the Brahmins who held that the sending of messengers is impossible. And the discussion on each of these two issues will come in detail, God willing. Muhyi. That.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage introduces the doctrine of the creation of human actions, framing it within the discussion of possibility for God. The matn line states: 'So He is the Creator of His servant and what he did, the Grantor of success to whomever He wills to reach.' The commentary explains that this issue branches from the earlier discussion of God's ability to bring into existence or annihilate. It then addresses a potential objection: some might say that the statement 'the possible is possible' is redundant because the subject and predicate are identical. The response is that 'what we can' (مَا أَمْكَنَا) is a relative pronoun indicating generality, meaning that God can either bring into existence or annihilate every possible thing. This statement refutes two groups: (1) those who claim some possibilities are obligatory for God, like the Mu'tazila who argue that God must do what is best for His servants; and (2) those who claim some possibilities are impossible for God, like the Brahmins who deny the possibility of prophethood. The commentary promises a detailed discussion of each group later.

توفيق

جائز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God creates human actions, then humans have no free will or responsibility, or that the statement 'God creates actions' is merely a tautology.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the statement is not redundant; it establishes that all possibilities, including human actions, are under God's power. The issue of human responsibility is treated separately, but here the focus is on God's absolute creative power.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the word 'ما' in 'ما أمكنا' indicate?
A) It indicates a specific object
B) It indicates generality, meaning every possible thing
C) It indicates negation
D) It indicates condition

Key Takeaway
God is the Creator of all actions, and every possible thing is subject to His power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every action you perform—even your intention to pray or your slip into sin—is created by God? If so, how does that affect your sense of personal responsibility? Are you more humble or more fearful? And if you struggle with this, what does that reveal about your reliance on your own strength?
?
The passage argues that the statement 'God creates actions' is not empty but full of meaning, affirming that every possibility is under His control. When you face a decision, do you act as if outcomes are truly in God's hands, or do you privately assume you can secure success by your own planning? What would change if you lived with the conviction that your success or failure is entirely His giving?
?
God grants success only to whom He wills. Does this comfort you or trouble you? When you see people who seem to have success in worldly or religious matters, do you attribute it to their effort or to God's will? How would this teaching change your view of someone who struggles in faith?

Refuting the Mu'tazila and Brahmins
Refutes two groups that impose obligation or impossibility on God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the principle that God can do any possible thing refutes the Mu'tazila claim that God must do what is best and the Brahmin denial of prophethood.

Core Idea
No possible thing is obligatory or impossible for God.

In this lesson, the author applies the previously established principle—that all possibilities are equally permissible for God—to refute two deviant groups. The Mu'tazila argue that God is obliged to do what is best for His servants, while the Brahmins deny the possibility of prophethood. Both views are rejected because they impose limits on divine power.

Guided Path
1
Recall the principle
Remember from the previous lesson that God can create or annihilate any possible thing. This is the foundation for the refutation.
2
Identify the first group: Mu'tazila
The Mu'tazila claim that some possibilities are obligatory for God, such as doing what is best for His servants. The passage refutes this by affirming that no possibility is obligatory.
Their view imposes a necessity on God, which contradicts the principle of divine omnipotence.
3
Identify the second group: Brahmins
The Brahmins claim that some possibilities are impossible for God, such as sending messengers (prophethood). The passage refutes this by affirming that no possibility is impossible.
Their view denies God's ability to do certain things, which also contradicts the principle.
4
Understand the unified refutation
Both groups are refuted by the same principle: all possibilities are equally within God's power. Neither obligation nor impossibility applies to God's actions.
The passage promises a detailed discussion later, but the core refutation is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Correction: The passage corrects this by affirming that no possible act is obligatory or impossible for God; all possibilities are equally subject to His will.

Checkpoint
What do the Brahmins claim according to the passage?
A) That God must do what is best
B) That the sending of messengers is impossible for God
C) That all actions are created by humans
D) That God cannot create evil

Key Takeaway
No possible thing is obligatory or impossible for God; both claims limit His absolute power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever expected God to act in a certain way because you thought it was the best or the most just? How does the teaching that nothing is obligatory upon God challenge your expectations? What would it mean to trust His wisdom over your own sense of 'must'?
?
When you face a difficult situation that seems impossible to resolve, do you doubt that God can change it? How does the passage's affirmation that nothing is impossible for God confront your doubts? Will you now cry out to Him with full certainty, even for what seems impossible?
?
Consider the Brahmins' denial of prophethood: they assumed God would not send messengers. Are there any 'impossibilities' you have unconsciously placed on God—areas where you think He would not act or intervene? How can you dismantle those mental limits and embrace His absolute power?

Allah is the Sole Creator of Actions
The author expounds the Ash'ari doctrine of divine creation of actions and outlines two branches.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Ash'ari school affirms that Allah alone creates the actions of servants, and how this relates to the two branches of the issue.

Core Idea
Allah alone creates every action; the servant's power has no creative effect.

This passage establishes the foundational Ash'ari position on divine creation. The author explains that Allah is the sole creator of both the servant and his actions, rooted in the Qur'anic verse 'Allah created you and what you do.' The lesson introduces the two branches of the issue: who brings the action into existence, and whether the servant has any acquisition (kasb) in it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on divine creation
Begin by reading the source_arabic and translation, focusing on the opening verse and its explanation that Allah is the creator of the servant and his action.
Pay attention to the analysis of the word 'ma' as a verbal noun.
2
Identify the two branches
Notice that the author explicitly states the issue has two branches: (1) whether Allah or the servant brings the action into existence, and (2) whether the servant has kasb. The first branch is covered here.
The second branch will be explained in the next lesson.
3
Study the Sunni position
The passage summarizes the madhhab of Ahl al-Sunna: voluntary actions occur solely by Allah's power, but the servant has power and choice that accompany the action without causal effect.
This is the core Ash'ari doctrine distinct from Qadariyya and Jabriyya.
4
Reflect on the role of power and choice
Understand that Allah's custom is to create power and choice in the servant, and then create the action concomitant with them. The servant does not cause the action.
The servant is a locus (mahall) for the action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَخَالِقُ لِعَبْدِهِ وَمَا عَمِلْ مُوَفِّقٌ لِمَنْ أَرَادَ أَنْ يَصِلْ
وجوب وحدانيته تعالى ، وعموم علمه للمعلومات، وقدرته وإرادته لسائر الممكنات ، فقال : وإذا ثبت وجوب انفرادِه تعالى بالخلق والإيجاد فَخَالِقُ أي : فالله تعالى لا غيره هو الخالق لِعَبْدِه المراد منه : كل مخلوق يصدر عنه الفعل، عاقلا كان أو غير عاقل، ومن النَّاس من قصر العبد على المُكلّف، أن بعض الأدلة التي ذكرها العلماء في هذه المسألة لا تجري في غير فعل المكلف. و«ما» في قول المصنف: «وما عمل مصدرية تسبك ما بعدها بمصدر ، وتقدير العبارة: والله خالق لعبده ولعمل عبده ولا خلاف في أنه خالق لعبده، وإنما ذكره للتمهيد لذكر ما بعده ، وللتأسي بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَاللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ) [الصافات: ٩٦].
وهذه المسألة ذات فرعين:
أحدهما : بيان هل المُوجِدُ للفعل المنسوب إلى العبد هو قدرة الله تعالى أم قدرة العبد؟ وثانيهما: بيان هل للعبد فيه كَسْبٌ أو لا ؟ وقد ذكر المصنف الفرع الأول هنا، وسيأتي قريباً كلامه عن الفرع الثاني عند قوله : وعندنا للعبد كسب». وخلاصة القول في هذه المسألة : أنَّ مذهب أهلِ السُّنَّة أنَّ أفعال العباد الاختيارية واقعة بقدرة الله تعالى وحدها، وليس لقدرة العباد تأثير فيها ، بل الله تعالى أجرى عادته بأن يوجد في العبد قدرة واختيارًا ، فإذا لم يكن هناك مانع أوجد فيه فعله المذكور مقارنا لهذه القدرة وهذا الاختيار الذين أوجدهما الله تعالى فيه، فيكون فعل العبد - على هذا ـ مخلوقا الله تعالى إبداعًا وإحداثًا ، ومَكْسوبًا للعبد، والمراد بكسبه : مقارنة وجود الفعل لقدرته واختياره، من غير أن يكون هناك تأثير منه ، منه، أو مدخل في وجوده سوى كونه محلا، وهذا مذهب الشَّيْخ أبي الحسن الأشعري، وسيأتي إيضاح معنى الكشب في الكلام على الفرع الثاني من فرعي المسألة .
So He is the Creator of His servant and what he did, He is the One who grants success to whom He wills to reach.
The necessity of His Oneness, Exalted, and the comprehensiveness of His knowledge of all known things, and His power and will over all possible things, so he said: And when the necessity of His exclusivity, Exalted, in creation and bringing into existence is established, then 'Creator' means that Allah, Exalted, none other than Him is the Creator of His servant, meaning by it: every created thing from whom the action proceeds, whether rational or non-rational. And among people are those who restrict 'servant' to the morally responsible, because some of the evidences mentioned by the scholars in this issue do not apply to the act of the non-moral agent. And 'ma' in the author's saying 'and what he did' is a masdariyya which makes what follows it into a source, and the estimation of the expression is: 'Allah is the Creator of His servant and of the work of His servant.' And there is no dispute that He is the Creator of His servant, but he mentioned it as a prelude to mention what follows, and in imitation of His saying, Exalted: 'And Allah created you and what you do' [Q. 37:96].
And this issue has two branches:
One of them: the clarification of whether the bringer into existence of the action attributed to the servant is the power of Allah, Exalted, or the power of the servant? And the second: the clarification of whether the servant has acquisition (kasb) in it or not? And the author mentioned the first branch here, and his discussion of the second branch will come soon at his saying: 'And with us, the servant has kasb.' And the summary of the statement in this issue is that the madhhab of Ahl al-Sunna is that the voluntary actions of servants occur solely by the power of Allah, Exalted, and there is no effect for the power of servants in them. Rather, Allah, Exalted, has established His custom that He creates in the servant power and choice, and if there is no obstacle, He creates in him that mentioned action concomitant with this power and this choice which Allah, Exalted, has created in him. Thus, the action of the servant, on this basis, is created by Allah, Exalted, as origination and innovation, and is acquired (maksub) by the servant. And the meaning of his kasb is the concomitance of the existence of the action with his power and choice, without there being any effect from him, or any entry in its existence other than his being a locus. And this is the madhhab of Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, and the clarification of the meaning of kasb will come in the discussion of the second branch of the two branches of the issue.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage is a classification and a doctrinal exposition. It begins with the verse line from the poem: 'So He is the Creator of His servant and what he did...' The author then explains the context: given the established necessity of Allah's oneness and His exclusive power to create, the term 'Creator' here means that Allah alone is the creator of the servant and his actions. The author clarifies that 'servant' refers to any creature from whom an action proceeds, whether rational or not, although some restrict it to morally responsible beings because some proofs only apply to their actions. He then explains that 'ma' in 'and what he did' is a verbal noun particle, so the phrase means 'Allah is the Creator of His servant and of his deed.' There is no dispute about Allah creating the servant; this is mentioned as a prelude to the main point: that Allah also creates the servant's actions, in line with the Qur'anic verse (37:96).
Next, the author outlines the two branches of this issue: (1) whether the agent who brings the action into existence is Allah's power or the servant's power; (2) whether the servant has any 'kasb' (acquisition) in the action. The first branch is addressed here. The author then summarizes the Sunni position: voluntary actions of servants occur solely by Allah's power; the servant's power has no effect. Rather, Allah's custom is to create in the servant power and choice, and when no obstacle prevents, He creates the action concomitant with that power and choice. Thus, the action is wholly created by Allah, but it is also 'acquired' by the servant in the sense that its existence accompanies his power and choice, without any causal influence from him. The servant is merely the locus (mahall) of the action. This is the Ash'ari doctrine, and the meaning of kasb will be further clarified in the discussion of the second branch.

Key Terms
خلق الأفعال
القدرة
الاختيار
أهل السنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that the servant's kasb means he independently creates his action through his own power.
Correction: The passage clarifies that kasb is merely the accompaniment of the action with power and choice; the servant has no creative effect.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari position in the passage, what is the role of the servant's power in the creation of his action?

B) The servant's power has no effect; Allah alone creates the action while the servant's power accompanies it
C) The servant's power creates the action but Allah controls the outcome
D) The servant's power and Allah's power jointly create the action

Key Takeaway
Allah alone creates every action of His servants; the servant's power and choice are created by Allah and merely accompany the action without causal effect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Do you truly believe that every action you perform—every prayer, every sin, every breath—is created solely by Allah? If so, why do you still feel pride in your good deeds or despair over your failures? Before your next action, pause and say: 'Allah created me and what I do.' How does that change your intention?
?
If your power and choice have no creative effect, then what is left of your responsibility? The lesson says you acquire the action by being its locus. Does that thought make you more humble or more fearful? Commit to memorising the Arabic phrase 'من غير أن يكون هناك تأثير منه' and repeating it whenever you feel self-sufficient.

Proof That the Servant Does Not Create His Actions
Sanusi presents two arguments proving the servant is not the creator of his actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proofs that the servant is not the independent creator of his own actions, including the experiential argument and the argument from preponderance and infinite regress.

Core Idea
Our actions are not independently created by us; only Allah is the Creator.

Sanusi here tackles a central question in Islamic theology: do humans create their own actions? Through careful reasoning, he shows that many actions occur without our full knowledge or intent, and that independent creation would lead to logical absurdities. This passage grounds the Ash'ari position that all actions are ultimately from Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two main arguments
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note that Sanusi first gives two experiential premises, then a more formal third argument. Try to distinguish them.
The experiential argument is in the first two sentences; the third argument starts with 'Third'.
2
Understand the experiential premises
Focus on the examples: turning in sleep and moving a finger. Sanusi argues we often do not perceive the full quantity or quality of our actions, proving we cannot be their independent creators.
This shows that conscious intent and full knowledge are absent in many actions.
3
Analyze the third argument
Trace the logical chain: if the servant were independent, he would need equal ability to do or leave an action, requiring a preponderant. If the preponderant comes from the servant, infinite regress follows; if from Allah, the point is proven.
This argument relies on the impossibility of preponderance without a preponderant.
4
Connect to the conclusion
Sanusi concludes that the servant is not the originator of his actions independently. Reflect on how both arguments converge on this point.
The conclusion is that all actions are created by Allah, affirming divine omnipotence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسأله خلق أفعال العِباد باختياره فعلا كانقلابه من جنب إلى جنب آخر ونحوه وهو لا يشعر بكمية ذلك الفعل ولا كيفيته، وأيضا المُحرَّكُ مِنَّا لأصبعه محرك لكل أجزائها لا محالة، ولا شعور له بها، فكيف يتوهم أنه يعرف حركتها ويقصدها ؟ ومتى ثبتت كل هذه المقدمات ثبت ضرورة أنَّ العبد غير موجدٍ لأفعاله بالاختيار والاستقلال. الثالث: لو كان العبد موجداً لفعله باختياره وقدرته استقلالاً لوجب أن يكون متمكنا من فعل كل عمل يُقْدِمُ عليه وتركه ، وإلا لم يكن قادرًا عليه مُستقلا بإيجاده، ولوجب أيضا أن يكون فعله ثمَّة مُرجّح يُرجّح على تركه ؛ إذ لو لم يتوقف على المرجّح والفرض أن صدور الفعل عن العبد جائز لا واجب للزم ترجيح أحد الأمرين المتساويين بغير مرجح، وهو محال ، وإذا لزم وجود المرجّح ، فهذا المرجّح إمَّا أن يكون من العبد باختياره فيلزم التسلسل لأنَّا ننتقل إلى صدور هذا المرجّح منه ، وهكذا ، وإن كان المرجح من الله فهو المطلوب.
The issue of the creation of the actions of servants: by his choice an action like his turning from one side to another and the like, and he does not perceive the quantity of that action nor its quality. Also, the mover among us of his finger is a mover of all its parts inevitably, and he has no perception of them, so how can he imagine that he knows its movement and intends it? And when all these premises are established, it is necessarily established that the servant is not an originator of his actions by choice and independently. Third: If the servant were an originator of his action by his choice and power independently, it would be necessary that he be able to do every action he undertakes and leave it, otherwise he would not be capable of it independently in originating it. And it would also be necessary that his action have a preponderant that preponderates it over its abandonment; because if it did not depend on the preponderant, and the assumption is that the occurrence of the action from the servant is possible not necessary, then the preponderance of one of the two equal alternatives without a preponderant would be necessary, which is impossible. And if the existence of the preponderant is necessary, then this preponderant is either from the servant by his choice, leading to infinite regress because we would move to the occurrence of this preponderant from him, and so on; or if the preponderant is from Allah, then that is the desired conclusion.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage presents a logical proof that the servant is not the independent creator of his own actions. It first offers two experiential premises: the servant often performs actions like shifting in sleep without perceiving their full quantity or quality; similarly, moving a finger involves moving all its parts without conscious awareness. These show that many actions occur without the servant's full knowledge and intent, making it impossible that he independently creates them. The conclusion states that if these premises are established, it necessarily follows that the servant is not the originator of his actions independently. Then a third, more formal argument is given: if the servant were independent, he would have equal ability to do or leave an action, requiring a preponderant to tip the scales. Since a choice without a preponderant would be a preponderance of equals (impossible), a preponderant is needed. If this preponderant comes from the servant, it leads to infinite regress; if from Allah, the point is proven. Thus, the servant's actions are created by Allah.

Key Terms
خالق
مُوجِد
اختيار
استقلال
مُرجِّح
تسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof denies human choice entirely; humans have no role in their actions.
Correction: The proof shows only that humans are not independent creators. Choice and acquisition (kasb) are affirmed; ultimate creation belongs to Allah.

Checkpoint
In the third argument, if the preponderant for an action comes from the servant's own choice, what problem arises?
A) The servant would be forced to act
B) An infinite regress of preponderants
C) The action would be impossible
D) The servant would have no free will

Key Takeaway
The passage demonstrates through logical reasoning that the servant cannot be the independent creator of his actions, affirming Allah's sole creative power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform even the simplest action like moving a finger, do you habitually feel that you are the sole originator of that movement? How does Sanusi’s observation that you are unaware of its full details challenge that feeling? Will you pause before your next action to acknowledge Allah’s hidden role?
?
Sanusi proves that if you were the independent creator of your actions, you would need to have equal power to do or leave each action. Think of a sin you committed or a good deed you performed—was it truly equally possible for you to do the opposite at that moment? What does that reveal about your actual independence?
?
The proof concludes that the preponderant for every action ultimately comes from Allah. Consider a moment when you felt proud of an accomplishment. Did you remember that the decisive factor came from Allah? Will you consciously attribute your next success to Allah alone, and thank Him for it?

Six Schools on the Creation of Human Actions
The commentator enumerates six opinions on the creation of human actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the six major Islamic theological schools on the creation of human voluntary actions, including the Ash'ari doctrine of kasb.

Core Idea
The debate over who creates human actions has six key positions, with kasb as the Sunni middle path.

This passage from the commentary presents a comprehensive map of the various theological positions on the creation of human acts. While involuntary actions are uncontroversially attributed to Allah, the real debate concerns voluntary actions. The author enumerates six distinct opinions, from extreme determinism to complete human autonomy, and then explains and defends the Ash'ari doctrine of kasb.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the six opinions
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once. Identify the six numbered opinions and note their key differences.
The opinions range from full determinism to full human creation.
2
Focus on the Ash'ari position
Pay special attention to the third opinion (Ash'ari). Notice how it distinguishes between Allah's creation and the servant's acquisition (kasb), using the analogy of whiteness and the body.
Understanding kasb is crucial for Sunni theology.
3
Analyze the last two opinions
Consider the opinions of al-Isfarayini and al-Baqillani. Why does the commentator say they are not authentically held? How does this affect the overall taxonomy?
These opinions are presented as debate positions, not actual beliefs.
4
Reflect on the significance
Think about why this classification matters. How does it clarify the Sunni stance on divine predestination and human responsibility?
This passage directly addresses a major theological controversy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة خلق أفعال العباد
أفعاله الاختيارية (۱) ، وأما الاضطراريَّة ؛ فهي مخلوقة له تعالى باتفاق أهل
(۱) قوله: (لسائر أفعاله الاختيارية) أي: لجميعها ، وفيه ردّ على المعتزلة القائلين بأن الخالق لها هو العبد. والحاصل أن الأفعال الاختيارية تعلق بها قدرتان قدرة المولى على طريق الإيجاد، وقدرة العبد على طريق الكسب، هذا مذهب أهل السنة ، ومذهب المعتزلة أنه لم يتعلق بها إلا قدرة العبد فقط على طريق الإيجاد، وكلهم مطبقون على ذلك ، ثم بعد ذلك اختلفوا: هل هذا الحكم ضروري أو نظري ؟ فذهب إلى الأول: أبو الحسن البصري من متأخريهم وإلى الثاني متقدموهم. واعلم أن العقلاء اختلفوا في هذه المسألة على ستة أقوال: الأول: الجبرية ، وهو أن المؤثر في أفعال العباد هو الله تعالى بقدرته ، وليس للعبد كسب. الثاني: قول المعتزلة ، وهو أن المؤثر في الأفعال الاختيارية هو العبد بقدرته ، فقد أثر فيها باختياره ، وليس لله تأثير في تلك الأفعال . والثالث: قول الأشعري ، وهو أن المؤثر هو الله بقدرته ، والعبد ليس مؤثرا بقدرته ، بل هي مقارنة للفعل على طريق الكسب، ومع ذلك فأهل السنة قائلون بإسناد الأفعال لا الله ، إذ القائم والقاعد والأكل والشارب هو العبد ، وإن كان الفعل مخلوقا لله ، فإن الفعل إنما يسند حقيقة لمن قام به، لا إلى من خلقه وأوجده ، ألا تری أن الأبيض مثلا هو الجسم، وإن كان البياض القائم به من خَلقه تعالى وإيجاده ، قال السعد: ولا عجب في خفاء هذا المعنى على عوام القدرية وجهلتهم، حتى شنعوا على أهل الحق في الأسواق ، وإنما العجب خفاؤه على خواصهم وعلمائهم؛ حتى سوّدوا به الصحائف والأوراق ، وبهذا ظهر أن تمسكهم بما ورد في الكتاب والسنة من استناد الأفعال إلى العباد لا يُثبت لهم المدعى، وهو كون فعل العبد واقعا بقدرته ومخلوقا له. والقول الرابع: قول الفلاسفة، وهو أن الله خلق للعبد قدرة تؤثر بطريق الإيجاب. والقول الخامس : قول الاستاذ الإسفراييني، وهو أن الفعل الاختياري أثر فيه الله والعبد بقدرتيهما ، فتشاركا في التأثير في ذلك الفعل . والقول السادس: قول القاضي الباقلاني، وهو بهما أيضا، لكن الله أثر بقدرته من حيث خلق الفعل، والعبد بقدرته من حيث الوصف بكون الفعل طاعة أو معصية. وهذان القولان لم يصحا عن القاضي والأستاذ ، وبتقدير صحتهما عنهما فهما إنما قالاهما في مقام المناظرة مع الخصم ، وليسا معتقدين بهما . الشنواني .
Issue of the creation of the actions of servants.
His voluntary actions (1), and as for involuntary actions, they are created by Him the Exalted by agreement of the people.
(1) His statement: 'for all his voluntary actions' i.e., all of them, and in it is a refutation of the Mu'tazila who say that the creator of them is the servant. And the conclusion is that voluntary actions have two powers attached to them: the power of the Master in the way of bringing into existence, and the power of the servant in the way of acquisition. This is the school of Ahl al-Sunna. The school of the Mu'tazila is that only the power of the servant attaches to them in the way of bringing into existence. And they all agree on that. Then after that they differed: is this ruling necessary (daruri) or theoretical (nazari)? The former was held by Abu al-Hasan al-Basri among their later scholars, and the latter by their earlier scholars. And know that the rational people differed on this issue according to six opinions:
First: the Jabriyya: that the influencer in the actions of servants is Allah the Exalted by His power, and the servant has no acquisition.
Second: the saying of the Mu'tazila: that the influencer in voluntary actions is the servant by his power, so he influences them by his choice, and Allah has no impact on those actions.
Third: the saying of the Ash'ari: that the influencer is Allah by His power, and the servant is not an influencer by his power, rather it is concomitant to the action in the way of acquisition. Nevertheless, Ahl al-Sunna attribute actions not to Allah; indeed, the one who stands, sits, eats, and drinks is the servant, even if the action is created by Allah. For the action is truly attributed to the one in whom it subsists, not to the one who created it and brought it into existence. Do you not see that the white object, for example, is the body, even though the whiteness subsisting in it is from His creation and bringing into existence? Al-Sa'd said: There is no wonder in the obscurity of this meaning to the common people of the Qadariyya and their ignorant ones, until they disparaged the people of truth in the markets. Rather, the wonder is its obscurity to their elite and scholars, until they blackened the pages and papers with it. By this it becomes clear that their clinging to what is reported in the Book and the Sunnah of attributing actions to servants does not prove their claim, which is that the servant's action occurs by his power and is created by him.
Fourth: the saying of the philosophers: that Allah created for the servant a power that influences by way of necessitation (ijab).
Fifth: the saying of al-Ustadh al-Isfarayini: that the voluntary action is influenced by Allah and the servant by their two powers, so they share in influencing that action.
Sixth: the saying of al-Qadi al-Baqillani: that it is also by both, but Allah influences by His power in terms of creating the action, and the servant influences by his power in terms of the description of the action being obedience or disobedience. These two sayings are not authentically reported from al-Qadi and al-Ustadh, and assuming their authenticity from them, they only said them in the context of debate with the opponent, and they do not hold them as beliefs. Al-Shanwani.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage is a classification and explanation of the different schools regarding the creation of human actions. It begins by stating the issue (mas'ala) of the creation of servants' actions, noting that involuntary actions are created by Allah by consensus. The commentator then explains that for voluntary actions, two powers are involved in the Ash'ari view: Allah's power in creation and the servant's power in acquisition (kasb)—this is the Sunni position. The Mu'tazila hold that only the servant's power creates. The passage then notes an intra-Mu'tazili dispute on whether this is necessary or theoretical knowledge. Then eight opinions are enumerated: (1) Jabriyya: only Allah acts, no kasb for the servant; (2) Mu'tazila: only the servant creates his own actions; (3) Ash'ariyya: Allah creates the action, the servant acquires it, and actions are attributed to the servant because they inhere in him, as whiteness inheres in a body; (4) Philosophers: Allah creates a power that necessitates action; (5) al-Isfarayini: both Allah and the servant share in influencing the action; (6) al-Baqillani: similar sharing but distinguishing creation from moral description. The commentator notes that the last two are not authentically held by their proponents and were only said in debate. Throughout, the commentator defends the Ash'ari position as the balanced view.

Key Terms
جبرية
معتزلة
أشعري
كسب
قدرة
فلاسفة
إسفراييني
باقلاني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Ash'ari doctrine of kasb denies human responsibility and makes God the doer of evil.
Correction: The passage clarifies that actions are attributed to the servant because they inhere in him, so the servant is truly the agent and responsible. God creates the action's existence, but the servant's acquisition makes him accountable.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which school holds that the servant is the sole creator of his voluntary actions?
A) Jabriyya
B) Mu'tazila
C) Ash'ariyya
D) Philosophers

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari doctrine of kasb resolves the tension between divine omnipotence and human responsibility by distinguishing Allah's creation of actions from the servant's acquisition of them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that every voluntary action of yours—every word, every movement—is created by Allah and only acquired by you, does this humble you into greater reliance on Him? Or does it tempt you to a fatalistic laziness? Which tendency do you find in your heart, and what will you do to correct it?
?
The Mu'tazila claimed that Allah does not influence your actions at all, leaving you completely independent. Do you ever live as if your choices are entirely your own, forgetting that Allah is the Creator of your very ability to choose? Take one decision you made today—can you sincerely attribute its existence to Allah's creation while still owning your responsibility?
?
The passage warns that extreme views lead to error: either denying human responsibility (Jabriyya) or denying divine power (Mu'tazila). Where do you see yourself leaning in your daily life? Do you more often excuse your sins by saying 'Allah created it' or do you act as if your success is solely by your own effort? How will you realign your heart to the balanced path of kasb?

The Meaning of Tawfiq (Divine Success)
Defines tawfiq as God's creation of power and inclination to obey.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise theological definition of tawfiq as God's creation of both the ability and the inner inclination to obey.

Core Idea
Tawfiq is not just ability; it is God-given ability plus the desire to obey.

This lesson explores the theological definition of tawfiq (divine success). The medieval scholar Imam al-Haramayn distinguished tawfiq from mere provision of means, explaining that it involves God creating both the capacity and the inner drive to perform obedience. Understanding this helps clarify God's role in human actions and the difference between a believer and a disbeliever.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the literal meaning.
Notice the concise style with embedded commentary.
2
Identify the two components of tawfiq
Find where tawfiq is defined as 'creating the power of obedience' and 'the inclination towards it'. Understand these two parts.
The power is the soundness of means and instruments; the inclination is the psychic resolve.
3
Understand why 'inclination' excludes the disbeliever
The disbeliever may have the power (means) but lacks the inclination to obey, so tawfiq is absent.
This shows tawfiq is more than external conditions.
4
Consider the two powers in the created being
The commentary distinguishes between power of obedience and power of inclination, both created by God.
5
Reflect on the theological implications
Ask: How does this definition preserve both divine omnipotence and human responsibility?

بيان أنَّ التَّوفيق والخذلانَ بمَشيئته تعالى وقُدرتِه. و(مُوَفِّقٌ مِن التَّوفيق، وهو لغة التأليف، وشرعًا: خَلْقُ قدرة الطَّاعة : والداعية إليها في العبد (۲) ، كما قاله إمام الحرمين، وأراد بالقدرة: سلامة الأسباب والآلات (۳) ؛ فزادَ قيد الداعية لإخراج الكافر (٤) . (۲) قوله: (خلقُ قدرة الطاعة) أي: القدرة على الطاعة . وقوله : ( والداعية إليها) أي: إلى الطاعة، أي: الميل النفساني والتصميم المصاحب للفعل، وهو عطف على الطاعة، فللمخلوق :قدرتان قدرة الطاعة، وقدرة الداعية الشنواني . (۳) قوله: (سلامة الأسباب من إضافة الصفة للموصوف ، لأن السلامة أمر اعتباري لا تتعلق به القدرة ، وقوله : والآلات) عطفه على الأسباب تفسير ، وقيل : عطف خاص على عام ؛ بناء على أن الأسباب عبارة عما يتهيأ به الفعل ويتحصل ، أعم من كونه حاملا عليه أو مستعانا به ، والآلات خاصة بما يستعان به وقيل عطف مغاير بناء على أن الأسباب هي الأشياء التي تكون حاملة على الفعل ؛ فالمكان الذي يصلي فيه ، والماء الذي يتوضأ به ، وعدم المانع من ذلك أسباب للفعل عرفيةٌ ، والأعضاء التي يحاول بها الفعل آلات له. الشنواني. (٤) قوله: (الإخراج الكافر أي لأنه ليس المراد بالقدرة العرض المقارن للفعل، نفى أنه هل المراد بالطاعة طاعةٌ مخصوصة كالإيمان ، وهو الذي يدل عليه إخراج الكافر فقط ، أو مطلقها ؛ فيراد المؤمن العاصي في الإخراج. الشنواني.
Clarifying that granting success (tawfiq) and abandonment (khidhlan) are by His will, Most High, and His power. And (He is) 'Grantor of success' from tawfiq, which is linguistically 'uniting', and in sacred law: creating the power of obedience and the inclination towards it in the servant (2), as stated by Imam al-Haramayn, and he meant by 'power': the soundness of means and instruments (3); so he added the restriction 'inclination' to exclude the disbeliever (4). (2) His saying: (creating the power of obedience) i.e. the power for obedience. And his saying: (and the inclination towards it) i.e. towards obedience, that is, the psychic inclination and resolve accompanying the act, and it is an appositive to obedience. So the created being has two powers: the power of obedience and the power of inclination. Al-Shanwani. (3) His saying: (soundness of means) is an attribute added to the described, because soundness is a relative matter to which power does not attach. And his saying: (and instruments) is an appositive to 'means' as explanation. It is said it is a specific joined to a general: based on that 'means' is that by which the act is prepared and obtained, general whether it carries one or assists, and 'instruments' specifically that with which one is assisted. And it is said it is a different appositive based on that 'means' are things that carry one to the act; so the place one prays in, the water one performs wudu with, and the absence of obstacles are conventional means for the act, and the limbs with which one attempts the act are its instruments. Al-Shanwani. (4) His saying: (to exclude the disbeliever) i.e. because what is meant by 'power' is not the accident concomitant with the act, and he asked: is what is meant by 'obedience' a specific obedience like faith, which is indicated by excluding only the disbeliever, or absolute obedience, so the disobedient believer would be included in the exclusion? Al-Shanwani.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of 'tawfiq' (granting success) and 'khidhlan' (abandonment) as being dependent on God's will and power. It begins by stating the title: 'Clarifying that tawfiq and khidhlan are by His will and power.' Then it defines 'tawfiq' linguistically as 'uniting' and legally as 'creating the power of obedience and the inclination towards it in the servant,' citing Imam al-Haramayn. The commentary explains that 'power' here means the soundness of means and instruments, i.e., the conditions that make the act possible. The added restriction 'inclination' (dā'iyah) is to exclude the disbeliever, because the disbeliever may have the means but not the inclination to obey. The commentary further breaks down the definition: the created being has two powers – the power for obedience and the power of inclination. It also discusses whether 'obedience' refers specifically to faith or to any act of obedience, which affects whether the disobedient believer is included in the exclusion.

Correction: Tawfiq is both the ability (power) and the inner inclination (dā'iyah) to obey.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
If tawfiq is a gift that includes both the means and the inner drive, what stops you from asking Allah in every prayer for both? Write down one specific act of obedience you struggle with, and commit to asking Allah for the desire to do it as much as for the ability.

The Definition of Tawfiq and the Condition of Da'iyah
Defines tawfiq linguistically and legally with the da'iyah condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise definition of tawfiq in Ash'ari theology, including why the inner inclination (da'iyah) is a necessary condition.

Core Idea
Tawfiq is not just ability; it includes the inner inclination that distinguishes believers from disbelievers.

This passage from Ithaaf al-Mureed clarifies what tawfiq really means. While many think of divine facilitation as merely giving ability, Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni explains that it also requires an inner pull towards obedience. This nuance protects a key theological distinction in the Ash'ari understanding of divine action and human responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation to get the overall sense. Note that the author begins with a general statement before defining terms.
2
Focus on the two definitions
Identify the linguistic definition (ta'lif) and the legal definition (creation of power and da'iyah). Understand why both components are needed.
3
Understand the clarification about 'power'
The author clarifies that 'power' here means soundness of causes and instruments, not just sheer ability. This is a key nuance.
4
Ask why da'iyah was added
The passage explicitly says the da'iyah condition excludes the disbeliever. Think about why a disbeliever might have ability but not true tawfiq.
5
Connect to the bigger picture
Reflect on how this definition upholds God's control over all actions (including the inclination) while still accounting for accountability.

بيانُ أنَّ التَّوفيق والخذلانَ بمَشيئته تعالى وقُدرتِه. وموفق من التوفيق، وهو لغة التأليف، وشرعًا: خَلْقُ قدرة الطَّاعة والداعية إليها في العبد، كما قاله إمام الحرمين، وأراد بالقدرة: سلامة الأسباب والآلات؛ فزادَ قيد الداعية لإخراج الكافر.
Statement that tawfiq and khidhlan are by His will and power. And (He is) muwaffiq (one who grants success) deriving from tawfiq, which linguistically means harmonizing, and legally: the creation of the power of obedience and the inclination (da'iyah) towards it in the servant, as stated by Imam al-Haramayn. He meant by power: the soundness of causes and instruments; thus he added the condition of da'iyah to exclude the disbeliever.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'tawfiq' (divine facilitation) as used by Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni. The author begins by stating the topic: that tawfiq and khidhlan (abandonment) are by God's will and power. Then he defines tawfiq: linguistically it means 'ta'lif' (harmonizing). In legal terminology, it is the creation of two things in the servant: (1) the power (qudra) to obey, and (2) the inclination (da'iyah) towards that obedience. He clarifies that by 'power' Imam al-Haramayn meant 'the soundness of causes and instruments' (salamat al-asbab wa al-alat). The author then explains why the condition of da'iyah was added: to exclude the disbeliever (kafir) from being considered 'muwaffaq'. The disbeliever may have the power and sound means, but lacks the inner inclination towards obedience, so he is not truly 'facilitated' to good. This highlights the Ash'ari emphasis on God's creation of both the capacity and the motivational inclination.

Misconception: Some think tawfiq is simply giving ability (sound means) to do good.
Correction: Tawfiq also requires the creation of an inner inclination (da'iyah) towards obedience; without it, even a capable person is not truly facilitated to good.

Key Takeaway
Tawfiq is the creation of both the power and the inner inclination to obey, and the da'iyah condition ensures that only believers are truly facilitated by God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
You claim to believe that everything is from Allah, yet you often take credit for your good deeds. How can you shift your mindset to see both your ability and your motivation as direct creations from Him? Write down one specific change in your daily gratitude practice.

Definition of Tawfiq and Khidhlan
The author defines two divine acts: tawfiq and khidhlan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic theological definitions of tawfiq (divine enabling) and khidhlan (divine abandonment) and how they relate to Allah's creation of human power.

Core Idea
Tawfiq and khidhlan mean Allah creates the power to obey or disobey in a person.

This lesson unpacks two key kalam terms that appear in the source. The author defines them as acts of divine creation, not merely abstract concepts. Understanding these definitions is essential for grasping the subsequent discussion on the two types of human power.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own definitions come through.
Notice the poetic line embedded in the prose.
2
Identify the definitions
Find the definitions of tawfiq and khidhlan. The author defines them as Allah creating the power for obedience or disobedience.
3
Reflect on the divine nature
Consider why these definitions are placed in the section on divine matters (Ilahiyyat). They are acts of Allah, not merely human states.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم الإلهيات .8 اعتقاده أنَّ الله تعالى هو الخالق لقدرةِ الطَّاعة فيمن أرادَ توفيقه ، وهو المراد بقوله : (لِمَنْ أَرَادَ أَنْ يَصِل) لرضاه ومحبّته . ٤٦ . وَخَاذِلٌ لِمَنْ أَرَادَ بُعْدَهُ وَمُنْجِرٌ لِمَنْ أَرَادَ وَعْدَهُ (وَخَاذِلٌ) أي : خالق لقدرة المعصية فيمن أرادَ خِذْلَانَه ، أي: ترك نُصرته وإعانته ، وهو المراد بقوله : (لِمَنْ أَرَادَ بُعْدَهُ عن رضاه ومحبته). ثم ذكر أن التوفيق والخذلان يتعلقان بقدرين من القدرة: الأول: قدرة واستطاعة لا يجب معها وجود الفعل، وهي التي تسبق الفعل وتكون قبل الإتيان به. والثاني: قدرة واستطاعة يجب معها وجود الفعل، وهي بغير شك مقارنة للفعل لا سابقة عليه . وقد أشارت نصوص الشريعة من الكتاب والسنة الصحيحة إلى هذين الضربين. فالإشارة إلى الأول منهما في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ مَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ إِلَيْهِ سَبِيلًا﴾ [آل عمران ٩٧] وقوله سبحانه: ﴿فَاتَقُوا اللهَ مَا اسْتَطَعْتُمْ﴾ [التغابن: ١٦] وفي قوله لعمران بن حصين: صل قائما، فإن لم تستطع فعلى جنب. ومعلوم أن الحج والصلاة واجبان على المستطيع بمعنى المتمكن من الفعل المُتهيّئ له، سواءٌ أَفَعَلَ أم لم يفعل. والإشارة إلى الضرب الثاني في قوله تعالى: ﴿مَا كَانُوا يَسْتَطِيعُونَ السَّمْعَ وَمَا كَانُوا يُبْصِرُونَ﴾ [هود: ٢٠] وقوله: ﴿وَعَرَضْنَا جَهَنَّمَ يَوْمَئِذٍ لِلْكَفِرِينَ عَرَضًا الَّذِينَ كَانَتْ أَعْيُنُهُمْ فِي غِطَاء عَن ذِكْرِى وَكَانُوا لَا يَسْتَطِيعُونَ سَمْعًا﴾ [الكهف: ١٠١] فالمراد بعدم استطاعتهم مشقة ذلك عليهم، وصعوبته على نفوسهم، فنفوسهم لا تُقْبِلُ عليه ولا تُرِيدُه، وإن كانوا قادرين على فعله متمكنين منه لو أرادوه . وهذا إيضاح وبيان لما أجاب به القوم: من أن العبد قادر حين التكليف بالقوة القريبة؛ لِمَا اتصف به من سلامة الآلات، وتوافر الأسباب.
Section on Divine Matters. 8. His belief that Allah Almighty is the Creator of the power of obedience in whomever He wills to grant success (tawfiq), and that is what is meant by His saying: 'for whomever He wills to reach' to His pleasure and love. 46. And a Withholder (khadhil) for whomever He wills distance from Him, and a Fulfiller for whomever He wills His promise. (And a Withholder) meaning: Creator of the power of disobedience in whomever He wills to abandon (khidhlan), i.e., to withhold His help and assistance, and that is what is meant by His saying: 'for whomever He wills distance from His pleasure and love.' Then he mentioned that tawfiq and khidhlan relate to two kinds of power: the first: a power and capacity (istita'a) with which the existence of the act is not obligatory, and it precedes the act and is before performing it. The second: a power and capacity with which the existence of the act is obligatory, and it is without doubt concurrent with the act, not preceding it. The texts of the Shari'a from the Book and authentic Sunna have indicated these two types. The indication of the first of them is in His saying: 'And due to Allah from the people is a pilgrimage to the House, for whoever is able (istata'a) to find a way to it' [Al 'Imran 97] and His saying: 'So fear Allah as much as you are able (istata'tum)' [Taghabun 16] and in His saying to 'Imran ibn Husayn: 'Pray standing; if you are unable, then on your side.' It is known that Hajj and prayer are obligatory upon the able (mustati') in the sense of one who is capable of the act and prepared for it, whether he does it or not. The indication of the second type is in His saying: 'They were not able (yastati'una) to hear and they were not seeing' [Hud 20] and His saying: 'And We will present Hell on that Day to the disbelievers as a presentation, those whose eyes were in a cover from My remembrance and they were not able (yastati'una) to hear' [Kahf 101]. The meaning of their inability (adam istita'atihim) is the difficulty of that for them and its hardship upon their souls, so their souls do not incline to it nor desire it, even though they were capable of doing it and able if they wanted it. And this is a clarification and explanation of what the group answered: that the servant is capable at the time of obligation by the proximate power (al-quwwa al-qariba), due to his being characterized by soundness of instruments and availability of means.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage defines two key terms: tawfiq (divine enabling) and khidhlan (divine abandonment). It begins by stating that belief in Allah as the Creator of the power for obedience in whomever He wills to grant success is part of the section on divine matters. The line of poetry then states that Allah is a Withholder for whomever He wills distance from Him, i.e., He creates in him the power of disobedience. The commentary explains that tawfiq and khidhlan are related to two kinds of power. The first kind is a power that does not necessitate the act; it precedes the act and is the basis for moral obligation (taklif). The second kind is a power that accompanies the act and necessarily brings it about. The author provides scriptural evidence for both: for the first, the verses on Hajj and piety show that ability means capability and preparedness, regardless of actual performance. For the second, the verses about the disbelievers' inability to hear or see show that they find it difficult and do not incline to it, though they have the physical capacity. The passage concludes by clarifying that this is the basis for the scholars' answer that the human is capable at the time of obligation by the 'proximate power' (al-quwwa al-qariba), which is due to soundness of instruments and availability of means.

Key Terms
توفيق
خذلان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think tawfiq and khidhlan are about Allah's predestination of actions without reference to created power.
Correction: The passage clarifies that both are specifically about Allah creating the power (qudra) for the act of obedience or disobedience.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does 'tawfiq' mean?
A) Allah's guidance to the truth
B) Allah's creation of the power of obedience
C) Allah's reward for obedience
D) Allah's love for the obedient

Key Takeaway
Tawfiq and khidhlan are defined as Allah's creation of the specific power for obedience and disobedience respectively.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you honestly depend on Allah to create the very power to obey in you, or do you unconsciously rely on your own strength? What would change if you started each act of worship with a plea for tawfiq?
?
When you fall into sin, do you recognize that Allah has withheld khidhlan from you as a test or justice, or do you blame Him? How can you respond to your disobedience with humility rather than resentment?
?
If Allah created the power for obedience in you today, what one obedience would you commit to? And if He created the power for disobedience, what sin are you most at risk of? Pray for tawfiq right now.

Divine Attributes
intermediate
6 min
Two Types of Human Power (Qudra)
The author explains the two types of power (qudra/istita'a) and provides scriptural evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between the two types of power (qudra/istita'a) mentioned in kalam: one that precedes the act and does not necessitate it, and one that accompanies the act and necessitates it.

Core Idea
There are two powers: one for potentiality (before the act) and one for actuality (with the act).

After defining tawfiq and khidhlan, the author introduces two categories of human power that are central to understanding moral obligation (taklif). This lesson explains the distinction with scriptural evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage describing the two powers
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the clear contrast between the two types.
2
Distinguish the two powers
The first power precedes the act and does not make the act necessary. The second power is concurrent with the act and makes it necessary.
Think of potential vs. actual ability.
3
Examine the scriptural evidence
For the first type, verses about Hajj and piety show ability means capability. For the second, verses about disbelievers show inability as psychological difficulty.
4
Understand the conclusion
The passage ends by stating that the servant is capable at obligation by the 'proximate power' (al-quwwa al-qariba), which is soundness of instruments and means.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم الإلهيات .8 اعتقاده أنَّ الله تعالى هو الخالق لقدرةِ الطَّاعة فيمن أرادَ توفيقه ، وهو المراد بقوله : (لِمَنْ أَرَادَ أَنْ يَصِل) لرضاه ومحبّته . ٤٦ . وَخَاذِلٌ لِمَنْ أَرَادَ بُعْدَهُ وَمُنْجِرٌ لِمَنْ أَرَادَ وَعْدَهُ (وَخَاذِلٌ) أي : خالق لقدرة المعصية فيمن أرادَ خِذْلَانَه ، أي: ترك نُصرته وإعانته ، وهو المراد بقوله : (لِمَنْ أَرَادَ بُعْدَهُ عن رضاه ومحبته). ثم ذكر أن التوفيق والخذلان يتعلقان بقدرين من القدرة: الأول: قدرة واستطاعة لا يجب معها وجود الفعل، وهي التي تسبق الفعل وتكون قبل الإتيان به. والثاني: قدرة واستطاعة يجب معها وجود الفعل، وهي بغير شك مقارنة للفعل لا سابقة عليه . وقد أشارت نصوص الشريعة من الكتاب والسنة الصحيحة إلى هذين الضربين. فالإشارة إلى الأول منهما في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ مَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ إِلَيْهِ سَبِيلًا﴾ [آل عمران ٩٧] وقوله سبحانه: ﴿فَاتَقُوا اللهَ مَا اسْتَطَعْتُمْ﴾ [التغابن: ١٦] وفي قوله لعمران بن حصين: صل قائما، فإن لم تستطع فعلى جنب. ومعلوم أن الحج والصلاة واجبان على المستطيع بمعنى المتمكن من الفعل المُتهيّئ له، سواءٌ أَفَعَلَ أم لم يفعل. والإشارة إلى الضرب الثاني في قوله تعالى: ﴿مَا كَانُوا يَسْتَطِيعُونَ السَّمْعَ وَمَا كَانُوا يُبْصِرُونَ﴾ [هود: ٢٠] وقوله: ﴿وَعَرَضْنَا جَهَنَّمَ يَوْمَئِذٍ لِلْكَفِرِينَ عَرَضًا الَّذِينَ كَانَتْ أَعْيُنُهُمْ فِي غِطَاء عَن ذِكْرِى وَكَانُوا لَا يَسْتَطِيعُونَ سَمْعًا﴾ [الكهف: ١٠١] فالمراد بعدم استطاعتهم مشقة ذلك عليهم، وصعوبته على نفوسهم، فنفوسهم لا تُقْبِلُ عليه ولا تُرِيدُه، وإن كانوا قادرين على فعله متمكنين منه لو أرادوه . وهذا إيضاح وبيان لما أجاب به القوم: من أن العبد قادر حين التكليف بالقوة القريبة؛ لِمَا اتصف به من سلامة الآلات، وتوافر الأسباب.
Section on Divine Matters. 8. His belief that Allah Almighty is the Creator of the power of obedience in whomever He wills to grant success (tawfiq), and that is what is meant by His saying: 'for whomever He wills to reach' to His pleasure and love. 46. And a Withholder (khadhil) for whomever He wills distance from Him, and a Fulfiller for whomever He wills His promise. (And a Withholder) meaning: Creator of the power of disobedience in whomever He wills to abandon (khidhlan), i.e., to withhold His help and assistance, and that is what is meant by His saying: 'for whomever He wills distance from His pleasure and love.' Then he mentioned that tawfiq and khidhlan relate to two kinds of power: the first: a power and capacity (istita'a) with which the existence of the act is not obligatory, and it precedes the act and is before performing it. The second: a power and capacity with which the existence of the act is obligatory, and it is without doubt concurrent with the act, not preceding it. The texts of the Shari'a from the Book and authentic Sunna have indicated these two types. The indication of the first of them is in His saying: 'And due to Allah from the people is a pilgrimage to the House, for whoever is able (istata'a) to find a way to it' [Al 'Imran 97] and His saying: 'So fear Allah as much as you are able (istata'tum)' [Taghabun 16] and in His saying to 'Imran ibn Husayn: 'Pray standing; if you are unable, then on your side.' It is known that Hajj and prayer are obligatory upon the able (mustati') in the sense of one who is capable of the act and prepared for it, whether he does it or not. The indication of the second type is in His saying: 'They were not able (yastati'una) to hear and they were not seeing' [Hud 20] and His saying: 'And We will present Hell on that Day to the disbelievers as a presentation, those whose eyes were in a cover from My remembrance and they were not able (yastati'una) to hear' [Kahf 101]. The meaning of their inability (adam istita'atihim) is the difficulty of that for them and its hardship upon their souls, so their souls do not incline to it nor desire it, even though they were capable of doing it and able if they wanted it. And this is a clarification and explanation of what the group answered: that the servant is capable at the time of obligation by the proximate power (al-quwwa al-qariba), due to his being characterized by soundness of instruments and availability of means.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage defines two key terms: tawfiq (divine enabling) and khidhlan (divine abandonment). It begins by stating that belief in Allah as the Creator of the power for obedience in whomever He wills to grant success is part of the section on divine matters. The line of poetry then states that Allah is a Withholder for whomever He wills distance from Him, i.e., He creates in him the power of disobedience. The commentary explains that tawfiq and khidhlan are related to two kinds of power. The first kind is a power that does not necessitate the act; it precedes the act and is the basis for moral obligation (taklif). The second kind is a power that accompanies the act and necessarily brings it about. The author provides scriptural evidence for both: for the first, the verses on Hajj and piety show that ability means capability and preparedness, regardless of actual performance. For the second, the verses about the disbelievers' inability to hear or see show that they find it difficult and do not incline to it, though they have the physical capacity. The passage concludes by clarifying that this is the basis for the scholars' answer that the human is capable at the time of obligation by the 'proximate power' (al-quwwa al-qariba), which is due to soundness of instruments and availability of means.

Checkpoint
What is the difference between the two types of power?
A) The first is for obedience, the second for disobedience.
B) The first precedes the act and does not necessitate it; the second is concurrent and necessitates it.
C) The first is from Allah, the second from the servant.
D) The first is physical, the second is spiritual.

Key Takeaway
The two powers distinguish potential ability (preceding) from actual ability (concurrent), both created by Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How often do you use the excuse of 'I can't' (inability) when in reality you have the physical capacity but lack the inclination? Reflect on a specific obligation you have been avoiding. What does this lesson teach you about your true ability? Will you now act as one who is 'mustati' (able) by the first type of power, or will you continue to claim inability like the disbelievers described? Commit to one action you will perform today.
?
The passage distinguishes between potential ability (before the act) and actual ability (with the act). Which type of ability are you relying on for your good deeds? Are you waiting for a perfect opportunity (potential ability) or are you engaging in the act right now, trusting that Allah gives you the concurrent power? Identify one good deed you have been postponing and decide to start it now, even if imperfectly.
?
The second type of power is concurrent with the act and necessitates it. This means that when you actually perform a good deed, Allah grants you the power to do it. How does this truth affect your sense of dependence on Allah? Do you feel empowered or humbled? How can you remind yourself daily that your ability to act comes from Allah at the very moment of action?
